<v n="20">The young man said to him, "All these I have kept. What do I still lack?"</v>
<v n="21">Jesus said to him, "If you would be perfect, go, sell what you possess and give to the poor, and you will have treasure in heaven; and come, follow me."</v>
<v n="22">When the young man heard this he went away sorrowful, for he had great possessions.</v>
<v n="23">And Jesus said to his disciples, "Truly, I say to you, only with difficulty will a rich person enter the kingdom of heaven.</v>
<v n="24">Again I tell you, it is easier for a camel to go through the eye of a needle than for a rich person to enter the kingdom of God."</v>
<v n="25">When the disciples heard this, they were greatly astonished, saying, "Who then can be saved?"</v>
<v n="26">But Jesus looked at them and said, "With man this is impossible, but with God all things are possible."</v>
<v n="27">Then Peter said in reply, "See, we have left everything and followed you. What then will we have?"</v>
<v n="28">Jesus said to them, "Truly, I say to you, in the new world, when the Son of Man will sit on his glorious throne, you who have followed me will also sit on twelve thrones, judging the twelve tribes of Israel.</v>
<v n="29">And everyone who has left houses or brothers or sisters or father or mother or children or lands, for my name's sake, will receive a hundredfold and will inherit eternal life.</v>
<v n="30">But many who are first will be last, and the last first.</v>
</c>
<c n="20">
<v n="1">"For the kingdom of heaven is like a master of a house who went out early in the morning to hire laborers for his vineyard.</v>
<v n="2">After agreeing with the laborers for a denarius a day, he sent them into his vineyard.</v>
<v n="3">And going out about the third hour he saw others standing idle in the marketplace,</v>
<v n="4">and to them he said, 'You go into the vineyard too, and whatever is right I will give you.'</v>
<v n="5">So they went. Going out again about the sixth hour and the ninth hour, he did the same.</v>
<v n="6">And about the eleventh hour he went out and found others standing. And he said to them, 'Why do you stand here idle all day?'</v>
<v n="7">They said to him, 'Because no one has hired us.' He said to them, 'You go into the vineyard too.'</v>
<v n="8">And when evening came, the owner of the vineyard said to his foreman, 'Call the laborers and pay them their wages, beginning with the last, up to the first.'</v>
<v n="9">And when those hired about the eleventh hour came, each of them received a denarius.</v>
<v n="10">Now when those hired first came, they thought they would receive more, but each of them also received a denarius.</v>
<v n="11">And on receiving it they grumbled at the master of the house,</v>
<v n="12">saying, 'These last worked only one hour, and you have made them equal to us who have borne the burden of the day and the scorching heat.'</v>
<v n="13">But he replied to one of them, 'Friend, I am doing you no wrong. Did you not agree with me for a denarius?</v>
<v n="14">Take what belongs to you and go. I choose to give to this last worker as I give to you.</v>
<v n="15">Am I not allowed to do what I choose with what belongs to me? Or do you begrudge my generosity?'</v>
<v n="16">So the last will be first, and the first last."</v>
<v n="17">And as Jesus was going up to Jerusalem, he took the twelve disciples aside, and on the way he said to them,</v>
<v n="18">"See, we are going up to Jerusalem. And the Son of Man will be delivered over to the chief priests and scribes, and they will condemn him to death</v>
<v n="19">and deliver him over to the Gentiles to be mocked and flogged and crucified, and he will be raised on the third day."</v>
<v n="20">Then the mother of the sons of Zebedee came up to him with her sons, and kneeling before him she asked him for something.</v>
<v n="21">And he said to her, "What do you want?" She said to him, "Say that these two sons of mine are to sit, one at your right hand and one at your left, in your kingdom."</v>
<v n="22">Jesus answered, "You do not know what you are asking. Are you able to drink the cup that I am to drink?" They said to him, "We are able."</v>
<v n="23">He said to them, "You will drink my cup, but to sit at my right hand and at my left is not mine to grant, but it is for those for whom it has been prepared by my Father."</v>
<v n="24">And when the ten heard it, they were indignant at the two brothers.</v>
<v n="25">But Jesus called them to him and said, "You know that the rulers of the Gentiles lord it over them, and their great ones exercise authority over them.</v>
<v n="26">It shall not be so among you. But whoever would be great among you must be your servant,</v>
<v n="27">and whoever would be first among you must be your slave,</v>
<v n="28">even as the Son of Man came not to be served but to serve, and to give his life as a ransom for many."</v>
<v n="29">And as they went out of Jericho, a great crowd followed him.</v>
<v n="30">And behold, there were two blind men sitting by the roadside, and when they heard that Jesus was passing by, they cried out, "Lord, have mercy on us, Son of David!"</v>
<v n="31">The crowd rebuked them, telling them to be silent, but they cried out all the more, "Lord, have mercy on us, Son of David!"</v>
<v n="32">And stopping, Jesus called them and said, "What do you want me to do for you?"</v>
<v n="33">They said to him, "Lord, let our eyes be opened."</v>
<v n="34">And Jesus in pity touched their eyes, and immediately they recovered their sight and followed him.</v>
</c>
<c n="21">
<v n="1">Now when they drew near to Jerusalem and came to Bethphage, to the Mount of Olives, then Jesus sent two disciples,</v>
<v n="2">saying to them, "Go into the village in front of you, and immediately you will find a donkey tied, and a colt with her. Untie them and bring them to me.</v>
<v n="3">If anyone says anything to you, you shall say, 'The Lord needs them,' and he will send them at once."</v>
<v n="4">This took place to fulfill what was spoken by the prophet, saying,</v>
<v n="5">"Say to the daughter of Zion, 'Behold, your king is coming to you, humble, and mounted on a donkey, and on a colt, the foal of a beast of burden.'"</v>
<v n="6">The disciples went and did as Jesus had directed them.</v>
<v n="7">They brought the donkey and the colt and put on them their cloaks, and he sat on them.</v>
<v n="8">Most of the crowd spread their cloaks on the road, and others cut branches from the trees and spread them on the road.</v>
<v n="9">And the crowds that went before him and that followed him were shouting, "Hosanna to the Son of David! Blessed is he who comes in the name of the Lord! Hosanna in the highest!"</v>
<v n="10">And when he entered Jerusalem, the whole city was stirred up, saying, "Who is this?"</v>
<v n="11">And the crowds said, "This is the prophet Jesus, from Nazareth of Galilee."</v>
<v n="12">And Jesus entered the temple and drove out all who sold and bought in the temple, and he overturned the tables of the money-changers and the seats of those who sold pigeons.</v>
<v n="13">He said to them, "It is written, 'My house shall be called a house of prayer,' but you make it a den of robbers."</v>
<v n="14">And the blind and the lame came to him in the temple, and he healed them.</v>
<v n="15">But when the chief priests and the scribes saw the wonderful things that he did, and the children crying out in the temple, "Hosanna to the Son of David!" they were indignant,</v>
<v n="16">and they said to him, "Do you hear what these are saying?" And Jesus said to them, "Yes; have you never read, "'Out of the mouth of infants and nursing babies you have prepared praise'?"</v>
<v n="17">And leaving them, he went out of the city to Bethany and lodged there.</v>
<v n="18">In the morning, as he was returning to the city, he became hungry.</v>
<v n="19">And seeing a fig tree by the wayside, he went to it and found nothing on it but only leaves. And he said to it, "May no fruit ever come from you again!" And the fig tree withered at once.</v>
<v n="20">When the disciples saw it, they marveled, saying, "How did the fig tree wither at once?"</v>
<v n="21">And Jesus answered them, "Truly, I say to you, if you have faith and do not doubt, you will not only do what has been done to the fig tree, but even if you say to this mountain, 'Be taken up and thrown into the sea,' it will happen.</v>
<v n="22">And whatever you ask in prayer, you will receive, if you have faith."</v>
<v n="23">And when he entered the temple, the chief priests and the elders of the people came up to him as he was teaching, and said, "By what authority are you doing these things, and who gave you this authority?"</v>
<v n="24">Jesus answered them, "I also will ask you one question, and if you tell me the answer, then I also will tell you by what authority I do these things.</v>
<v n="25">The baptism of John, from where did it come? From heaven or from man?" And they discussed it among themselves, saying, "If we say, 'From heaven,' he will say to us, 'Why then did you not believe him?'</v>
<v n="26">But if we say, 'From man,' we are afraid of the crowd, for they all hold that John was a prophet."</v>
<v n="27">So they answered Jesus, "We do not know." And he said to them, "Neither will I tell you by what authority I do these things.</v>
<v n="28">"What do you think? A man had two sons. And he went to the first and said, 'Son, go and work in the vineyard today.'</v>
<v n="29">And he answered, 'I will not,' but afterward he changed his mind and went.</v>
<v n="30">And he went to the other son and said the same. And he answered, 'I go, sir,' but did not go.</v>
<v n="31">Which of the two did the will of his father?" They said, "The first." Jesus said to them, "Truly, I say to you, the tax collectors and the prostitutes go into the kingdom of God before you.</v>
<v n="32">For John came to you in the way of righteousness, and you did not believe him, but the tax collectors and the prostitutes believed him. And even when you saw it, you did not afterward change your minds and believe him.</v>
<v n="33">"Hear another parable. There was a master of a house who planted a vineyard and put a fence around it and dug a winepress in it and built a tower and leased it to tenants, and went into another country.</v>
<v n="34">When the season for fruit drew near, he sent his servants to the tenants to get his fruit.</v>
<v n="35">And the tenants took his servants and beat one, killed another, and stoned another.</v>
<v n="36">Again he sent other servants, more than the first. And they did the same to them.</v>
<v n="37">Finally he sent his son to them, saying, 'They will respect my son.'</v>
<v n="38">But when the tenants saw the son, they said to themselves, 'This is the heir. Come, let us kill him and have his inheritance.'</v>
<v n="39">And they took him and threw him out of the vineyard and killed him.</v>
<v n="40">When therefore the owner of the vineyard comes, what will he do to those tenants?"</v>
<v n="41">They said to him, "He will put those wretches to a miserable death and let out the vineyard to other tenants who will give him the fruits in their seasons."</v>
<v n="42">Jesus said to them, "Have you never read in the Scriptures: "'The stone that the builders rejected has become the cornerstone; this was the Lord's doing, and it is marvelous in our eyes'?</v>
<v n="43">Therefore I tell you, the kingdom of God will be taken away from you and given to a people producing its fruits.</v>
<v n="44">And the one who falls on this stone will be broken to pieces; and when it falls on anyone, it will crush him."</v>
<v n="45">When the chief priests and the Pharisees heard his parables, they perceived that he was speaking about them.</v>
<v n="46">And although they were seeking to arrest him, they feared the crowds, because they held him to be a prophet.</v>
</c>
<c n="22">
<v n="1">And again Jesus spoke to them in parables, saying,</v>
<v n="2">"The kingdom of heaven may be compared to a king who gave a wedding feast for his son,</v>
<v n="3">and sent his servants to call those who were invited to the wedding feast, but they would not come.</v>
<v n="4">Again he sent other servants, saying, 'Tell those who are invited, See, I have prepared my dinner, my oxen and my fat calves have been slaughtered, and everything is ready. Come to the wedding feast.'</v>
<v n="5">But they paid no attention and went off, one to his farm, another to his business,</v>
<v n="6">while the rest seized his servants, treated them shamefully, and killed them.</v>
<v n="7">The king was angry, and he sent his troops and destroyed those murderers and burned their city.</v>
<v n="8">Then he said to his servants, 'The wedding feast is ready, but those invited were not worthy.</v>
<v n="9">Go therefore to the main roads and invite to the wedding feast as many as you find.'</v>
<v n="10">And those servants went out into the roads and gathered all whom they found, both bad and good. So the wedding hall was filled with guests.</v>
<v n="11">"But when the king came in to look at the guests, he saw there a man who had no wedding garment.</v>
<v n="12">And he said to him, 'Friend, how did you get in here without a wedding garment?' And he was speechless.</v>
<v n="13">Then the king said to the attendants, 'Bind him hand and foot and cast him into the outer darkness. In that place there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth.'</v>
<v n="14">For many are called, but few are chosen."</v>
<v n="15">Then the Pharisees went and plotted how to entangle him in his talk.</v>
<v n="16">And they sent their disciples to him, along with the Herodians, saying, "Teacher, we know that you are true and teach the way of God truthfully, and you do not care about anyone's opinion, for you are not swayed by appearances.</v>
<v n="17">Tell us, then, what you think. Is it lawful to pay taxes to Caesar, or not?"</v>
<v n="18">But Jesus, aware of their malice, said, "Why put me to the test, you hypocrites?</v>
<v n="19">Show me the coin for the tax." And they brought him a denarius.</v>
<v n="20">And Jesus said to them, "Whose likeness and inscription is this?"</v>
<v n="21">They said, "Caesar's." Then he said to them, "Therefore render to Caesar the things that are Caesar's, and to God the things that are God's."</v>
<v n="22">When they heard it, they marveled. And they left him and went away.</v>
<v n="23">The same day Sadducees came to him, who say that there is no resurrection, and they asked him a question,</v>
<v n="24">saying, "Teacher, Moses said, 'If a man dies having no children, his brother must marry the widow and raise up children for his brother.'</v>
<v n="25">Now there were seven brothers among us. The first married and died, and having no children left his wife to his brother.</v>
<v n="26">So too the second and third, down to the seventh.</v>
<v n="27">After them all, the woman died.</v>
<v n="28">In the resurrection, therefore, of the seven, whose wife will she be? For they all had her."</v>
<v n="29">But Jesus answered them, "You are wrong, because you know neither the Scriptures nor the power of God.</v>
<v n="30">For in the resurrection they neither marry nor are given in marriage, but are like angels in heaven.</v>
<v n="31">And as for the resurrection of the dead, have you not read what was said to you by God:</v>
<v n="32">'I am the God of Abraham, and the God of Isaac, and the God of Jacob'? He is not God of the dead, but of the living."</v>
<v n="33">And when the crowd heard it, they were astonished at his teaching.</v>
<v n="34">But when the Pharisees heard that he had silenced the Sadducees, they gathered together.</v>
<v n="35">And one of them, a lawyer, asked him a question to test him.</v>
<v n="36">"Teacher, which is the great commandment in the Law?"</v>
<v n="37">And he said to him, "You shall love the Lord your God with all your heart and with all your soul and with all your mind.</v>
<v n="38">This is the great and first commandment.</v>
<v n="39">And a second is like it: You shall love your neighbor as yourself.</v>
<v n="40">On these two commandments depend all the Law and the Prophets."</v>
<v n="41">Now while the Pharisees were gathered together, Jesus asked them a question,</v>
<v n="42">saying, "What do you think about the Christ? Whose son is he?" They said to him, "The son of David."</v>
<v n="43">He said to them, "How is it then that David, in the Spirit, calls him Lord, saying,</v>
<v n="44">"'The Lord said to my Lord, Sit at my right hand, until I put your enemies under your feet'?</v>
<v n="45">If then David calls him Lord, how is he his son?"</v>
<v n="46">And no one was able to answer him a word, nor from that day did anyone dare to ask him any more questions.</v>
</c>
<c n="23">
<v n="1">Then Jesus said to the crowds and to his disciples,</v>
<v n="2">"The scribes and the Pharisees sit on Moses' seat,</v>
<v n="3">so practice and observe whatever they tell you--but not what they do. For they preach, but do not practice.</v>
<v n="4">They tie up heavy burdens, hard to bear, and lay them on people's shoulders, but they themselves are not willing to move them with their finger.</v>
<v n="5">They do all their deeds to be seen by others. For they make their phylacteries broad and their fringes long,</v>
<v n="6">and they love the place of honor at feasts and the best seats in the synagogues</v>
<v n="7">and greetings in the marketplaces and being called rabbi by others.</v>
<v n="8">But you are not to be called rabbi, for you have one teacher, and you are all brothers.</v>
<v n="9">And call no man your father on earth, for you have one Father, who is in heaven.</v>
<v n="10">Neither be called instructors, for you have one instructor, the Christ.</v>
<v n="11">The greatest among you shall be your servant.</v>
<v n="12">Whoever exalts himself will be humbled, and whoever humbles himself will be exalted.</v>
<v n="13">"But woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you shut the kingdom of heaven in people's faces. For you neither enter yourselves nor allow those who would enter to go in.</v>
<v n="14">See Footnote</v>
<v n="15">Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you travel across sea and land to make a single proselyte, and when he becomes a proselyte, you make him twice as much a child of hell as yourselves.</v>
<v n="16">"Woe to you, blind guides, who say, 'If anyone swears by the temple, it is nothing, but if anyone swears by the gold of the temple, he is bound by his oath.'</v>
<v n="17">You blind fools! For which is greater, the gold or the temple that has made the gold sacred?</v>
<v n="18">And you say, 'If anyone swears by the altar, it is nothing, but if anyone swears by the gift that is on the altar, he is bound by his oath.'</v>
<v n="19">You blind men! For which is greater, the gift or the altar that makes the gift sacred?</v>
<v n="20">So whoever swears by the altar swears by it and by everything on it.</v>
<v n="21">And whoever swears by the temple swears by it and by him who dwells in it.</v>
<v n="22">And whoever swears by heaven swears by the throne of God and by him who sits upon it.</v>
<v n="23">"Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you tithe mint and dill and cumin, and have neglected the weightier matters of the law: justice and mercy and faithfulness. These you ought to have done, without neglecting the others.</v>
<v n="24">You blind guides, straining out a gnat and swallowing a camel!</v>
<v n="25">"Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you clean the outside of the cup and the plate, but inside they are full of greed and self-indulgence.</v>
<v n="26">You blind Pharisee! First clean the inside of the cup and the plate, that the outside also may be clean.</v>
<v n="27">"Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you are like whitewashed tombs, which outwardly appear beautiful, but within are full of dead people's bones and all uncleanness.</v>
<v n="28">So you also outwardly appear righteous to others, but within you are full of hypocrisy and lawlessness.</v>
<v n="29">"Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! For you build the tombs of the prophets and decorate the monuments of the righteous,</v>
<v n="30">saying, 'If we had lived in the days of our fathers, we would not have taken part with them in shedding the blood of the prophets.'</v>
<v n="31">Thus you witness against yourselves that you are sons of those who murdered the prophets.</v>
<v n="32">Fill up, then, the measure of your fathers.</v>
<v n="33">You serpents, you brood of vipers, how are you to escape being sentenced to hell?</v>
<v n="34">Therefore I send you prophets and wise men and scribes, some of whom you will kill and crucify, and some you will flog in your synagogues and persecute from town to town,</v>
<v n="35">so that on you may come all the righteous blood shed on earth, from the blood of innocent Abel to the blood of Zechariah the son of Barachiah, whom you murdered between the sanctuary and the altar.</v>
<v n="36">Truly, I say to you, all these things will come upon this generation.</v>
<v n="37">"O Jerusalem, Jerusalem, the city that kills the prophets and stones those who are sent to it! How often would I have gathered your children together as a hen gathers her brood under her wings, and you would not!</v>
<v n="38">See, your house is left to you desolate.</v>
<v n="39">For I tell you, you will not see me again, until you say, 'Blessed is he who comes in the name of the Lord.'"</v>
</c>
<c n="24">
<v n="1">Jesus left the temple and was going away, when his disciples came to point out to him the buildings of the temple.</v>
<v n="2">But he answered them, "You see all these, do you not? Truly, I say to you, there will not be left here one stone upon another that will not be thrown down."</v>
<v n="3">As he sat on the Mount of Olives, the disciples came to him privately, saying, "Tell us, when will these things be, and what will be the sign of your coming and of the close of the age?"</v>
<v n="4">And Jesus answered them, "See that no one leads you astray.</v>
<v n="5">For many will come in my name, saying, 'I am the Christ,' and they will lead many astray.</v>
<v n="6">And you will hear of wars and rumors of wars. See that you are not alarmed, for this must take place, but the end is not yet.</v>
<v n="7">For nation will rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom, and there will be famines and earthquakes in various places.</v>
<v n="8">All these are but the beginning of the birth pains.</v>
<v n="9">"Then they will deliver you up to tribulation and put you to death, and you will be hated by all nations for my name's sake.</v>
<v n="10">And then many will fall away and betray one another and hate one another.</v>
<v n="11">And many false prophets will arise and lead many astray.</v>
<v n="12">And because lawlessness will be increased, the love of many will grow cold.</v>
<v n="13">But the one who endures to the end will be saved.</v>
<v n="14">And this gospel of the kingdom will be proclaimed throughout the whole world as a testimony to all nations, and then the end will come.</v>
<v n="15">"So when you see the abomination of desolation spoken of by the prophet Daniel, standing in the holy place (let the reader understand),</v>
<v n="16">then let those who are in Judea flee to the mountains.</v>
<v n="17">Let the one who is on the housetop not go down to take what is in his house,</v>
<v n="18">and let the one who is in the field not turn back to take his cloak.</v>
<v n="19">And alas for women who are pregnant and for those who are nursing infants in those days!</v>
<v n="20">Pray that your flight may not be in winter or on a Sabbath.</v>
<v n="21">For then there will be great tribulation, such as has not been from the beginning of the world until now, no, and never will be.</v>
<v n="22">And if those days had not been cut short, no human being would be saved. But for the sake of the elect those days will be cut short.</v>
<v n="23">Then if anyone says to you, 'Look, here is the Christ!' or 'There he is!' do not believe it.</v>
<v n="24">For false christs and false prophets will arise and perform great signs and wonders, so as to lead astray, if possible, even the elect.</v>
<v n="25">See, I have told you beforehand.</v>
<v n="26">So, if they say to you, 'Look, he is in the wilderness,' do not go out. If they say, 'Look, he is in the inner rooms,' do not believe it.</v>
<v n="27">For as the lightning comes from the east and shines as far as the west, so will be the coming of the Son of Man.</v>
<v n="28">Wherever the corpse is, there the vultures will gather.</v>
<v n="29">"Immediately after the tribulation of those days the sun will be darkened, and the moon will not give its light, and the stars will fall from heaven, and the powers of the heavens will be shaken.</v>
<v n="30">Then will appear in heaven the sign of the Son of Man, and then all the tribes of the earth will mourn, and they will see the Son of Man coming on the clouds of heaven with power and great glory.</v>
<v n="31">And he will send out his angels with a loud trumpet call, and they will gather his elect from the four winds, from one end of heaven to the other.</v>
<v n="32">"From the fig tree learn its lesson: as soon as its branch becomes tender and puts out its leaves, you know that summer is near.</v>
<v n="33">So also, when you see all these things, you know that he is near, at the very gates.</v>
<v n="34">Truly, I say to you, this generation will not pass away until all these things take place.</v>
<v n="35">Heaven and earth will pass away, but my words will not pass away.</v>
<v n="36">"But concerning that day and hour no one knows, not even the angels of heaven, nor the Son, but the Father only.</v>
<v n="37">As were the days of Noah, so will be the coming of the Son of Man.</v>
<v n="38">For as in those days before the flood they were eating and drinking, marrying and giving in marriage, until the day when Noah entered the ark,</v>
<v n="39">and they were unaware until the flood came and swept them all away, so will be the coming of the Son of Man.</v>
<v n="40">Then two men will be in the field; one will be taken and one left.</v>
<v n="41">Two women will be grinding at the mill; one will be taken and one left.</v>
<v n="42">Therefore, stay awake, for you do not know on what day your Lord is coming.</v>
<v n="43">But know this, that if the master of the house had known in what part of the night the thief was coming, he would have stayed awake and would not have let his house be broken into.</v>
<v n="44">Therefore you also must be ready, for the Son of Man is coming at an hour you do not expect.</v>
<v n="45">"Who then is the faithful and wise servant, whom his master has set over his household, to give them their food at the proper time?</v>
<v n="46">Blessed is that servant whom his master will find so doing when he comes.</v>
<v n="47">Truly, I say to you, he will set him over all his possessions.</v>
<v n="48">But if that wicked servant says to himself, 'My master is delayed,'</v>
<v n="49">and begins to beat his fellow servants and eats and drinks with drunkards,</v>
<v n="50">the master of that servant will come on a day when he does not expect him and at an hour he does not know</v>
<v n="51">and will cut him in pieces and put him with the hypocrites. In that place there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth.</v>
</c>
<c n="25">
<v n="1">"Then the kingdom of heaven will be like ten virgins who took their lamps and went to meet the bridegroom.</v>
<v n="2">Five of them were foolish, and five were wise.</v>
<v n="3">For when the foolish took their lamps, they took no oil with them,</v>
<v n="4">but the wise took flasks of oil with their lamps.</v>
<v n="5">As the bridegroom was delayed, they all became drowsy and slept.</v>
<v n="6">But at midnight there was a cry, 'Here is the bridegroom! Come out to meet him.'</v>
<v n="7">Then all those virgins rose and trimmed their lamps.</v>
<v n="8">And the foolish said to the wise, 'Give us some of your oil, for our lamps are going out.'</v>
<v n="9">But the wise answered, saying, 'Since there will not be enough for us and for you, go rather to the dealers and buy for yourselves.'</v>
<v n="10">And while they were going to buy, the bridegroom came, and those who were ready went in with him to the marriage feast, and the door was shut.</v>
<v n="11">Afterward the other virgins came also, saying, 'Lord, lord, open to us.'</v>
<v n="12">But he answered, 'Truly, I say to you, I do not know you.'</v>
<v n="13">Watch therefore, for you know neither the day nor the hour.</v>
<v n="14">"For it will be like a man going on a journey, who called his servants and entrusted to them his property.</v>
<v n="15">To one he gave five talents, to another two, to another one, to each according to his ability. Then he went away.</v>
<v n="16">He who had received the five talents went at once and traded with them, and he made five talents more.</v>
<v n="17">So also he who had the two talents made two talents more.</v>
<v n="18">But he who had received the one talent went and dug in the ground and hid his master's money.</v>
<v n="19">Now after a long time the master of those servants came and settled accounts with them.</v>
<v n="20">And he who had received the five talents came forward, bringing five talents more, saying, 'Master, you delivered to me five talents; here I have made five talents more.'</v>
<v n="21">His master said to him, 'Well done, good and faithful servant. You have been faithful over a little; I will set you over much. Enter into the joy of your master.'</v>
<v n="22">And he also who had the two talents came forward, saying, 'Master, you delivered to me two talents; here I have made two talents more.'</v>
<v n="23">His master said to him, 'Well done, good and faithful servant. You have been faithful over a little; I will set you over much. Enter into the joy of your master.'</v>
<v n="24">He also who had received the one talent came forward, saying, 'Master, I knew you to be a hard man, reaping where you did not sow, and gathering where you scattered no seed,</v>
<v n="25">so I was afraid, and I went and hid your talent in the ground. Here you have what is yours.'</v>
<v n="26">But his master answered him, 'You wicked and slothful servant! You knew that I reap where I have not sowed and gather where I scattered no seed?</v>
<v n="27">Then you ought to have invested my money with the bankers, and at my coming I should have received what was my own with interest.</v>
<v n="28">So take the talent from him and give it to him who has the ten talents.</v>
<v n="29">For to everyone who has will more be given, and he will have an abundance. But from the one who has not, even what he has will be taken away.</v>
<v n="30">And cast the worthless servant into the outer darkness. In that place there will be weeping and gnashing of teeth.'</v>
<v n="31">"When the Son of Man comes in his glory, and all the angels with him, then he will sit on his glorious throne.</v>
<v n="32">Before him will be gathered all the nations, and he will separate people one from another as a shepherd separates the sheep from the goats.</v>
<v n="33">And he will place the sheep on his right, but the goats on the left.</v>
<v n="34">Then the King will say to those on his right, 'Come, you who are blessed by my Father, inherit the kingdom prepared for you from the foundation of the world.</v>
<v n="35">For I was hungry and you gave me food, I was thirsty and you gave me drink, I was a stranger and you welcomed me,</v>
<v n="36">I was naked and you clothed me, I was sick and you visited me, I was in prison and you came to me.'</v>
<v n="37">Then the righteous will answer him, saying, 'Lord, when did we see you hungry and feed you, or thirsty and give you drink?</v>
<v n="38">And when did we see you a stranger and welcome you, or naked and clothe you?</v>
<v n="39">And when did we see you sick or in prison and visit you?'</v>
<v n="40">And the King will answer them, 'Truly, I say to you, as you did it to one of the least of these my brothers, you did it to me.'</v>
<v n="41">"Then he will say to those on his left, 'Depart from me, you cursed, into the eternal fire prepared for the devil and his angels.</v>
<v n="42">For I was hungry and you gave me no food, I was thirsty and you gave me no drink,</v>
<v n="43">I was a stranger and you did not welcome me, naked and you did not clothe me, sick and in prison and you did not visit me.'</v>
<v n="44">Then they also will answer, saying, 'Lord, when did we see you hungry or thirsty or a stranger or naked or sick or in prison, and did not minister to you?'</v>
<v n="45">Then he will answer them, saying, 'Truly, I say to you, as you did not do it to one of the least of these, you did not do it to me.'</v>
<v n="46">And these will go away into eternal punishment, but the righteous into eternal life."</v>
</c>
<c n="26">
<v n="1">When Jesus had finished all these sayings, he said to his disciples,</v>
<v n="2">"You know that after two days the Passover is coming, and the Son of Man will be delivered up to be crucified."</v>
<v n="3">Then the chief priests and the elders of the people gathered in the palace of the high priest, whose name was Caiaphas,</v>
<v n="4">and plotted together in order to arrest Jesus by stealth and kill him.</v>
<v n="5">But they said, "Not during the feast, lest there be an uproar among the people."</v>
<v n="6">Now when Jesus was at Bethany in the house of Simon the leper,</v>
<v n="7">a woman came up to him with an alabaster flask of very expensive ointment, and she poured it on his head as he reclined at table.</v>
<v n="8">And when the disciples saw it, they were indignant, saying, "Why this waste?</v>
<v n="9">For this could have been sold for a large sum and given to the poor."</v>
<v n="10">But Jesus, aware of this, said to them, "Why do you trouble the woman? For she has done a beautiful thing to me.</v>
<v n="11">For you always have the poor with you, but you will not always have me.</v>
<v n="12">In pouring this ointment on my body, she has done it to prepare me for burial.</v>
<v n="13">Truly, I say to you, wherever this gospel is proclaimed in the whole world, what she has done will also be told in memory of her."</v>
<v n="14">Then one of the twelve, whose name was Judas Iscariot, went to the chief priests</v>
<v n="15">and said, "What will you give me if I deliver him over to you?" And they paid him thirty pieces of silver.</v>
<v n="16">And from that moment he sought an opportunity to betray him.</v>
<v n="17">Now on the first day of Unleavened Bread the disciples came to Jesus, saying, "Where will you have us prepare for you to eat the Passover?"</v>
<v n="18">He said, "Go into the city to a certain man and say to him, 'The Teacher says, My time is at hand. I will keep the Passover at your house with my disciples.'"</v>
<v n="19">And the disciples did as Jesus had directed them, and they prepared the Passover.</v>
<v n="20">When it was evening, he reclined at table with the twelve.</v>
<v n="21">And as they were eating, he said, "Truly, I say to you, one of you will betray me."</v>
<v n="22">And they were very sorrowful and began to say to him one after another, "Is it I, Lord?"</v>
<v n="23">He answered, "He who has dipped his hand in the dish with me will betray me.</v>
<v n="24">The Son of Man goes as it is written of him, but woe to that man by whom the Son of Man is betrayed! It would have been better for that man if he had not been born."</v>
<v n="25">Judas, who would betray him, answered, "Is it I, Rabbi?" He said to him, "You have said so."</v>
<v n="26">Now as they were eating, Jesus took bread, and after blessing it broke it and gave it to the disciples, and said, "Take, eat; this is my body."</v>
<v n="27">And he took a cup, and when he had given thanks he gave it to them, saying, "Drink of it, all of you,</v>
<v n="28">for this is my blood of the covenant, which is poured out for many for the forgiveness of sins.</v>
<v n="29">I tell you I will not drink again of this fruit of the vine until that day when I drink it new with you in my Father's kingdom."</v>
<v n="30">And when they had sung a hymn, they went out to the Mount of Olives.</v>
<v n="31">Then Jesus said to them, "You will all fall away because of me this night. For it is written, 'I will strike the shepherd, and the sheep of the flock will be scattered.'</v>
<v n="32">But after I am raised up, I will go before you to Galilee."</v>
<v n="33">Peter answered him, "Though they all fall away because of you, I will never fall away."</v>
<v n="34">Jesus said to him, "Truly, I tell you, this very night, before the rooster crows, you will deny me three times."</v>
<v n="35">Peter said to him, "Even if I must die with you, I will not deny you!" And all the disciples said the same.</v>
<v n="36">Then Jesus went with them to a place called Gethsemane, and he said to his disciples, "Sit here, while I go over there and pray."</v>
<v n="37">And taking with him Peter and the two sons of Zebedee, he began to be sorrowful and troubled.</v>
<v n="38">Then he said to them, "My soul is very sorrowful, even to death; remain here, and watch with me."</v>
<v n="39">And going a little farther he fell on his face and prayed, saying, "My Father, if it be possible, let this cup pass from me; nevertheless, not as I will, but as you will."</v>
<v n="40">And he came to the disciples and found them sleeping. And he said to Peter, "So, could you not watch with me one hour?</v>
<v n="41">Watch and pray that you may not enter into temptation. The spirit indeed is willing, but the flesh is weak."</v>
<v n="42">Again, for the second time, he went away and prayed, "My Father, if this cannot pass unless I drink it, your will be done."</v>
<v n="43">And again he came and found them sleeping, for their eyes were heavy.</v>
<v n="44">So, leaving them again, he went away and prayed for the third time, saying the same words again.</v>
<v n="45">Then he came to the disciples and said to them, "Sleep and take your rest later on. See, the hour is at hand, and the Son of Man is betrayed into the hands of sinners.</v>
<v n="46">Rise, let us be going; see, my betrayer is at hand."</v>
<v n="47">While he was still speaking, Judas came, one of the twelve, and with him a great crowd with swords and clubs, from the chief priests and the elders of the people.</v>
<v n="48">Now the betrayer had given them a sign, saying, "The one I will kiss is the man; seize him."</v>
<v n="49">And he came up to Jesus at once and said, "Greetings, Rabbi!" And he kissed him.</v>
<v n="50">Jesus said to him, "Friend, do what you came to do." Then they came up and laid hands on Jesus and seized him.</v>
<v n="51">And behold, one of those who were with Jesus stretched out his hand and drew his sword and struck the servant of the high priest and cut off his ear.</v>
<v n="52">Then Jesus said to him, "Put your sword back into its place. For all who take the sword will perish by the sword.</v>
<v n="53">Do you think that I cannot appeal to my Father, and he will at once send me more than twelve legions of angels?</v>
<v n="54">But how then should the Scriptures be fulfilled, that it must be so?"</v>
<v n="55">At that hour Jesus said to the crowds, "Have you come out as against a robber, with swords and clubs to capture me? Day after day I sat in the temple teaching, and you did not seize me.</v>
<v n="56">But all this has taken place that the Scriptures of the prophets might be fulfilled." Then all the disciples left him and fled.</v>
<v n="57">Then those who had seized Jesus led him to Caiaphas the high priest, where the scribes and the elders had gathered.</v>
<v n="58">And Peter was following him at a distance, as far as the courtyard of the high priest, and going inside he sat with the guards to see the end.</v>
<v n="59">Now the chief priests and the whole Council were seeking false testimony against Jesus that they might put him to death,</v>
<v n="60">but they found none, though many false witnesses came forward. At last two came forward</v>
<v n="61">and said, "This man said, 'I am able to destroy the temple of God, and to rebuild it in three days.'"</v>
<v n="62">And the high priest stood up and said, "Have you no answer to make? What is it that these men testify against you?"</v>
<v n="63">But Jesus remained silent. And the high priest said to him, "I adjure you by the living God, tell us if you are the Christ, the Son of God."</v>
<v n="64">Jesus said to him, "You have said so. But I tell you, from now on you will see the Son of Man seated at the right hand of Power and coming on the clouds of heaven."</v>
<v n="65">Then the high priest tore his robes and said, "He has uttered blasphemy. What further witnesses do we need? You have now heard his blasphemy.</v>
<v n="66">What is your judgment?" They answered, "He deserves death."</v>
<v n="67">Then they spit in his face and struck him. And some slapped him,</v>
<v n="68">saying, "Prophesy to us, you Christ! Who is it that struck you?"</v>
<v n="69">Now Peter was sitting outside in the courtyard. And a servant girl came up to him and said, "You also were with Jesus the Galilean."</v>
<v n="70">But he denied it before them all, saying, "I do not know what you mean."</v>
<v n="71">And when he went out to the entrance, another servant girl saw him, and she said to the bystanders, "This man was with Jesus of Nazareth."</v>
<v n="72">And again he denied it with an oath: "I do not know the man."</v>
<v n="73">After a little while the bystanders came up and said to Peter, "Certainly you too are one of them, for your accent betrays you."</v>
<v n="74">Then he began to invoke a curse on himself and to swear, "I do not know the man." And immediately the rooster crowed.</v>
<v n="75">And Peter remembered the saying of Jesus, "Before the rooster crows, you will deny me three times." And he went out and wept bitterly.</v>
</c>
<c n="27">
<v n="1">When morning came, all the chief priests and the elders of the people took counsel against Jesus to put him to death.</v>
<v n="2">And they bound him and led him away and delivered him over to Pilate the governor.</v>
<v n="3">Then when Judas, his betrayer, saw that Jesus was condemned, he changed his mind and brought back the thirty pieces of silver to the chief priests and the elders,</v>
<v n="4">saying, "I have sinned by betraying innocent blood." They said, "What is that to us? See to it yourself."</v>
<v n="5">And throwing down the pieces of silver into the temple, he departed, and he went and hanged himself.</v>
<v n="6">But the chief priests, taking the pieces of silver, said, "It is not lawful to put them into the treasury, since it is blood money."</v>
<v n="7">So they took counsel and bought with them the potter's field as a burial place for strangers.</v>
<v n="8">Therefore that field has been called the Field of Blood to this day.</v>
<v n="9">Then was fulfilled what had been spoken by the prophet Jeremiah, saying, "And they took the thirty pieces of silver, the price of him on whom a price had been set by some of the sons of Israel,</v>
<v n="10">and they gave them for the potter's field, as the Lord directed me."</v>
<v n="11">Now Jesus stood before the governor, and the governor asked him, "Are you the King of the Jews?" Jesus said, "You have said so."</v>
<v n="12">But when he was accused by the chief priests and elders, he gave no answer.</v>
<v n="13">Then Pilate said to him, "Do you not hear how many things they testify against you?"</v>
<v n="14">But he gave him no answer, not even to a single charge, so that the governor was greatly amazed.</v>
<v n="15">Now at the feast the governor was accustomed to release for the crowd any one prisoner whom they wanted.</v>
<v n="16">And they had then a notorious prisoner called Barabbas.</v>
<v n="17">So when they had gathered, Pilate said to them, "Whom do you want me to release for you: Barabbas, or Jesus who is called Christ?"</v>
<v n="18">For he knew that it was out of envy that they had delivered him up.</v>
<v n="19">Besides, while he was sitting on the judgment seat, his wife sent word to him, "Have nothing to do with that righteous man, for I have suffered much because of him today in a dream."</v>
<v n="20">Now the chief priests and the elders persuaded the crowd to ask for Barabbas and destroy Jesus.</v>
<v n="21">The governor again said to them, "Which of the two do you want me to release for you?" And they said, "Barabbas."</v>
<v n="22">Pilate said to them, "Then what shall I do with Jesus who is called Christ?" They all said, "Let him be crucified!"</v>
<v n="23">And he said, "Why, what evil has he done?" But they shouted all the more, "Let him be crucified!"</v>
<v n="24">So when Pilate saw that he was gaining nothing, but rather that a riot was beginning, he took water and washed his hands before the crowd, saying, "I am innocent of this man's blood; see to it yourselves."</v>
<v n="25">And all the people answered, "His blood be on us and on our children!"</v>
<v n="26">Then he released for them Barabbas, and having scourged Jesus, delivered him to be crucified.</v>
<v n="27">Then the soldiers of the governor took Jesus into the governor's headquarters, and they gathered the whole battalion before him.</v>
<v n="28">And they stripped him and put a scarlet robe on him,</v>
<v n="29">and twisting together a crown of thorns, they put it on his head and put a reed in his right hand. And kneeling before him, they mocked him, saying, "Hail, King of the Jews!"</v>
<v n="30">And they spit on him and took the reed and struck him on the head.</v>
<v n="31">And when they had mocked him, they stripped him of the robe and put his own clothes on him and led him away to crucify him.</v>
<v n="32">As they went out, they found a man of Cyrene, Simon by name. They compelled this man to carry his cross.</v>
<v n="33">And when they came to a place called Golgotha (which means Place of a Skull),</v>
<v n="34">they offered him wine to drink, mixed with gall, but when he tasted it, he would not drink it.</v>
<v n="35">And when they had crucified him, they divided his garments among them by casting lots.</v>
<v n="36">Then they sat down and kept watch over him there.</v>
<v n="37">And over his head they put the charge against him, which read, "This is Jesus, the King of the Jews."</v>
<v n="38">Then two robbers were crucified with him, one on the right and one on the left.</v>
<v n="39">And those who passed by derided him, wagging their heads</v>
<v n="40">and saying, "You who would destroy the temple and rebuild it in three days, save yourself! If you are the Son of God, come down from the cross."</v>
<v n="41">So also the chief priests, with the scribes and elders, mocked him, saying,</v>
<v n="42">"He saved others; he cannot save himself. He is the King of Israel; let him come down now from the cross, and we will believe in him.</v>
<v n="43">He trusts in God; let God deliver him now, if he desires him. For he said, 'I am the Son of God.'"</v>
<v n="44">And the robbers who were crucified with him also reviled him in the same way.</v>
<v n="45">Now from the sixth hour there was darkness over all the land until the ninth hour.</v>
<v n="46">And about the ninth hour Jesus cried out with a loud voice, saying, "Eli, Eli, lema sabachthani?" that is, "My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?"</v>
<v n="47">And some of the bystanders, hearing it, said, "This man is calling Elijah."</v>
<v n="48">And one of them at once ran and took a sponge, filled it with sour wine, and put it on a reed and gave it to him to drink.</v>
<v n="49">But the others said, "Wait, let us see whether Elijah will come to save him."</v>
<v n="50">And Jesus cried out again with a loud voice and yielded up his spirit.</v>
<v n="51">And behold, the curtain of the temple was torn in two, from top to bottom. And the earth shook, and the rocks were split.</v>
<v n="52">The tombs also were opened. And many bodies of the saints who had fallen asleep were raised,</v>
<v n="53">and coming out of the tombs after his resurrection they went into the holy city and appeared to many.</v>
<v n="54">When the centurion and those who were with him, keeping watch over Jesus, saw the earthquake and what took place, they were filled with awe and said, "Truly this was the Son of God!"</v>
<v n="55">There were also many women there, looking on from a distance, who had followed Jesus from Galilee, ministering to him,</v>
<v n="56">among whom were Mary Magdalene and Mary the mother of James and Joseph and the mother of the sons of Zebedee.</v>
<v n="57">When it was evening, there came a rich man from Arimathea, named Joseph, who also was a disciple of Jesus.</v>
<v n="58">He went to Pilate and asked for the body of Jesus. Then Pilate ordered it to be given to him.</v>
<v n="59">And Joseph took the body and wrapped it in a clean linen shroud</v>
<v n="60">and laid it in his own new tomb, which he had cut in the rock. And he rolled a great stone to the entrance of the tomb and went away.</v>
<v n="61">Mary Magdalene and the other Mary were there, sitting opposite the tomb.</v>
<v n="62">Next day, that is, after the day of Preparation, the chief priests and the Pharisees gathered before Pilate</v>
<v n="63">and said, "Sir, we remember how that impostor said, while he was still alive, 'After three days I will rise.'</v>
<v n="64">Therefore order the tomb to be made secure until the third day, lest his disciples go and steal him away and tell the people, 'He has risen from the dead,' and the last fraud will be worse than the first."</v>
<v n="65">Pilate said to them, "You have a guard of soldiers. Go, make it as secure as you can."</v>
<v n="66">So they went and made the tomb secure by sealing the stone and setting a guard.</v>
</c>
<c n="28">
<v n="1">Now after the Sabbath, toward the dawn of the first day of the week, Mary Magdalene and the other Mary went to see the tomb.</v>
<v n="2">And behold, there was a great earthquake, for an angel of the Lord descended from heaven and came and rolled back the stone and sat on it.</v>
<v n="3">His appearance was like lightning, and his clothing white as snow.</v>
<v n="4">And for fear of him the guards trembled and became like dead men.</v>
<v n="5">But the angel said to the women, "Do not be afraid, for I know that you seek Jesus who was crucified.</v>
<v n="6">He is not here, for he has risen, as he said. Come, see the place where he lay.</v>
<v n="7">Then go quickly and tell his disciples that he has risen from the dead, and behold, he is going before you to Galilee; there you will see him. See, I have told you."</v>
<v n="8">So they departed quickly from the tomb with fear and great joy, and ran to tell his disciples.</v>
<v n="9">And behold, Jesus met them and said, "Greetings!" And they came up and took hold of his feet and worshiped him.</v>
<v n="10">Then Jesus said to them, "Do not be afraid; go and tell my brothers to go to Galilee, and there they will see me."</v>
<v n="11">While they were going, behold, some of the guard went into the city and told the chief priests all that had taken place.</v>
<v n="12">And when they had assembled with the elders and taken counsel, they gave a sufficient sum of money to the soldiers</v>
<v n="13">and said, "Tell people, 'His disciples came by night and stole him away while we were asleep.'</v>
<v n="14">And if this comes to the governor's ears, we will satisfy him and keep you out of trouble."</v>
<v n="15">So they took the money and did as they were directed. And this story has been spread among the Jews to this day.</v>
<v n="16">Now the eleven disciples went to Galilee, to the mountain to which Jesus had directed them.</v>
<v n="17">And when they saw him they worshiped him, but some doubted.</v>
<v n="18">And Jesus came and said to them, "All authority in heaven and on earth has been given to me.</v>
<v n="19">Go therefore and make disciples of all nations, baptizing them in the name of the Father and of the Son and of the Holy Spirit,</v>
<v n="20">teaching them to observe all that I have commanded you. And behold, I am with you always, to the end of the age."</v>
</c>
</b>
<b n="Mark">
<c n="1">
<v n="1">The beginning of the gospel of Jesus Christ, the Son of God.</v>
<v n="2">As it is written in Isaiah the prophet, "Behold, I send my messenger before your face, who will prepare your way,</v>
<v n="3">the voice of one crying in the wilderness: 'Prepare the way of the Lord, make his paths straight,'"</v>
<v n="4">John appeared, baptizing in the wilderness and proclaiming a baptism of repentance for the forgiveness of sins.</v>
<v n="5">And all the country of Judea and all Jerusalem were going out to him and were being baptized by him in the river Jordan, confessing their sins.</v>
<v n="6">Now John was clothed with camel's hair and wore a leather belt around his waist and ate locusts and wild honey.</v>
<v n="7">And he preached, saying, "After me comes he who is mightier than I, the strap of whose sandals I am not worthy to stoop down and untie.</v>
<v n="8">I have baptized you with water, but he will baptize you with the Holy Spirit."</v>
<v n="9">In those days Jesus came from Nazareth of Galilee and was baptized by John in the Jordan.</v>
<v n="10">And when he came up out of the water, immediately he saw the heavens opening and the Spirit descending on him like a dove.</v>
<v n="11">And a voice came from heaven, "You are my beloved Son; with you I am well pleased."</v>
<v n="12">The Spirit immediately drove him out into the wilderness.</v>
<v n="13">And he was in the wilderness forty days, being tempted by Satan. And he was with the wild animals, and the angels were ministering to him.</v>
<v n="14">Now after John was arrested, Jesus came into Galilee, proclaiming the gospel of God,</v>
<v n="15">and saying, "The time is fulfilled, and the kingdom of God is at hand; repent and believe in the gospel."</v>
<v n="16">Passing alongside the Sea of Galilee, he saw Simon and Andrew the brother of Simon casting a net into the sea, for they were fishermen.</v>
<v n="17">And Jesus said to them, "Follow me, and I will make you become fishers of men."</v>
<v n="18">And immediately they left their nets and followed him.</v>
<v n="19">And going on a little farther, he saw James the son of Zebedee and John his brother, who were in their boat mending the nets.</v>
<v n="20">And immediately he called them, and they left their father Zebedee in the boat with the hired servants and followed him.</v>
<v n="21">And they went into Capernaum, and immediately on the Sabbath he entered the synagogue and was teaching.</v>
<v n="22">And they were astonished at his teaching, for he taught them as one who had authority, and not as the scribes.</v>
<v n="23">And immediately there was in their synagogue a man with an unclean spirit. And he cried out,</v>
<v n="24">"What have you to do with us, Jesus of Nazareth? Have you come to destroy us? I know who you are--the Holy One of God."</v>
<v n="25">But Jesus rebuked him, saying, "Be silent, and come out of him!"</v>
<v n="26">And the unclean spirit, convulsing him and crying out with a loud voice, came out of him.</v>
<v n="27">And they were all amazed, so that they questioned among themselves, saying, "What is this? A new teaching with authority! He commands even the unclean spirits, and they obey him."</v>
<v n="28">And at once his fame spread everywhere throughout all the surrounding region of Galilee.</v>
<v n="29">And immediately he left the synagogue and entered the house of Simon and Andrew, with James and John.</v>
<v n="30">Now Simon's mother-in-law lay ill with a fever, and immediately they told him about her.</v>
<v n="31">And he came and took her by the hand and lifted her up, and the fever left her, and she began to serve them.</v>
<v n="32">That evening at sundown they brought to him all who were sick or oppressed by demons.</v>
<v n="33">And the whole city was gathered together at the door.</v>
<v n="34">And he healed many who were sick with various diseases, and cast out many demons. And he would not permit the demons to speak, because they knew him.</v>
<v n="35">And rising very early in the morning, while it was still dark, he departed and went out to a desolate place, and there he prayed.</v>
<v n="36">And Simon and those who were with him searched for him,</v>
<v n="37">and they found him and said to him, "Everyone is looking for you."</v>
<v n="38">And he said to them, "Let us go on to the next towns, that I may preach there also, for that is why I came out."</v>
<v n="39">And he went throughout all Galilee, preaching in their synagogues and casting out demons.</v>
<v n="40">And a leper came to him, imploring him, and kneeling said to him, "If you will, you can make me clean."</v>
<v n="41">Moved with pity, he stretched out his hand and touched him and said to him, "I will; be clean."</v>
<v n="42">And immediately the leprosy left him, and he was made clean.</v>
<v n="43">And Jesus sternly charged him and sent him away at once,</v>
<v n="44">and said to him, "See that you say nothing to anyone, but go, show yourself to the priest and offer for your cleansing what Moses commanded, for a proof to them."</v>
<v n="45">But he went out and began to talk freely about it, and to spread the news, so that Jesus could no longer openly enter a town, but was out in desolate places, and people were coming to him from every quarter.</v>
</c>
<c n="2">
<v n="1">And when he returned to Capernaum after some days, it was reported that he was at home.</v>
<v n="2">And many were gathered together, so that there was no more room, not even at the door. And he was preaching the word to them.</v>
<v n="3">And they came, bringing to him a paralytic carried by four men.</v>
<v n="4">And when they could not get near him because of the crowd, they removed the roof above him, and when they had made an opening, they let down the bed on which the paralytic lay.</v>
<v n="5">And when Jesus saw their faith, he said to the paralytic, "My son, your sins are forgiven."</v>
<v n="6">Now some of the scribes were sitting there, questioning in their hearts,</v>
<v n="7">"Why does this man speak like that? He is blaspheming! Who can forgive sins but God alone?"</v>
<v n="8">And immediately Jesus, perceiving in his spirit that they thus questioned within themselves, said to them, "Why do you question these things in your hearts?</v>
<v n="9">Which is easier, to say to the paralytic, 'Your sins are forgiven,' or to say, 'Rise, take up your bed and walk'?</v>
<v n="10">But that you may know that the Son of Man has authority on earth to forgive sins"--he said to the paralytic--</v>
<v n="11">"I say to you, rise, pick up your bed, and go home."</v>
<v n="12">And he rose and immediately picked up his bed and went out before them all, so that they were all amazed and glorified God, saying, "We never saw anything like this!"</v>
<v n="13">He went out again beside the sea, and all the crowd was coming to him, and he was teaching them.</v>
<v n="14">And as he passed by, he saw Levi the son of Alphaeus sitting at the tax booth, and he said to him, "Follow me." And he rose and followed him.</v>
<v n="15">And as he reclined at table in his house, many tax collectors and sinners were reclining with Jesus and his disciples, for there were many who followed him.</v>
<v n="16">And the scribes of the Pharisees, when they saw that he was eating with sinners and tax collectors, said to his disciples, "Why does he eat with tax collectors and sinners?"</v>
<v n="17">And when Jesus heard it, he said to them, "Those who are well have no need of a physician, but those who are sick. I came not to call the righteous, but sinners."</v>
<v n="18">Now John's disciples and the Pharisees were fasting. And people came and said to him, "Why do John's disciples and the disciples of the Pharisees fast, but your disciples do not fast?"</v>
<v n="19">And Jesus said to them, "Can the wedding guests fast while the bridegroom is with them? As long as they have the bridegroom with them, they cannot fast.</v>
<v n="20">The days will come when the bridegroom is taken away from them, and then they will fast in that day.</v>
<v n="21">No one sews a piece of unshrunk cloth on an old garment. If he does, the patch tears away from it, the new from the old, and a worse tear is made.</v>
<v n="22">And no one puts new wine into old wineskins. If he does, the wine will burst the skins--and the wine is destroyed, and so are the skins. But new wine is for fresh wineskins."</v>
<v n="23">One Sabbath he was going through the grainfields, and as they made their way, his disciples began to pluck heads of grain.</v>
<v n="24">And the Pharisees were saying to him, "Look, why are they doing what is not lawful on the Sabbath?"</v>
<v n="25">And he said to them, "Have you never read what David did, when he was in need and was hungry, he and those who were with him:</v>
<v n="26">how he entered the house of God, in the time of Abiathar the high priest, and ate the bread of the Presence, which it is not lawful for any but the priests to eat, and also gave it to those who were with him?"</v>
<v n="27">And he said to them, "The Sabbath was made for man, not man for the Sabbath.</v>
<v n="28">So the Son of Man is lord even of the Sabbath."</v>
</c>
<c n="3">
<v n="1">Again he entered the synagogue, and a man was there with a withered hand.</v>
<v n="2">And they watched Jesus, to see whether he would heal him on the Sabbath, so that they might accuse him.</v>
<v n="3">And he said to the man with the withered hand, "Come here."</v>
<v n="4">And he said to them, "Is it lawful on the Sabbath to do good or to do harm, to save life or to kill?" But they were silent.</v>
<v n="5">And he looked around at them with anger, grieved at their hardness of heart, and said to the man, "Stretch out your hand." He stretched it out, and his hand was restored.</v>
<v n="6">The Pharisees went out and immediately held counsel with the Herodians against him, how to destroy him.</v>
<v n="7">Jesus withdrew with his disciples to the sea, and a great crowd followed, from Galilee and Judea</v>
<v n="8">and Jerusalem and Idumea and from beyond the Jordan and from around Tyre and Sidon. When the great crowd heard all that he was doing, they came to him.</v>
<v n="9">And he told his disciples to have a boat ready for him because of the crowd, lest they crush him,</v>
<v n="10">for he had healed many, so that all who had diseases pressed around him to touch him.</v>
<v n="11">And whenever the unclean spirits saw him, they fell down before him and cried out, "You are the Son of God."</v>
<v n="12">And he strictly ordered them not to make him known.</v>
<v n="13">And he went up on the mountain and called to him those whom he desired, and they came to him.</v>
<v n="14">And he appointed twelve (whom he also named apostles) so that they might be with him and he might send them out to preach</v>
<v n="15">and have authority to cast out demons.</v>
<v n="16">He appointed the twelve: Simon (to whom he gave the name Peter);</v>
<v n="17">James the son of Zebedee and John the brother of James (to whom he gave the name Boanerges, that is, Sons of Thunder);</v>
<v n="18">Andrew, and Philip, and Bartholomew, and Matthew, and Thomas, and James the son of Alphaeus, and Thaddaeus, and Simon the Cananaean,</v>
<v n="19">and Judas Iscariot, who betrayed him.</v>
<v n="20">Then he went home, and the crowd gathered again, so that they could not even eat.</v>
<v n="21">And when his family heard it, they went out to seize him, for they were saying, "He is out of his mind."</v>
<v n="22">And the scribes who came down from Jerusalem were saying, "He is possessed by Beelzebul," and "by the prince of demons he casts out the demons."</v>
<v n="23">And he called them to him and said to them in parables, "How can Satan cast out Satan?</v>
<v n="24">If a kingdom is divided against itself, that kingdom cannot stand.</v>
<v n="25">And if a house is divided against itself, that house will not be able to stand.</v>
<v n="26">And if Satan has risen up against himself and is divided, he cannot stand, but is coming to an end.</v>
<v n="27">But no one can enter a strong man's house and plunder his goods, unless he first binds the strong man. Then indeed he may plunder his house.</v>
<v n="28">"Truly, I say to you, all sins will be forgiven the children of man, and whatever blasphemies they utter,</v>
<v n="29">but whoever blasphemes against the Holy Spirit never has forgiveness, but is guilty of an eternal sin"--</v>
<v n="30">for they had said, "He has an unclean spirit."</v>
<v n="31">And his mother and his brothers came, and standing outside they sent to him and called him.</v>
<v n="32">And a crowd was sitting around him, and they said to him, "Your mother and your brothers are outside, seeking you."</v>
<v n="33">And he answered them, "Who are my mother and my brothers?"</v>
<v n="34">And looking about at those who sat around him, he said, "Here are my mother and my brothers!</v>
<v n="35">Whoever does the will of God, he is my brother and sister and mother."</v>
</c>
<c n="4">
<v n="1">Again he began to teach beside the sea. And a very large crowd gathered about him, so that he got into a boat and sat in it on the sea, and the whole crowd was beside the sea on the land.</v>
<v n="2">And he was teaching them many things in parables, and in his teaching he said to them:</v>
<v n="3">"Listen! A sower went out to sow.</v>
<v n="4">And as he sowed, some seed fell along the path, and the birds came and devoured it.</v>
<v n="5">Other seed fell on rocky ground, where it did not have much soil, and immediately it sprang up, since it had no depth of soil.</v>
<v n="6">And when the sun rose it was scorched, and since it had no root, it withered away.</v>
<v n="7">Other seed fell among thorns, and the thorns grew up and choked it, and it yielded no grain.</v>
<v n="8">And other seeds fell into good soil and produced grain, growing up and increasing and yielding thirtyfold and sixtyfold and a hundredfold."</v>
<v n="9">And he said, "He who has ears to hear, let him hear."</v>
<v n="10">And when he was alone, those around him with the twelve asked him about the parables.</v>
<v n="11">And he said to them, "To you has been given the secret of the kingdom of God, but for those outside everything is in parables,</v>
<v n="12">so that "they may indeed see but not perceive, and may indeed hear but not understand, lest they should turn and be forgiven."</v>
<v n="13">And he said to them, "Do you not understand this parable? How then will you understand all the parables?</v>
<v n="14">The sower sows the word.</v>
<v n="15">And these are the ones along the path, where the word is sown: when they hear, Satan immediately comes and takes away the word that is sown in them.</v>
<v n="16">And these are the ones sown on rocky ground: the ones who, when they hear the word, immediately receive it with joy.</v>
<v n="17">And they have no root in themselves, but endure for a while; then, when tribulation or persecution arises on account of the word, immediately they fall away.</v>
<v n="18">And others are the ones sown among thorns. They are those who hear the word,</v>
<v n="19">but the cares of the world and the deceitfulness of riches and the desires for other things enter in and choke the word, and it proves unfruitful.</v>
<v n="20">But those that were sown on the good soil are the ones who hear the word and accept it and bear fruit, thirtyfold and sixtyfold and a hundredfold."</v>
<v n="21">And he said to them, "Is a lamp brought in to be put under a basket, or under a bed, and not on a stand?</v>
<v n="22">For nothing is hidden except to be made manifest; nor is anything secret except to come to light.</v>
<v n="23">If anyone has ears to hear, let him hear."</v>
<v n="24">And he said to them, "Pay attention to what you hear: with the measure you use, it will be measured to you, and still more will be added to you.</v>
<v n="25">For to the one who has, more will be given, and from the one who has not, even what he has will be taken away."</v>
<v n="26">And he said, "The kingdom of God is as if a man should scatter seed on the ground.</v>
<v n="27">He sleeps and rises night and day, and the seed sprouts and grows; he knows not how.</v>
<v n="28">The earth produces by itself, first the blade, then the ear, then the full grain in the ear.</v>
<v n="29">But when the grain is ripe, at once he puts in the sickle, because the harvest has come."</v>
<v n="30">And he said, "With what can we compare the kingdom of God, or what parable shall we use for it?</v>
<v n="31">It is like a grain of mustard seed, which, when sown on the ground, is the smallest of all the seeds on earth,</v>
<v n="32">yet when it is sown it grows up and becomes larger than all the garden plants and puts out large branches, so that the birds of the air can make nests in its shade."</v>
<v n="33">With many such parables he spoke the word to them, as they were able to hear it.</v>
<v n="34">He did not speak to them without a parable, but privately to his own disciples he explained everything.</v>
<v n="35">On that day, when evening had come, he said to them, "Let us go across to the other side."</v>
<v n="36">And leaving the crowd, they took him with them in the boat, just as he was. And other boats were with him.</v>
<v n="37">And a great windstorm arose, and the waves were breaking into the boat, so that the boat was already filling.</v>
<v n="38">But he was in the stern, asleep on the cushion. And they woke him and said to him, "Teacher, do you not care that we are perishing?"</v>
<v n="39">And he awoke and rebuked the wind and said to the sea, "Peace! Be still!" And the wind ceased, and there was a great calm.</v>
<v n="40">He said to them, "Why are you so afraid? Have you still no faith?"</v>
<v n="41">And they were filled with great fear and said to one another, "Who then is this, that even wind and sea obey him?"</v>
</c>
<c n="5">
<v n="1">They came to the other side of the sea, to the country of the Gerasenes.</v>
<v n="2">And when Jesus had stepped out of the boat, immediately there met him out of the tombs a man with an unclean spirit.</v>
<v n="3">He lived among the tombs. And no one could bind him anymore, not even with a chain,</v>
<v n="4">for he had often been bound with shackles and chains, but he wrenched the chains apart, and he broke the shackles in pieces. No one had the strength to subdue him.</v>
<v n="5">Night and day among the tombs and on the mountains he was always crying out and bruising himself with stones.</v>
<v n="6">And when he saw Jesus from afar, he ran and fell down before him.</v>
<v n="7">And crying out with a loud voice, he said, "What have you to do with me, Jesus, Son of the Most High God? I adjure you by God, do not torment me."</v>
<v n="8">For he was saying to him, "Come out of the man, you unclean spirit!"</v>
<v n="9">And Jesus asked him, "What is your name?" He replied, "My name is Legion, for we are many."</v>
<v n="10">And he begged him earnestly not to send them out of the country.</v>
<v n="11">Now a great herd of pigs was feeding there on the hillside,</v>
<v n="12">and they begged him, saying, "Send us to the pigs; let us enter them."</v>
<v n="13">So he gave them permission. And the unclean spirits came out, and entered the pigs, and the herd, numbering about two thousand, rushed down the steep bank into the sea and were drowned in the sea.</v>
<v n="14">The herdsmen fled and told it in the city and in the country. And people came to see what it was that had happened.</v>
<v n="15">And they came to Jesus and saw the demon-possessed man, the one who had had the legion, sitting there, clothed and in his right mind, and they were afraid.</v>
<v n="16">And those who had seen it described to them what had happened to the demon-possessed man and to the pigs.</v>
<v n="17">And they began to beg Jesus to depart from their region.</v>
<v n="18">As he was getting into the boat, the man who had been possessed with demons begged him that he might be with him.</v>
<v n="19">And he did not permit him but said to him, "Go home to your friends and tell them how much the Lord has done for you, and how he has had mercy on you."</v>
<v n="20">And he went away and began to proclaim in the Decapolis how much Jesus had done for him, and everyone marveled.</v>
<v n="21">And when Jesus had crossed again in the boat to the other side, a great crowd gathered about him, and he was beside the sea.</v>
<v n="22">Then came one of the rulers of the synagogue, Jairus by name, and seeing him, he fell at his feet</v>
<v n="23">and implored him earnestly, saying, "My little daughter is at the point of death. Come and lay your hands on her, so that she may be made well and live."</v>
<v n="24">And he went with him.And a great crowd followed him and thronged about him.</v>
<v n="25">And there was a woman who had had a discharge of blood for twelve years,</v>
<v n="26">and who had suffered much under many physicians, and had spent all that she had, and was no better but rather grew worse.</v>
<v n="27">She had heard the reports about Jesus and came up behind him in the crowd and touched his garment.</v>
<v n="28">For she said, "If I touch even his garments, I will be made well."</v>
<v n="29">And immediately the flow of blood dried up, and she felt in her body that she was healed of her disease.</v>
<v n="30">And Jesus, perceiving in himself that power had gone out from him, immediately turned about in the crowd and said, "Who touched my garments?"</v>
<v n="31">And his disciples said to him, "You see the crowd pressing around you, and yet you say, 'Who touched me?'"</v>
<v n="32">And he looked around to see who had done it.</v>
<v n="33">But the woman, knowing what had happened to her, came in fear and trembling and fell down before him and told him the whole truth.</v>
<v n="34">And he said to her, "Daughter, your faith has made you well; go in peace, and be healed of your disease."</v>
<v n="35">While he was still speaking, there came from the ruler's house some who said, "Your daughter is dead. Why trouble the Teacher any further?"</v>
<v n="36">But overhearing what they said, Jesus said to the ruler of the synagogue, "Do not fear, only believe."</v>
<v n="37">And he allowed no one to follow him except Peter and James and John the brother of James.</v>
<v n="38">They came to the house of the ruler of the synagogue, and Jesus saw a commotion, people weeping and wailing loudly.</v>
<v n="39">And when he had entered, he said to them, "Why are you making a commotion and weeping? The child is not dead but sleeping."</v>
<v n="40">And they laughed at him. But he put them all outside and took the child's father and mother and those who were with him and went in where the child was.</v>
<v n="41">Taking her by the hand he said to her, "Talitha cumi," which means, "Little girl, I say to you, arise."</v>
<v n="42">And immediately the girl got up and began walking (for she was twelve years of age), and they were immediately overcome with amazement.</v>
<v n="43">And he strictly charged them that no one should know this, and told them to give her something to eat.</v>
</c>
<c n="6">
<v n="1">He went away from there and came to his hometown, and his disciples followed him.</v>
<v n="2">And on the Sabbath he began to teach in the synagogue, and many who heard him were astonished, saying, "Where did this man get these things? What is the wisdom given to him? How are such mighty works done by his hands?</v>
<v n="3">Is not this the carpenter, the son of Mary and brother of James and Joses and Judas and Simon? And are not his sisters here with us?" And they took offense at him.</v>
<v n="4">And Jesus said to them, "A prophet is not without honor, except in his hometown and among his relatives and in his own household."</v>
<v n="5">And he could do no mighty work there, except that he laid his hands on a few sick people and healed them.</v>
<v n="6">And he marveled because of their unbelief.And he went about among the villages teaching.</v>
<v n="7">And he called the twelve and began to send them out two by two, and gave them authority over the unclean spirits.</v>
<v n="8">He charged them to take nothing for their journey except a staff--no bread, no bag, no money in their belts--</v>
<v n="9">but to wear sandals and not put on two tunics.</v>
<v n="10">And he said to them, "Whenever you enter a house, stay there until you depart from there.</v>
<v n="11">And if any place will not receive you and they will not listen to you, when you leave, shake off the dust that is on your feet as a testimony against them."</v>
<v n="12">So they went out and proclaimed that people should repent.</v>
<v n="13">And they cast out many demons and anointed with oil many who were sick and healed them.</v>
<v n="14">King Herod heard of it, for Jesus' name had become known. Some said, "John the Baptist has been raised from the dead. That is why these miraculous powers are at work in him."</v>
<v n="15">But others said, "He is Elijah." And others said, "He is a prophet, like one of the prophets of old."</v>
<v n="16">But when Herod heard of it, he said, "John, whom I beheaded, has been raised."</v>
<v n="17">For it was Herod who had sent and seized John and bound him in prison for the sake of Herodias, his brother Philip's wife, because he had married her.</v>
<v n="18">For John had been saying to Herod, "It is not lawful for you to have your brother's wife."</v>
<v n="19">And Herodias had a grudge against him and wanted to put him to death. But she could not,</v>
<v n="20">for Herod feared John, knowing that he was a righteous and holy man, and he kept him safe. When he heard him, he was greatly perplexed, and yet he heard him gladly.</v>
<v n="21">But an opportunity came when Herod on his birthday gave a banquet for his nobles and military commanders and the leading men of Galilee.</v>
<v n="22">For when Herodias's daughter came in and danced, she pleased Herod and his guests. And the king said to the girl, "Ask me for whatever you wish, and I will give it to you."</v>
<v n="23">And he vowed to her, "Whatever you ask me, I will give you, up to half of my kingdom."</v>
<v n="24">And she went out and said to her mother, "For what should I ask?" And she said, "The head of John the Baptist."</v>
<v n="25">And she came in immediately with haste to the king and asked, saying, "I want you to give me at once the head of John the Baptist on a platter."</v>
<v n="26">And the king was exceedingly sorry, but because of his oaths and his guests he did not want to break his word to her.</v>
<v n="27">And immediately the king sent an executioner with orders to bring John's head. He went and beheaded him in the prison</v>
<v n="28">and brought his head on a platter and gave it to the girl, and the girl gave it to her mother.</v>
<v n="29">When his disciples heard of it, they came and took his body and laid it in a tomb.</v>
<v n="30">The apostles returned to Jesus and told him all that they had done and taught.</v>
<v n="31">And he said to them, "Come away by yourselves to a desolate place and rest a while." For many were coming and going, and they had no leisure even to eat.</v>
<v n="32">And they went away in the boat to a desolate place by themselves.</v>
<v n="33">Now many saw them going and recognized them, and they ran there on foot from all the towns and got there ahead of them.</v>
<v n="34">When he went ashore he saw a great crowd, and he had compassion on them, because they were like sheep without a shepherd. And he began to teach them many things.</v>
