<v n="35">And when it grew late, his disciples came to him and said, "This is a desolate place, and the hour is now late.</v>
<v n="36">Send them away to go into the surrounding countryside and villages and buy themselves something to eat."</v>
<v n="37">But he answered them, "You give them something to eat." And they said to him, "Shall we go and buy two hundred denarii worth of bread and give it to them to eat?"</v>
<v n="38">And he said to them, "How many loaves do you have? Go and see." And when they had found out, they said, "Five, and two fish."</v>
<v n="39">Then he commanded them all to sit down in groups on the green grass.</v>
<v n="40">So they sat down in groups, by hundreds and by fifties.</v>
<v n="41">And taking the five loaves and the two fish he looked up to heaven and said a blessing and broke the loaves and gave them to the disciples to set before the people. And he divided the two fish among them all.</v>
<v n="42">And they all ate and were satisfied.</v>
<v n="43">And they took up twelve baskets full of broken pieces and of the fish.</v>
<v n="44">And those who ate the loaves were five thousand men.</v>
<v n="45">Immediately he made his disciples get into the boat and go before him to the other side, to Bethsaida, while he dismissed the crowd.</v>
<v n="46">And after he had taken leave of them, he went up on the mountain to pray.</v>
<v n="47">And when evening came, the boat was out on the sea, and he was alone on the land.</v>
<v n="48">And he saw that they were making headway painfully, for the wind was against them. And about the fourth watch of the night he came to them, walking on the sea. He meant to pass by them,</v>
<v n="49">but when they saw him walking on the sea they thought it was a ghost, and cried out,</v>
<v n="50">for they all saw him and were terrified. But immediately he spoke to them and said, "Take heart; it is I. Do not be afraid."</v>
<v n="51">And he got into the boat with them, and the wind ceased. And they were utterly astounded,</v>
<v n="52">for they did not understand about the loaves, but their hearts were hardened.</v>
<v n="53">When they had crossed over, they came to land at Gennesaret and moored to the shore.</v>
<v n="54">And when they got out of the boat, the people immediately recognized him</v>
<v n="55">and ran about the whole region and began to bring the sick people on their beds to wherever they heard he was.</v>
<v n="56">And wherever he came, in villages, cities, or countryside, they laid the sick in the marketplaces and implored him that they might touch even the fringe of his garment. And as many as touched it were made well.</v>
</c>
<c n="7">
<v n="1">Now when the Pharisees gathered to him, with some of the scribes who had come from Jerusalem,</v>
<v n="2">they saw that some of his disciples ate with hands that were defiled, that is, unwashed.</v>
<v n="3">(For the Pharisees and all the Jews do not eat unless they wash their hands, holding to the tradition of the elders,</v>
<v n="4">and when they come from the marketplace, they do not eat unless they wash. And there are many other traditions that they observe, such as the washing of cups and pots and copper vessels and dining couches. )</v>
<v n="5">And the Pharisees and the scribes asked him, "Why do your disciples not walk according to the tradition of the elders, but eat with defiled hands?"</v>
<v n="6">And he said to them, "Well did Isaiah prophesy of you hypocrites, as it is written, "'This people honors me with their lips, but their heart is far from me;</v>
<v n="7">in vain do they worship me, teaching as doctrines the commandments of men.'</v>
<v n="8">You leave the commandment of God and hold to the tradition of men."</v>
<v n="9">And he said to them, "You have a fine way of rejecting the commandment of God in order to establish your tradition!</v>
<v n="10">For Moses said, 'Honor your father and your mother'; and, 'Whoever reviles father or mother must surely die.'</v>
<v n="11">But you say, 'If a man tells his father or his mother, Whatever you would have gained from me is Corban' (that is, given to God)--</v>
<v n="12">then you no longer permit him to do anything for his father or mother,</v>
<v n="13">thus making void the word of God by your tradition that you have handed down. And many such things you do."</v>
<v n="14">And he called the people to him again and said to them, "Hear me, all of you, and understand:</v>
<v n="15">There is nothing outside a person that by going into him can defile him, but the things that come out of a person are what defile him."</v>
<v n="16">See Footnote</v>
<v n="17">And when he had entered the house and left the people, his disciples asked him about the parable.</v>
<v n="18">And he said to them, "Then are you also without understanding? Do you not see that whatever goes into a person from outside cannot defile him,</v>
<v n="19">since it enters not his heart but his stomach, and is expelled?" (Thus he declared all foods clean.)</v>
<v n="20">And he said, "What comes out of a person is what defiles him.</v>
<v n="21">For from within, out of the heart of man, come evil thoughts, sexual immorality, theft, murder, adultery,</v>
<v n="22">coveting, wickedness, deceit, sensuality, envy, slander, pride, foolishness.</v>
<v n="23">All these evil things come from within, and they defile a person."</v>
<v n="24">And from there he arose and went away to the region of Tyre and Sidon. And he entered a house and did not want anyone to know, yet he could not be hidden.</v>
<v n="25">But immediately a woman whose little daughter was possessed by an unclean spirit heard of him and came and fell down at his feet.</v>
<v n="26">Now the woman was a Gentile, a Syrophoenician by birth. And she begged him to cast the demon out of her daughter.</v>
<v n="27">And he said to her, "Let the children be fed first, for it is not right to take the children's bread and throw it to the dogs."</v>
<v n="28">But she answered him, "Yes, Lord; yet even the dogs under the table eat the children's crumbs."</v>
<v n="29">And he said to her, "For this statement you may go your way; the demon has left your daughter."</v>
<v n="30">And she went home and found the child lying in bed and the demon gone.</v>
<v n="31">Then he returned from the region of Tyre and went through Sidon to the Sea of Galilee, in the region of the Decapolis.</v>
<v n="32">And they brought to him a man who was deaf and had a speech impediment, and they begged him to lay his hand on him.</v>
<v n="33">And taking him aside from the crowd privately, he put his fingers into his ears, and after spitting touched his tongue.</v>
<v n="34">And looking up to heaven, he sighed and said to him, "Ephphatha," that is, "Be opened."</v>
<v n="35">And his ears were opened, his tongue was released, and he spoke plainly.</v>
<v n="36">And Jesus charged them to tell no one. But the more he charged them, the more zealously they proclaimed it.</v>
<v n="37">And they were astonished beyond measure, saying, "He has done all things well. He even makes the deaf hear and the mute speak."</v>
</c>
<c n="8">
<v n="1">In those days, when again a great crowd had gathered, and they had nothing to eat, he called his disciples to him and said to them,</v>
<v n="2">"I have compassion on the crowd, because they have been with me now three days and have nothing to eat.</v>
<v n="3">And if I send them away hungry to their homes, they will faint on the way. And some of them have come from far away."</v>
<v n="4">And his disciples answered him, "How can one feed these people with bread here in this desolate place?"</v>
<v n="5">And he asked them, "How many loaves do you have?" They said, "Seven."</v>
<v n="6">And he directed the crowd to sit down on the ground. And he took the seven loaves, and having given thanks, he broke them and gave them to his disciples to set before the people; and they set them before the crowd.</v>
<v n="7">And they had a few small fish. And having blessed them, he said that these also should be set before them.</v>
<v n="8">And they ate and were satisfied. And they took up the broken pieces left over, seven baskets full.</v>
<v n="9">And there were about four thousand people. And he sent them away.</v>
<v n="10">And immediately he got into the boat with his disciples and went to the district of Dalmanutha.</v>
<v n="11">The Pharisees came and began to argue with him, seeking from him a sign from heaven to test him.</v>
<v n="12">And he sighed deeply in his spirit and said, "Why does this generation seek a sign? Truly, I say to you, no sign will be given to this generation."</v>
<v n="13">And he left them, got into the boat again, and went to the other side.</v>
<v n="14">Now they had forgotten to bring bread, and they had only one loaf with them in the boat.</v>
<v n="15">And he cautioned them, saying, "Watch out; beware of the leaven of the Pharisees and the leaven of Herod."</v>
<v n="16">And they began discussing with one another the fact that they had no bread.</v>
<v n="17">And Jesus, aware of this, said to them, "Why are you discussing the fact that you have no bread? Do you not yet perceive or understand? Are your hearts hardened?</v>
<v n="18">Having eyes do you not see, and having ears do you not hear? And do you not remember?</v>
<v n="19">When I broke the five loaves for the five thousand, how many baskets full of broken pieces did you take up?" They said to him, "Twelve."</v>
<v n="20">"And the seven for the four thousand, how many baskets full of broken pieces did you take up?" And they said to him, "Seven."</v>
<v n="21">And he said to them, "Do you not yet understand?"</v>
<v n="22">And they came to Bethsaida. And some people brought to him a blind man and begged him to touch him.</v>
<v n="23">And he took the blind man by the hand and led him out of the village, and when he had spit on his eyes and laid his hands on him, he asked him, "Do you see anything?"</v>
<v n="24">And he looked up and said, "I see men, but they look like trees, walking."</v>
<v n="25">Then Jesus laid his hands on his eyes again; and he opened his eyes, his sight was restored, and he saw everything clearly.</v>
<v n="26">And he sent him to his home, saying, "Do not even enter the village."</v>
<v n="27">And Jesus went on with his disciples to the villages of Caesarea Philippi. And on the way he asked his disciples, "Who do people say that I am?"</v>
<v n="28">And they told him, "John the Baptist; and others say, Elijah; and others, one of the prophets."</v>
<v n="29">And he asked them, "But who do you say that I am?" Peter answered him, "You are the Christ."</v>
<v n="30">And he strictly charged them to tell no one about him.</v>
<v n="31">And he began to teach them that the Son of Man must suffer many things and be rejected by the elders and the chief priests and the scribes and be killed, and after three days rise again.</v>
<v n="32">And he said this plainly. And Peter took him aside and began to rebuke him.</v>
<v n="33">But turning and seeing his disciples, he rebuked Peter and said, "Get behind me, Satan! For you are not setting your mind on the things of God, but on the things of man."</v>
<v n="34">And he called to him the crowd with his disciples and said to them, "If anyone would come after me, let him deny himself and take up his cross and follow me.</v>
<v n="35">For whoever would save his life will lose it, but whoever loses his life for my sake and the gospel's will save it.</v>
<v n="36">For what does it profit a man to gain the whole world and forfeit his life?</v>
<v n="37">For what can a man give in return for his life?</v>
<v n="38">For whoever is ashamed of me and of my words in this adulterous and sinful generation, of him will the Son of Man also be ashamed when he comes in the glory of his Father with the holy angels."</v>
</c>
<c n="9">
<v n="1">And he said to them, "Truly, I say to you, there are some standing here who will not taste death until they see the kingdom of God after it has come with power."</v>
<v n="2">And after six days Jesus took with him Peter and James and John, and led them up a high mountain by themselves. And he was transfigured before them,</v>
<v n="3">and his clothes became radiant, intensely white, as no one on earth could bleach them.</v>
<v n="4">And there appeared to them Elijah with Moses, and they were talking with Jesus.</v>
<v n="5">And Peter said to Jesus, "Rabbi, it is good that we are here. Let us make three tents, one for you and one for Moses and one for Elijah."</v>
<v n="6">For he did not know what to say, for they were terrified.</v>
<v n="7">And a cloud overshadowed them, and a voice came out of the cloud, "This is my beloved Son; listen to him."</v>
<v n="8">And suddenly, looking around, they no longer saw anyone with them but Jesus only.</v>
<v n="9">And as they were coming down the mountain, he charged them to tell no one what they had seen, until the Son of Man had risen from the dead.</v>
<v n="10">So they kept the matter to themselves, questioning what this rising from the dead might mean.</v>
<v n="11">And they asked him, "Why do the scribes say that first Elijah must come?"</v>
<v n="12">And he said to them, "Elijah does come first to restore all things. And how is it written of the Son of Man that he should suffer many things and be treated with contempt?</v>
<v n="13">But I tell you that Elijah has come, and they did to him whatever they pleased, as it is written of him."</v>
<v n="14">And when they came to the disciples, they saw a great crowd around them, and scribes arguing with them.</v>
<v n="15">And immediately all the crowd, when they saw him, were greatly amazed and ran up to him and greeted him.</v>
<v n="16">And he asked them, "What are you arguing about with them?"</v>
<v n="17">And someone from the crowd answered him, "Teacher, I brought my son to you, for he has a spirit that makes him mute.</v>
<v n="18">And whenever it seizes him, it throws him down, and he foams and grinds his teeth and becomes rigid. So I asked your disciples to cast it out, and they were not able."</v>
<v n="19">And he answered them, "O faithless generation, how long am I to be with you? How long am I to bear with you? Bring him to me."</v>
<v n="20">And they brought the boy to him. And when the spirit saw him, immediately it convulsed the boy, and he fell on the ground and rolled about, foaming at the mouth.</v>
<v n="21">And Jesus asked his father, "How long has this been happening to him?" And he said, "From childhood.</v>
<v n="22">And it has often cast him into fire and into water, to destroy him. But if you can do anything, have compassion on us and help us."</v>
<v n="23">And Jesus said to him, "If you can! All things are possible for one who believes."</v>
<v n="24">Immediately the father of the child cried out and said, "I believe; help my unbelief!"</v>
<v n="25">And when Jesus saw that a crowd came running together, he rebuked the unclean spirit, saying to it, "You mute and deaf spirit, I command you, come out of him and never enter him again."</v>
<v n="26">And after crying out and convulsing him terribly, it came out, and the boy was like a corpse, so that most of them said, "He is dead."</v>
<v n="27">But Jesus took him by the hand and lifted him up, and he arose.</v>
<v n="28">And when he had entered the house, his disciples asked him privately, "Why could we not cast it out?"</v>
<v n="29">And he said to them, "This kind cannot be driven out by anything but prayer."</v>
<v n="30">They went on from there and passed through Galilee. And he did not want anyone to know,</v>
<v n="31">for he was teaching his disciples, saying to them, "The Son of Man is going to be delivered into the hands of men, and they will kill him. And when he is killed, after three days he will rise."</v>
<v n="32">But they did not understand the saying, and were afraid to ask him.</v>
<v n="33">And they came to Capernaum. And when he was in the house he asked them, "What were you discussing on the way?"</v>
<v n="34">But they kept silent, for on the way they had argued with one another about who was the greatest.</v>
<v n="35">And he sat down and called the twelve. And he said to them, "If anyone would be first, he must be last of all and servant of all."</v>
<v n="36">And he took a child and put him in the midst of them, and taking him in his arms, he said to them,</v>
<v n="37">"Whoever receives one such child in my name receives me, and whoever receives me, receives not me but him who sent me."</v>
<v n="38">John said to him, "Teacher, we saw someone casting out demons in your name, and we tried to stop him, because he was not following us."</v>
<v n="39">But Jesus said, "Do not stop him, for no one who does a mighty work in my name will be able soon afterward to speak evil of me.</v>
<v n="40">For the one who is not against us is for us.</v>
<v n="41">For truly, I say to you, whoever gives you a cup of water to drink because you belong to Christ will by no means lose his reward.</v>
<v n="42">"Whoever causes one of these little ones who believe in me to sin, it would be better for him if a great millstone were hung around his neck and he were thrown into the sea.</v>
<v n="43">And if your hand causes you to sin, cut it off. It is better for you to enter life crippled than with two hands to go to hell, to the unquenchable fire.</v>
<v n="44">See Footnote</v>
<v n="45">And if your foot causes you to sin, cut it off. It is better for you to enter life lame than with two feet to be thrown into hell.</v>
<v n="46">See Footnote</v>
<v n="47">And if your eye causes you to sin, tear it out. It is better for you to enter the kingdom of God with one eye than with two eyes to be thrown into hell,</v>
<v n="48">'where their worm does not die and the fire is not quenched.'</v>
<v n="49">For everyone will be salted with fire.</v>
<v n="50">Salt is good, but if the salt has lost its saltiness, how will you make it salty again? Have salt in yourselves, and be at peace with one another."</v>
</c>
<c n="10">
<v n="1">And he left there and went to the region of Judea and beyond the Jordan, and crowds gathered to him again. And again, as was his custom, he taught them.</v>
<v n="2">And Pharisees came up and in order to test him asked, "Is it lawful for a man to divorce his wife?"</v>
<v n="3">He answered them, "What did Moses command you?"</v>
<v n="4">They said, "Moses allowed a man to write a certificate of divorce and to send her away."</v>
<v n="5">And Jesus said to them, "Because of your hardness of heart he wrote you this commandment.</v>
<v n="6">But from the beginning of creation, 'God made them male and female.'</v>
<v n="7">'Therefore a man shall leave his father and mother and hold fast to his wife,</v>
<v n="8">and they shall become one flesh.' So they are no longer two but one flesh.</v>
<v n="9">What therefore God has joined together, let not man separate."</v>
<v n="10">And in the house the disciples asked him again about this matter.</v>
<v n="11">And he said to them, "Whoever divorces his wife and marries another commits adultery against her,</v>
<v n="12">and if she divorces her husband and marries another, she commits adultery."</v>
<v n="13">And they were bringing children to him that he might touch them, and the disciples rebuked them.</v>
<v n="14">But when Jesus saw it, he was indignant and said to them, "Let the children come to me; do not hinder them, for to such belongs the kingdom of God.</v>
<v n="15">Truly, I say to you, whoever does not receive the kingdom of God like a child shall not enter it."</v>
<v n="16">And he took them in his arms and blessed them, laying his hands on them.</v>
<v n="17">And as he was setting out on his journey, a man ran up and knelt before him and asked him, "Good Teacher, what must I do to inherit eternal life?"</v>
<v n="18">And Jesus said to him, "Why do you call me good? No one is good except God alone.</v>
<v n="19">You know the commandments: 'Do not murder, Do not commit adultery, Do not steal, Do not bear false witness, Do not defraud, Honor your father and mother.'"</v>
<v n="20">And he said to him, "Teacher, all these I have kept from my youth."</v>
<v n="21">And Jesus, looking at him, loved him, and said to him, "You lack one thing: go, sell all that you have and give to the poor, and you will have treasure in heaven; and come, follow me."</v>
<v n="22">Disheartened by the saying, he went away sorrowful, for he had great possessions.</v>
<v n="23">And Jesus looked around and said to his disciples, "How difficult it will be for those who have wealth to enter the kingdom of God!"</v>
<v n="24">And the disciples were amazed at his words. But Jesus said to them again, "Children, how difficult it is to enter the kingdom of God!</v>
<v n="25">It is easier for a camel to go through the eye of a needle than for a rich person to enter the kingdom of God."</v>
<v n="26">And they were exceedingly astonished, and said to him, "Then who can be saved?"</v>
<v n="27">Jesus looked at them and said, "With man it is impossible, but not with God. For all things are possible with God."</v>
<v n="28">Peter began to say to him, "See, we have left everything and followed you."</v>
<v n="29">Jesus said, "Truly, I say to you, there is no one who has left house or brothers or sisters or mother or father or children or lands, for my sake and for the gospel,</v>
<v n="30">who will not receive a hundredfold now in this time, houses and brothers and sisters and mothers and children and lands, with persecutions, and in the age to come eternal life.</v>
<v n="31">But many who are first will be last, and the last first."</v>
<v n="32">And they were on the road, going up to Jerusalem, and Jesus was walking ahead of them. And they were amazed, and those who followed were afraid. And taking the twelve again, he began to tell them what was to happen to him,</v>
<v n="33">saying, "See, we are going up to Jerusalem, and the Son of Man will be delivered over to the chief priests and the scribes, and they will condemn him to death and deliver him over to the Gentiles.</v>
<v n="34">And they will mock him and spit on him, and flog him and kill him. And after three days he will rise."</v>
<v n="35">And James and John, the sons of Zebedee, came up to him and said to him, "Teacher, we want you to do for us whatever we ask of you."</v>
<v n="36">And he said to them, "What do you want me to do for you?"</v>
<v n="37">And they said to him, "Grant us to sit, one at your right hand and one at your left, in your glory."</v>
<v n="38">Jesus said to them, "You do not know what you are asking. Are you able to drink the cup that I drink, or to be baptized with the baptism with which I am baptized?"</v>
<v n="39">And they said to him, "We are able." And Jesus said to them, "The cup that I drink you will drink, and with the baptism with which I am baptized, you will be baptized,</v>
<v n="40">but to sit at my right hand or at my left is not mine to grant, but it is for those for whom it has been prepared."</v>
<v n="41">And when the ten heard it, they began to be indignant at James and John.</v>
<v n="42">And Jesus called them to him and said to them, "You know that those who are considered rulers of the Gentiles lord it over them, and their great ones exercise authority over them.</v>
<v n="43">But it shall not be so among you. But whoever would be great among you must be your servant,</v>
<v n="44">and whoever would be first among you must be slave of all.</v>
<v n="45">For even the Son of Man came not to be served but to serve, and to give his life as a ransom for many."</v>
<v n="46">And they came to Jericho. And as he was leaving Jericho with his disciples and a great crowd, Bartimaeus, a blind beggar, the son of Timaeus, was sitting by the roadside.</v>
<v n="47">And when he heard that it was Jesus of Nazareth, he began to cry out and say, "Jesus, Son of David, have mercy on me!"</v>
<v n="48">And many rebuked him, telling him to be silent. But he cried out all the more, "Son of David, have mercy on me!"</v>
<v n="49">And Jesus stopped and said, "Call him." And they called the blind man, saying to him, "Take heart. Get up; he is calling you."</v>
<v n="50">And throwing off his cloak, he sprang up and came to Jesus.</v>
<v n="51">And Jesus said to him, "What do you want me to do for you?" And the blind man said to him, "Rabbi, let me recover my sight."</v>
<v n="52">And Jesus said to him, "Go your way; your faith has made you well." And immediately he recovered his sight and followed him on the way.</v>
</c>
<c n="11">
<v n="1">Now when they drew near to Jerusalem, to Bethphage and Bethany, at the Mount of Olives, Jesus sent two of his disciples</v>
<v n="2">and said to them, "Go into the village in front of you, and immediately as you enter it you will find a colt tied, on which no one has ever sat. Untie it and bring it.</v>
<v n="3">If anyone says to you, 'Why are you doing this?' say, 'The Lord has need of it and will send it back here immediately.'"</v>
<v n="4">And they went away and found a colt tied at a door outside in the street, and they untied it.</v>
<v n="5">And some of those standing there said to them, "What are you doing, untying the colt?"</v>
<v n="6">And they told them what Jesus had said, and they let them go.</v>
<v n="7">And they brought the colt to Jesus and threw their cloaks on it, and he sat on it.</v>
<v n="8">And many spread their cloaks on the road, and others spread leafy branches that they had cut from the fields.</v>
<v n="9">And those who went before and those who followed were shouting, "Hosanna! Blessed is he who comes in the name of the Lord!</v>
<v n="10">Blessed is the coming kingdom of our father David! Hosanna in the highest!"</v>
<v n="11">And he entered Jerusalem and went into the temple. And when he had looked around at everything, as it was already late, he went out to Bethany with the twelve.</v>
<v n="12">On the following day, when they came from Bethany, he was hungry.</v>
<v n="13">And seeing in the distance a fig tree in leaf, he went to see if he could find anything on it. When he came to it, he found nothing but leaves, for it was not the season for figs.</v>
<v n="14">And he said to it, "May no one ever eat fruit from you again." And his disciples heard it.</v>
<v n="15">And they came to Jerusalem. And he entered the temple and began to drive out those who sold and those who bought in the temple, and he overturned the tables of the money-changers and the seats of those who sold pigeons.</v>
<v n="16">And he would not allow anyone to carry anything through the temple.</v>
<v n="17">And he was teaching them and saying to them, "Is it not written, 'My house shall be called a house of prayer for all the nations'? But you have made it a den of robbers."</v>
<v n="18">And the chief priests and the scribes heard it and were seeking a way to destroy him, for they feared him, because all the crowd was astonished at his teaching.</v>
<v n="19">And when evening came they went out of the city.</v>
<v n="20">As they passed by in the morning, they saw the fig tree withered away to its roots.</v>
<v n="21">And Peter remembered and said to him, "Rabbi, look! The fig tree that you cursed has withered."</v>
<v n="22">And Jesus answered them, "Have faith in God.</v>
<v n="23">Truly, I say to you, whoever says to this mountain, 'Be taken up and thrown into the sea,' and does not doubt in his heart, but believes that what he says will come to pass, it will be done for him.</v>
<v n="24">Therefore I tell you, whatever you ask in prayer, believe that you have received it, and it will be yours.</v>
<v n="25">And whenever you stand praying, forgive, if you have anything against anyone, so that your Father also who is in heaven may forgive you your trespasses."</v>
<v n="26">See Footnote</v>
<v n="27">And they came again to Jerusalem. And as he was walking in the temple, the chief priests and the scribes and the elders came to him,</v>
<v n="28">and they said to him, "By what authority are you doing these things, or who gave you this authority to do them?"</v>
<v n="29">Jesus said to them, "I will ask you one question; answer me, and I will tell you by what authority I do these things.</v>
<v n="30">Was the baptism of John from heaven or from man? Answer me."</v>
<v n="31">And they discussed it with one another, saying, "If we say, 'From heaven,' he will say, 'Why then did you not believe him?'</v>
<v n="32">But shall we say, 'From man'?"--they were afraid of the people, for they all held that John really was a prophet.</v>
<v n="33">So they answered Jesus, "We do not know." And Jesus said to them, "Neither will I tell you by what authority I do these things."</v>
</c>
<c n="12">
<v n="1">And he began to speak to them in parables. "A man planted a vineyard and put a fence around it and dug a pit for the winepress and built a tower, and leased it to tenants and went into another country.</v>
<v n="2">When the season came, he sent a servant to the tenants to get from them some of the fruit of the vineyard.</v>
<v n="3">And they took him and beat him and sent him away empty-handed.</v>
<v n="4">Again he sent to them another servant, and they struck him on the head and treated him shamefully.</v>
<v n="5">And he sent another, and him they killed. And so with many others: some they beat, and some they killed.</v>
<v n="6">He had still one other, a beloved son. Finally he sent him to them, saying, 'They will respect my son.'</v>
<v n="7">But those tenants said to one another, 'This is the heir. Come, let us kill him, and the inheritance will be ours.'</v>
<v n="8">And they took him and killed him and threw him out of the vineyard.</v>
<v n="9">What will the owner of the vineyard do? He will come and destroy the tenants and give the vineyard to others.</v>
<v n="10">Have you not read this Scripture: "'The stone that the builders rejected has become the cornerstone;</v>
<v n="11">this was the Lord's doing, and it is marvelous in our eyes'?"</v>
<v n="12">And they were seeking to arrest him but feared the people, for they perceived that he had told the parable against them. So they left him and went away.</v>
<v n="13">And they sent to him some of the Pharisees and some of the Herodians, to trap him in his talk.</v>
<v n="14">And they came and said to him, "Teacher, we know that you are true and do not care about anyone's opinion. For you are not swayed by appearances, but truly teach the way of God. Is it lawful to pay taxes to Caesar, or not? Should we pay them, or should we not?"</v>
<v n="15">But, knowing their hypocrisy, he said to them, "Why put me to the test? Bring me a denarius and let me look at it."</v>
<v n="16">And they brought one. And he said to them, "Whose likeness and inscription is this?" They said to him, "Caesar's."</v>
<v n="17">Jesus said to them, "Render to Caesar the things that are Caesar's, and to God the things that are God's." And they marveled at him.</v>
<v n="18">And Sadducees came to him, who say that there is no resurrection. And they asked him a question, saying,</v>
<v n="19">"Teacher, Moses wrote for us that if a man's brother dies and leaves a wife, but leaves no child, the man must take the widow and raise up offspring for his brother.</v>
<v n="20">There were seven brothers; the first took a wife, and when he died left no offspring.</v>
<v n="21">And the second took her, and died, leaving no offspring. And the third likewise.</v>
<v n="22">And the seven left no offspring. Last of all the woman also died.</v>
<v n="23">In the resurrection, when they rise again, whose wife will she be? For the seven had her as wife."</v>
<v n="24">Jesus said to them, "Is this not the reason you are wrong, because you know neither the Scriptures nor the power of God?</v>
<v n="25">For when they rise from the dead, they neither marry nor are given in marriage, but are like angels in heaven.</v>
<v n="26">And as for the dead being raised, have you not read in the book of Moses, in the passage about the bush, how God spoke to him, saying, 'I am the God of Abraham, and the God of Isaac, and the God of Jacob'?</v>
<v n="27">He is not God of the dead, but of the living. You are quite wrong."</v>
<v n="28">And one of the scribes came up and heard them disputing with one another, and seeing that he answered them well, asked him, "Which commandment is the most important of all?"</v>
<v n="29">Jesus answered, "The most important is, 'Hear, O Israel: The Lord our God, the Lord is one.</v>
<v n="30">And you shall love the Lord your God with all your heart and with all your soul and with all your mind and with all your strength.'</v>
<v n="31">The second is this: 'You shall love your neighbor as yourself.' There is no other commandment greater than these."</v>
<v n="32">And the scribe said to him, "You are right, Teacher. You have truly said that he is one, and there is no other besides him.</v>
<v n="33">And to love him with all the heart and with all the understanding and with all the strength, and to love one's neighbor as oneself, is much more than all whole burnt offerings and sacrifices."</v>
<v n="34">And when Jesus saw that he answered wisely, he said to him, "You are not far from the kingdom of God." And after that no one dared to ask him any more questions.</v>
<v n="35">And as Jesus taught in the temple, he said, "How can the scribes say that the Christ is the son of David?</v>
<v n="36">David himself, in the Holy Spirit, declared, "'The Lord said to my Lord, Sit at my right hand, until I put your enemies under your feet.'</v>
<v n="37">David himself calls him Lord. So how is he his son?" And the great throng heard him gladly.</v>
<v n="38">And in his teaching he said, "Beware of the scribes, who like to walk around in long robes and like greetings in the marketplaces</v>
<v n="39">and have the best seats in the synagogues and the places of honor at feasts,</v>
<v n="40">who devour widows' houses and for a pretense make long prayers. They will receive the greater condemnation."</v>
<v n="41">And he sat down opposite the treasury and watched the people putting money into the offering box. Many rich people put in large sums.</v>
<v n="42">And a poor widow came and put in two small copper coins, which make a penny.</v>
<v n="43">And he called his disciples to him and said to them, "Truly, I say to you, this poor widow has put in more than all those who are contributing to the offering box.</v>
<v n="44">For they all contributed out of their abundance, but she out of her poverty has put in everything she had, all she had to live on."</v>
</c>
<c n="13">
<v n="1">And as he came out of the temple, one of his disciples said to him, "Look, Teacher, what wonderful stones and what wonderful buildings!"</v>
<v n="2">And Jesus said to him, "Do you see these great buildings? There will not be left here one stone upon another that will not be thrown down."</v>
<v n="3">And as he sat on the Mount of Olives opposite the temple, Peter and James and John and Andrew asked him privately,</v>
<v n="4">"Tell us, when will these things be, and what will be the sign when all these things are about to be accomplished?"</v>
<v n="5">And Jesus began to say to them, "See that no one leads you astray.</v>
<v n="6">Many will come in my name, saying, 'I am he!' and they will lead many astray.</v>
<v n="7">And when you hear of wars and rumors of wars, do not be alarmed. This must take place, but the end is not yet.</v>
<v n="8">For nation will rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom. There will be earthquakes in various places; there will be famines. These are but the beginning of the birth pains.</v>
<v n="9">"But be on your guard. For they will deliver you over to councils, and you will be beaten in synagogues, and you will stand before governors and kings for my sake, to bear witness before them.</v>
<v n="10">And the gospel must first be proclaimed to all nations.</v>
<v n="11">And when they bring you to trial and deliver you over, do not be anxious beforehand what you are to say, but say whatever is given you in that hour, for it is not you who speak, but the Holy Spirit.</v>
<v n="12">And brother will deliver brother over to death, and the father his child, and children will rise against parents and have them put to death.</v>
<v n="13">And you will be hated by all for my name's sake. But the one who endures to the end will be saved.</v>
<v n="14">"But when you see the abomination of desolation standing where it ought not to be (let the reader understand), then let those who are in Judea flee to the mountains.</v>
<v n="15">Let the one who is on the housetop not go down, nor enter his house, to take anything out,</v>
<v n="16">and let the one who is in the field not turn back to take his cloak.</v>
<v n="17">And alas for women who are pregnant and for those who are nursing infants in those days!</v>
<v n="18">Pray that it may not happen in winter.</v>
<v n="19">For in those days there will be such tribulation as has not been from the beginning of the creation that God created until now, and never will be.</v>
<v n="20">And if the Lord had not cut short the days, no human being would be saved. But for the sake of the elect, whom he chose, he shortened the days.</v>
<v n="21">And then if anyone says to you, 'Look, here is the Christ!' or 'Look, there he is!' do not believe it.</v>
<v n="22">False christs and false prophets will arise and perform signs and wonders, to lead astray, if possible, the elect.</v>
<v n="23">But be on guard; I have told you all things beforehand.</v>
<v n="24">"But in those days, after that tribulation, the sun will be darkened, and the moon will not give its light,</v>
<v n="25">and the stars will be falling from heaven, and the powers in the heavens will be shaken.</v>
<v n="26">And then they will see the Son of Man coming in clouds with great power and glory.</v>
<v n="27">And then he will send out the angels and gather his elect from the four winds, from the ends of the earth to the ends of heaven.</v>
<v n="28">"From the fig tree learn its lesson: as soon as its branch becomes tender and puts out its leaves, you know that summer is near.</v>
<v n="29">So also, when you see these things taking place, you know that he is near, at the very gates.</v>
<v n="30">Truly, I say to you, this generation will not pass away until all these things take place.</v>
<v n="31">Heaven and earth will pass away, but my words will not pass away.</v>
<v n="32">"But concerning that day or that hour, no one knows, not even the angels in heaven, nor the Son, but only the Father.</v>
<v n="33">Be on guard, keep awake. For you do not know when the time will come.</v>
<v n="34">It is like a man going on a journey, when he leaves home and puts his servants in charge, each with his work, and commands the doorkeeper to stay awake.</v>
<v n="35">Therefore stay awake--for you do not know when the master of the house will come, in the evening, or at midnight, or when the cock crows, or in the morning--</v>
<v n="36">lest he come suddenly and find you asleep.</v>
<v n="37">And what I say to you I say to all: Stay awake."</v>
</c>
<c n="14">
<v n="1">It was now two days before the Passover and the Feast of Unleavened Bread. And the chief priests and the scribes were seeking how to arrest him by stealth and kill him,</v>
<v n="2">for they said, "Not during the feast, lest there be an uproar from the people."</v>
<v n="3">And while he was at Bethany in the house of Simon the leper, as he was reclining at table, a woman came with an alabaster flask of ointment of pure nard, very costly, and she broke the flask and poured it over his head.</v>
<v n="4">There were some who said to themselves indignantly, "Why was the ointment wasted like that?</v>
<v n="5">For this ointment could have been sold for more than three hundred denarii and given to the poor." And they scolded her.</v>
<v n="6">But Jesus said, "Leave her alone. Why do you trouble her? She has done a beautiful thing to me.</v>
<v n="7">For you always have the poor with you, and whenever you want, you can do good for them. But you will not always have me.</v>
<v n="8">She has done what she could; she has anointed my body beforehand for burial.</v>
<v n="9">And truly, I say to you, wherever the gospel is proclaimed in the whole world, what she has done will be told in memory of her."</v>
<v n="10">Then Judas Iscariot, who was one of the twelve, went to the chief priests in order to betray him to them.</v>
<v n="11">And when they heard it, they were glad and promised to give him money. And he sought an opportunity to betray him.</v>
<v n="12">And on the first day of Unleavened Bread, when they sacrificed the Passover lamb, his disciples said to him, "Where will you have us go and prepare for you to eat the Passover?"</v>
<v n="13">And he sent two of his disciples and said to them, "Go into the city, and a man carrying a jar of water will meet you. Follow him,</v>
<v n="14">and wherever he enters, say to the master of the house, 'The Teacher says, Where is my guest room, where I may eat the Passover with my disciples?'</v>
<v n="15">And he will show you a large upper room furnished and ready; there prepare for us."</v>
<v n="16">And the disciples set out and went to the city and found it just as he had told them, and they prepared the Passover.</v>
<v n="17">And when it was evening, he came with the twelve.</v>
<v n="18">And as they were reclining at table and eating, Jesus said, "Truly, I say to you, one of you will betray me, one who is eating with me."</v>
<v n="19">They began to be sorrowful and to say to him one after another, "Is it I?"</v>
<v n="20">He said to them, "It is one of the twelve, one who is dipping bread into the dish with me.</v>
<v n="21">For the Son of Man goes as it is written of him, but woe to that man by whom the Son of Man is betrayed! It would have been better for that man if he had not been born."</v>
<v n="22">And as they were eating, he took bread, and after blessing it broke it and gave it to them, and said, "Take; this is my body."</v>
<v n="23">And he took a cup, and when he had given thanks he gave it to them, and they all drank of it.</v>
<v n="24">And he said to them, "This is my blood of the covenant, which is poured out for many.</v>
<v n="25">Truly, I say to you, I will not drink again of the fruit of the vine until that day when I drink it new in the kingdom of God."</v>
<v n="26">And when they had sung a hymn, they went out to the Mount of Olives.</v>
<v n="27">And Jesus said to them, "You will all fall away, for it is written, 'I will strike the shepherd, and the sheep will be scattered.'</v>
<v n="28">But after I am raised up, I will go before you to Galilee."</v>
<v n="29">Peter said to him, "Even though they all fall away, I will not."</v>
<v n="30">And Jesus said to him, "Truly, I tell you, this very night, before the rooster crows twice, you will deny me three times."</v>
<v n="31">But he said emphatically, "If I must die with you, I will not deny you." And they all said the same.</v>
<v n="32">And they went to a place called Gethsemane. And he said to his disciples, "Sit here while I pray."</v>
<v n="33">And he took with him Peter and James and John, and began to be greatly distressed and troubled.</v>
<v n="34">And he said to them, "My soul is very sorrowful, even to death. Remain here and watch."</v>
<v n="35">And going a little farther, he fell on the ground and prayed that, if it were possible, the hour might pass from him.</v>
<v n="36">And he said, "Abba, Father, all things are possible for you. Remove this cup from me. Yet not what I will, but what you will."</v>
<v n="37">And he came and found them sleeping, and he said to Peter, "Simon, are you asleep? Could you not watch one hour?</v>
<v n="38">Watch and pray that you may not enter into temptation. The spirit indeed is willing, but the flesh is weak."</v>
<v n="39">And again he went away and prayed, saying the same words.</v>
<v n="40">And again he came and found them sleeping, for their eyes were very heavy, and they did not know what to answer him.</v>
<v n="41">And he came the third time and said to them, "Are you still sleeping and taking your rest? It is enough; the hour has come. The Son of Man is betrayed into the hands of sinners.</v>
<v n="42">Rise, let us be going; see, my betrayer is at hand."</v>
<v n="43">And immediately, while he was still speaking, Judas came, one of the twelve, and with him a crowd with swords and clubs, from the chief priests and the scribes and the elders.</v>
<v n="44">Now the betrayer had given them a sign, saying, "The one I will kiss is the man. Seize him and lead him away under guard."</v>
<v n="45">And when he came, he went up to him at once and said, "Rabbi!" And he kissed him.</v>
<v n="46">And they laid hands on him and seized him.</v>
<v n="47">But one of those who stood by drew his sword and struck the servant of the high priest and cut off his ear.</v>
<v n="48">And Jesus said to them, "Have you come out as against a robber, with swords and clubs to capture me?</v>
<v n="49">Day after day I was with you in the temple teaching, and you did not seize me. But let the Scriptures be fulfilled."</v>
<v n="50">And they all left him and fled.</v>
<v n="51">And a young man followed him, with nothing but a linen cloth about his body. And they seized him,</v>
<v n="52">but he left the linen cloth and ran away naked.</v>
<v n="53">And they led Jesus to the high priest. And all the chief priests and the elders and the scribes came together.</v>
<v n="54">And Peter had followed him at a distance, right into the courtyard of the high priest. And he was sitting with the guards and warming himself at the fire.</v>
<v n="55">Now the chief priests and the whole Council were seeking testimony against Jesus to put him to death, but they found none.</v>
<v n="56">For many bore false witness against him, but their testimony did not agree.</v>
<v n="57">And some stood up and bore false witness against him, saying,</v>
<v n="58">"We heard him say, 'I will destroy this temple that is made with hands, and in three days I will build another, not made with hands.'"</v>
<v n="59">Yet even about this their testimony did not agree.</v>
<v n="60">And the high priest stood up in the midst and asked Jesus, "Have you no answer to make? What is it that these men testify against you?"</v>
<v n="61">But he remained silent and made no answer. Again the high priest asked him, "Are you the Christ, the Son of the Blessed?"</v>
<v n="62">And Jesus said, "I am, and you will see the Son of Man seated at the right hand of Power, and coming with the clouds of heaven."</v>
<v n="63">And the high priest tore his garments and said, "What further witnesses do we need?</v>
<v n="64">You have heard his blasphemy. What is your decision?" And they all condemned him as deserving death.</v>
<v n="65">And some began to spit on him and to cover his face and to strike him, saying to him, "Prophesy!" And the guards received him with blows.</v>
<v n="66">And as Peter was below in the courtyard, one of the servant girls of the high priest came,</v>
<v n="67">and seeing Peter warming himself, she looked at him and said, "You also were with the Nazarene, Jesus."</v>
<v n="68">But he denied it, saying, "I neither know nor understand what you mean." And he went out into the gateway and the rooster crowed.</v>
<v n="69">And the servant girl saw him and began again to say to the bystanders, "This man is one of them."</v>
<v n="70">But again he denied it. And after a little while the bystanders again said to Peter, "Certainly you are one of them, for you are a Galilean."</v>
<v n="71">But he began to invoke a curse on himself and to swear, "I do not know this man of whom you speak."</v>
<v n="72">And immediately the rooster crowed a second time. And Peter remembered how Jesus had said to him, "Before the rooster crows twice, you will deny me three times." And he broke down and wept.</v>
</c>
<c n="15">
<v n="1">And as soon as it was morning, the chief priests held a consultation with the elders and scribes and the whole Council. And they bound Jesus and led him away and delivered him over to Pilate.</v>
<v n="2">And Pilate asked him, "Are you the King of the Jews?" And he answered him, "You have said so."</v>
<v n="3">And the chief priests accused him of many things.</v>
<v n="4">And Pilate again asked him, "Have you no answer to make? See how many charges they bring against you."</v>
<v n="5">But Jesus made no further answer, so that Pilate was amazed.</v>
<v n="6">Now at the feast he used to release for them one prisoner for whom they asked.</v>
<v n="7">And among the rebels in prison, who had committed murder in the insurrection, there was a man called Barabbas.</v>
<v n="8">And the crowd came up and began to ask Pilate to do as he usually did for them.</v>
<v n="9">And he answered them, saying, "Do you want me to release for you the King of the Jews?"</v>
<v n="10">For he perceived that it was out of envy that the chief priests had delivered him up.</v>
<v n="11">But the chief priests stirred up the crowd to have him release for them Barabbas instead.</v>
<v n="12">And Pilate again said to them, "Then what shall I do with the man you call the King of the Jews?"</v>
<v n="13">And they cried out again, "Crucify him."</v>
<v n="14">And Pilate said to them, "Why, what evil has he done?" But they shouted all the more, "Crucify him."</v>
<v n="15">So Pilate, wishing to satisfy the crowd, released for them Barabbas, and having scourged Jesus, he delivered him to be crucified.</v>
<v n="16">And the soldiers led him away inside the palace (that is, the governor's headquarters), and they called together the whole battalion.</v>
<v n="17">And they clothed him in a purple cloak, and twisting together a crown of thorns, they put it on him.</v>
<v n="18">And they began to salute him, "Hail, King of the Jews!"</v>
<v n="19">And they were striking his head with a reed and spitting on him and kneeling down in homage to him.</v>
<v n="20">And when they had mocked him, they stripped him of the purple cloak and put his own clothes on him. And they led him out to crucify him.</v>
<v n="21">And they compelled a passerby, Simon of Cyrene, who was coming in from the country, the father of Alexander and Rufus, to carry his cross.</v>
<v n="22">And they brought him to the place called Golgotha (which means Place of a Skull).</v>
<v n="23">And they offered him wine mixed with myrrh, but he did not take it.</v>
<v n="24">And they crucified him and divided his garments among them, casting lots for them, to decide what each should take.</v>
<v n="25">And it was the third hour when they crucified him.</v>
<v n="26">And the inscription of the charge against him read, "The King of the Jews."</v>
<v n="27">And with him they crucified two robbers, one on his right and one on his left.</v>
<v n="28">See Footnote</v>
<v n="29">And those who passed by derided him, wagging their heads and saying, "Aha! You who would destroy the temple and rebuild it in three days,</v>
<v n="30">save yourself, and come down from the cross!"</v>
<v n="31">So also the chief priests with the scribes mocked him to one another, saying, "He saved others; he cannot save himself.</v>
<v n="32">Let the Christ, the King of Israel, come down now from the cross that we may see and believe." Those who were crucified with him also reviled him.</v>
<v n="33">And when the sixth hour had come, there was darkness over the whole land until the ninth hour.</v>
<v n="34">And at the ninth hour Jesus cried with a loud voice, "Eloi, Eloi, lema sabachthani?" which means, "My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?"</v>
<v n="35">And some of the bystanders hearing it said, "Behold, he is calling Elijah."</v>
<v n="36">And someone ran and filled a sponge with sour wine, put it on a reed and gave it to him to drink, saying, "Wait, let us see whether Elijah will come to take him down."</v>
<v n="37">And Jesus uttered a loud cry and breathed his last.</v>
<v n="38">And the curtain of the temple was torn in two, from top to bottom.</v>
<v n="39">And when the centurion, who stood facing him, saw that in this way he breathed his last, he said, "Truly this man was the Son of God!"</v>
<v n="40">There were also women looking on from a distance, among whom were Mary Magdalene, and Mary the mother of James the younger and of Joses, and Salome.</v>
<v n="41">When he was in Galilee, they followed him and ministered to him, and there were also many other women who came up with him to Jerusalem.</v>
<v n="42">And when evening had come, since it was the day of Preparation, that is, the day before the Sabbath,</v>
<v n="43">Joseph of Arimathea, a respected member of the Council, who was also himself looking for the kingdom of God, took courage and went to Pilate and asked for the body of Jesus.</v>
<v n="44">Pilate was surprised to hear that he should have already died. And summoning the centurion, he asked him whether he was already dead.</v>
<v n="45">And when he learned from the centurion that he was dead, he granted the corpse to Joseph.</v>
<v n="46">And Joseph bought a linen shroud, and taking him down, wrapped him in the linen shroud and laid him in a tomb that had been cut out of the rock. And he rolled a stone against the entrance of the tomb.</v>
<v n="47">Mary Magdalene and Mary the mother of Joses saw where he was laid.</v>
</c>
<c n="16">
<v n="1">When the Sabbath was past, Mary Magdalene and Mary the mother of James and Salome bought spices, so that they might go and anoint him.</v>
<v n="2">And very early on the first day of the week, when the sun had risen, they went to the tomb.</v>
<v n="3">And they were saying to one another, "Who will roll away the stone for us from the entrance of the tomb?"</v>
<v n="4">And looking up, they saw that the stone had been rolled back--it was very large.</v>
<v n="5">And entering the tomb, they saw a young man sitting on the right side, dressed in a white robe, and they were alarmed.</v>
<v n="6">And he said to them, "Do not be alarmed. You seek Jesus of Nazareth, who was crucified. He has risen; he is not here. See the place where they laid him.</v>
<v n="7">But go, tell his disciples and Peter that he is going before you to Galilee. There you will see him, just as he told you."</v>
<v n="8">And they went out and fled from the tomb, for trembling and astonishment had seized them, and they said nothing to anyone, for they were afraid. [Some of the earliest manuscripts do not include 16:9-20.]</v>
<v n="9">[[Now when he rose early on the first day of the week, he appeared first to Mary Magdalene, from whom he had cast out seven demons.</v>
<v n="10">She went and told those who had been with him, as they mourned and wept.</v>
<v n="11">But when they heard that he was alive and had been seen by her, they would not believe it.</v>
<v n="12">After these things he appeared in another form to two of them, as they were walking into the country.</v>
<v n="13">And they went back and told the rest, but they did not believe them.</v>
<v n="14">Afterward he appeared to the eleven themselves as they were reclining at table, and he rebuked them for their unbelief and hardness of heart, because they had not believed those who saw him after he had risen.</v>
<v n="15">And he said to them, "Go into all the world and proclaim the gospel to the whole creation.</v>
<v n="16">Whoever believes and is baptized will be saved, but whoever does not believe will be condemned.</v>
<v n="17">And these signs will accompany those who believe: in my name they will cast out demons; they will speak in new tongues;</v>
<v n="18">they will pick up serpents with their hands; and if they drink any deadly poison, it will not hurt them; they will lay their hands on the sick, and they will recover."</v>
<v n="19">So then the Lord Jesus, after he had spoken to them, was taken up into heaven and sat down at the right hand of God.</v>
<v n="20">And they went out and preached everywhere, while the Lord worked with them and confirmed the message by accompanying signs.]]</v>
</c>
</b>
<b n="Luke">
<c n="1">
<v n="1">Inasmuch as many have undertaken to compile a narrative of the things that have been accomplished among us,</v>
<v n="2">just as those who from the beginning were eyewitnesses and ministers of the word have delivered them to us,</v>
<v n="3">it seemed good to me also, having followed all things closely for some time past, to write an orderly account for you, most excellent Theophilus,</v>
<v n="4">that you may have certainty concerning the things you have been taught.</v>
<v n="5">In the days of Herod, king of Judea, there was a priest named Zechariah, of the division of Abijah. And he had a wife from the daughters of Aaron, and her name was Elizabeth.</v>
<v n="6">And they were both righteous before God, walking blamelessly in all the commandments and statutes of the Lord.</v>
<v n="7">But they had no child, because Elizabeth was barren, and both were advanced in years.</v>
<v n="8">Now while he was serving as priest before God when his division was on duty,</v>
<v n="9">according to the custom of the priesthood, he was chosen by lot to enter the temple of the Lord and burn incense.</v>
<v n="10">And the whole multitude of the people were praying outside at the hour of incense.</v>
<v n="11">And there appeared to him an angel of the Lord standing on the right side of the altar of incense.</v>
<v n="12">And Zechariah was troubled when he saw him, and fear fell upon him.</v>
<v n="13">But the angel said to him, "Do not be afraid, Zechariah, for your prayer has been heard, and your wife Elizabeth will bear you a son, and you shall call his name John.</v>
<v n="14">And you will have joy and gladness, and many will rejoice at his birth,</v>
<v n="15">for he will be great before the Lord. And he must not drink wine or strong drink, and he will be filled with the Holy Spirit, even from his mother's womb.</v>
<v n="16">And he will turn many of the children of Israel to the Lord their God,</v>
<v n="17">and he will go before him in the spirit and power of Elijah, to turn the hearts of the fathers to the children, and the disobedient to the wisdom of the just, to make ready for the Lord a people prepared."</v>
<v n="18">And Zechariah said to the angel, "How shall I know this? For I am an old man, and my wife is advanced in years."</v>
<v n="19">And the angel answered him, "I am Gabriel, who stands in the presence of God, and I was sent to speak to you and to bring you this good news.</v>
<v n="20">And behold, you will be silent and unable to speak until the day that these things take place, because you did not believe my words, which will be fulfilled in their time."</v>
<v n="21">And the people were waiting for Zechariah, and they were wondering at his delay in the temple.</v>
<v n="22">And when he came out, he was unable to speak to them, and they realized that he had seen a vision in the temple. And he kept making signs to them and remained mute.</v>
<v n="23">And when his time of service was ended, he went to his home.</v>
<v n="24">After these days his wife Elizabeth conceived, and for five months she kept herself hidden, saying,</v>
<v n="25">"Thus the Lord has done for me in the days when he looked on me, to take away my reproach among people."</v>
<v n="26">In the sixth month the angel Gabriel was sent from God to a city of Galilee named Nazareth,</v>
<v n="27">to a virgin betrothed to a man whose name was Joseph, of the house of David. And the virgin's name was Mary.</v>
<v n="28">And he came to her and said, "Greetings, O favored one, the Lord is with you!"</v>
<v n="29">But she was greatly troubled at the saying, and tried to discern what sort of greeting this might be.</v>
<v n="30">And the angel said to her, "Do not be afraid, Mary, for you have found favor with God.</v>
<v n="31">And behold, you will conceive in your womb and bear a son, and you shall call his name Jesus.</v>
<v n="32">He will be great and will be called the Son of the Most High. And the Lord God will give to him the throne of his father David,</v>
<v n="33">and he will reign over the house of Jacob forever, and of his kingdom there will be no end."</v>
<v n="34">And Mary said to the angel, "How will this be, since I am a virgin?"</v>
<v n="35">And the angel answered her, "The Holy Spirit will come upon you, and the power of the Most High will overshadow you; therefore the child to be born will be called holy--the Son of God.</v>
<v n="36">And behold, your relative Elizabeth in her old age has also conceived a son, and this is the sixth month with her who was called barren.</v>
<v n="37">For nothing will be impossible with God."</v>
<v n="38">And Mary said, "Behold, I am the servant of the Lord; let it be to me according to your word." And the angel departed from her.</v>
<v n="39">In those days Mary arose and went with haste into the hill country, to a town in Judah,</v>
<v n="40">and she entered the house of Zechariah and greeted Elizabeth.</v>
<v n="41">And when Elizabeth heard the greeting of Mary, the baby leaped in her womb. And Elizabeth was filled with the Holy Spirit,</v>
<v n="42">and she exclaimed with a loud cry, "Blessed are you among women, and blessed is the fruit of your womb!</v>
<v n="43">And why is this granted to me that the mother of my Lord should come to me?</v>
<v n="44">For behold, when the sound of your greeting came to my ears, the baby in my womb leaped for joy.</v>
<v n="45">And blessed is she who believed that there would be a fulfillment of what was spoken to her from the Lord."</v>
<v n="46">And Mary said, "My soul magnifies the Lord,</v>
<v n="47">and my spirit rejoices in God my Savior,</v>
<v n="48">for he has looked on the humble estate of his servant. For behold, from now on all generations will call me blessed;</v>
<v n="49">for he who is mighty has done great things for me, and holy is his name.</v>
<v n="50">And his mercy is for those who fear him from generation to generation.</v>
<v n="51">He has shown strength with his arm; he has scattered the proud in the thoughts of their hearts;</v>
<v n="52">he has brought down the mighty from their thrones and exalted those of humble estate;</v>
<v n="53">he has filled the hungry with good things, and the rich he has sent empty away.</v>
<v n="54">He has helped his servant Israel, in remembrance of his mercy,</v>
<v n="55">as he spoke to our fathers, to Abraham and to his offspring forever."</v>
<v n="56">And Mary remained with her about three months and returned to her home.</v>
<v n="57">Now the time came for Elizabeth to give birth, and she bore a son.</v>
<v n="58">And her neighbors and relatives heard that the Lord had shown great mercy to her, and they rejoiced with her.</v>
<v n="59">And on the eighth day they came to circumcise the child. And they would have called him Zechariah after his father,</v>
<v n="60">but his mother answered, "No; he shall be called John."</v>
<v n="61">And they said to her, "None of your relatives is called by this name."</v>
<v n="62">And they made signs to his father, inquiring what he wanted him to be called.</v>
<v n="63">And he asked for a writing tablet and wrote, "His name is John." And they all wondered.</v>
<v n="64">And immediately his mouth was opened and his tongue loosed, and he spoke, blessing God.</v>
<v n="65">And fear came on all their neighbors. And all these things were talked about through all the hill country of Judea,</v>
<v n="66">and all who heard them laid them up in their hearts, saying, "What then will this child be?" For the hand of the Lord was with him.</v>
<v n="67">And his father Zechariah was filled with the Holy Spirit and prophesied, saying,</v>
<v n="68">"Blessed be the Lord God of Israel, for he has visited and redeemed his people</v>
<v n="69">and has raised up a horn of salvation for us in the house of his servant David,</v>
<v n="70">as he spoke by the mouth of his holy prophets from of old,</v>
<v n="71">that we should be saved from our enemies and from the hand of all who hate us;</v>
<v n="72">to show the mercy promised to our fathers and to remember his holy covenant,</v>
<v n="73">the oath that he swore to our father Abraham, to grant us</v>
<v n="74">that we, being delivered from the hand of our enemies, might serve him without fear,</v>
<v n="75">in holiness and righteousness before him all our days.</v>
<v n="76">And you, child, will be called the prophet of the Most High; for you will go before the Lord to prepare his ways,</v>
<v n="77">to give knowledge of salvation to his people in the forgiveness of their sins,</v>
<v n="78">because of the tender mercy of our God, whereby the sunrise shall visit us from on high</v>
<v n="79">to give light to those who sit in darkness and in the shadow of death, to guide our feet into the way of peace."</v>
<v n="80">And the child grew and became strong in spirit, and he was in the wilderness until the day of his public appearance to Israel.</v>
</c>
<c n="2">
<v n="1">In those days a decree went out from Caesar Augustus that all the world should be registered.</v>
<v n="2">This was the first registration when Quirinius was governor of Syria.</v>
<v n="3">And all went to be registered, each to his own town.</v>
<v n="4">And Joseph also went up from Galilee, from the town of Nazareth, to Judea, to the city of David, which is called Bethlehem, because he was of the house and lineage of David,</v>
<v n="5">to be registered with Mary, his betrothed, who was with child.</v>
<v n="6">And while they were there, the time came for her to give birth.</v>
<v n="7">And she gave birth to her firstborn son and wrapped him in swaddling cloths and laid him in a manger, because there was no place for them in the inn.</v>
<v n="8">And in the same region there were shepherds out in the field, keeping watch over their flock by night.</v>
<v n="9">And an angel of the Lord appeared to them, and the glory of the Lord shone around them, and they were filled with fear.</v>
<v n="10">And the angel said to them, "Fear not, for behold, I bring you good news of a great joy that will be for all the people.</v>
<v n="11">For unto you is born this day in the city of David a Savior, who is Christ the Lord.</v>
<v n="12">And this will be a sign for you: you will find a baby wrapped in swaddling cloths and lying in a manger."</v>
<v n="13">And suddenly there was with the angel a multitude of the heavenly host praising God and saying,</v>
<v n="14">"Glory to God in the highest, and on earth peace among those with whom he is pleased!"</v>
<v n="15">When the angels went away from them into heaven, the shepherds said to one another, "Let us go over to Bethlehem and see this thing that has happened, which the Lord has made known to us."</v>
<v n="16">And they went with haste and found Mary and Joseph, and the baby lying in a manger.</v>
<v n="17">And when they saw it, they made known the saying that had been told them concerning this child.</v>
<v n="18">And all who heard it wondered at what the shepherds told them.</v>
<v n="19">But Mary treasured up all these things, pondering them in her heart.</v>
<v n="20">And the shepherds returned, glorifying and praising God for all they had heard and seen, as it had been told them.</v>
<v n="21">And at the end of eight days, when he was circumcised, he was called Jesus, the name given by the angel before he was conceived in the womb.</v>
<v n="22">And when the time came for their purification according to the Law of Moses, they brought him up to Jerusalem to present him to the Lord</v>
<v n="23">(as it is written in the Law of the Lord, "Every male who first opens the womb shall be called holy to the Lord")</v>
<v n="24">and to offer a sacrifice according to what is said in the Law of the Lord, "a pair of turtledoves, or two young pigeons."</v>
<v n="25">Now there was a man in Jerusalem, whose name was Simeon, and this man was righteous and devout, waiting for the consolation of Israel, and the Holy Spirit was upon him.</v>
<v n="26">And it had been revealed to him by the Holy Spirit that he would not see death before he had seen the Lord's Christ.</v>
<v n="27">And he came in the Spirit into the temple, and when the parents brought in the child Jesus, to do for him according to the custom of the Law,</v>
<v n="28">he took him up in his arms and blessed God and said,</v>
<v n="29">"Lord, now you are letting your servant depart in peace, according to your word;</v>
<v n="30">for my eyes have seen your salvation</v>
<v n="31">that you have prepared in the presence of all peoples,</v>
<v n="32">a light for revelation to the Gentiles, and for glory to your people Israel."</v>
<v n="33">And his father and his mother marveled at what was said about him.</v>
<v n="34">And Simeon blessed them and said to Mary his mother, "Behold, this child is appointed for the fall and rising of many in Israel, and for a sign that is opposed</v>
<v n="35">(and a sword will pierce through your own soul also), so that thoughts from many hearts may be revealed."</v>
<v n="36">And there was a prophetess, Anna, the daughter of Phanuel, of the tribe of Asher. She was advanced in years, having lived with her husband seven years from when she was a virgin,</v>
<v n="37">and then as a widow until she was eighty-four. She did not depart from the temple, worshiping with fasting and prayer night and day.</v>
<v n="38">And coming up at that very hour she began to give thanks to God and to speak of him to all who were waiting for the redemption of Jerusalem.</v>
<v n="39">And when they had performed everything according to the Law of the Lord, they returned into Galilee, to their own town of Nazareth.</v>
<v n="40">And the child grew and became strong, filled with wisdom. And the favor of God was upon him.</v>
<v n="41">Now his parents went to Jerusalem every year at the Feast of the Passover.</v>
<v n="42">And when he was twelve years old, they went up according to custom.</v>
<v n="43">And when the feast was ended, as they were returning, the boy Jesus stayed behind in Jerusalem. His parents did not know it,</v>
<v n="44">but supposing him to be in the group they went a day's journey, but then they began to search for him among their relatives and acquaintances,</v>
<v n="45">and when they did not find him, they returned to Jerusalem, searching for him.</v>
<v n="46">After three days they found him in the temple, sitting among the teachers, listening to them and asking them questions.</v>
<v n="47">And all who heard him were amazed at his understanding and his answers.</v>
<v n="48">And when his parents saw him, they were astonished. And his mother said to him, "Son, why have you treated us so? Behold, your father and I have been searching for you in great distress."</v>
<v n="49">And he said to them, "Why were you looking for me? Did you not know that I must be in my Father's house?"</v>
<v n="50">And they did not understand the saying that he spoke to them.</v>
<v n="51">And he went down with them and came to Nazareth and was submissive to them. And his mother treasured up all these things in her heart.</v>
<v n="52">And Jesus increased in wisdom and in stature and in favor with God and man.</v>
</c>
<c n="3">
<v n="1">In the fifteenth year of the reign of Tiberius Caesar, Pontius Pilate being governor of Judea, and Herod being tetrarch of Galilee, and his brother Philip tetrarch of the region of Ituraea and Trachonitis, and Lysanias tetrarch of Abilene,</v>
<v n="2">during the high priesthood of Annas and Caiaphas, the word of God came to John the son of Zechariah in the wilderness.</v>
<v n="3">And he went into all the region around the Jordan, proclaiming a baptism of repentance for the forgiveness of sins.</v>
<v n="4">As it is written in the book of the words of Isaiah the prophet, "The voice of one crying in the wilderness: 'Prepare the way of the Lord, make his paths straight.</v>
<v n="5">Every valley shall be filled, and every mountain and hill shall be made low, and the crooked shall become straight, and the rough places shall become level ways,</v>
<v n="6">and all flesh shall see the salvation of God.'"</v>
<v n="7">He said therefore to the crowds that came out to be baptized by him, "You brood of vipers! Who warned you to flee from the wrath to come?</v>
<v n="8">Bear fruits in keeping with repentance. And do not begin to say to yourselves, 'We have Abraham as our father.' For I tell you, God is able from these stones to raise up children for Abraham.</v>
<v n="9">Even now the axe is laid to the root of the trees. Every tree therefore that does not bear good fruit is cut down and thrown into the fire."</v>
<v n="10">And the crowds asked him, "What then shall we do?"</v>
<v n="11">And he answered them, "Whoever has two tunics is to share with him who has none, and whoever has food is to do likewise."</v>
<v n="12">Tax collectors also came to be baptized and said to him, "Teacher, what shall we do?"</v>
<v n="13">And he said to them, "Collect no more than you are authorized to do."</v>
<v n="14">Soldiers also asked him, "And we, what shall we do?" And he said to them, "Do not extort money from anyone by threats or by false accusation, and be content with your wages."</v>
<v n="15">As the people were in expectation, and all were questioning in their hearts concerning John, whether he might be the Christ,</v>
<v n="16">John answered them all, saying, "I baptize you with water, but he who is mightier than I is coming, the strap of whose sandals I am not worthy to untie. He will baptize you with the Holy Spirit and with fire.</v>
<v n="17">His winnowing fork is in his hand, to clear his threshing floor and to gather the wheat into his barn, but the chaff he will burn with unquenchable fire."</v>
<v n="18">So with many other exhortations he preached good news to the people.</v>
<v n="19">But Herod the tetrarch, who had been reproved by him for Herodias, his brother's wife, and for all the evil things that Herod had done,</v>
<v n="20">added this to them all, that he locked up John in prison.</v>
<v n="21">Now when all the people were baptized, and when Jesus also had been baptized and was praying, the heavens were opened,</v>
<v n="22">and the Holy Spirit descended on him in bodily form, like a dove; and a voice came from heaven, "You are my beloved Son; with you I am well pleased."</v>
<v n="23">Jesus, when he began his ministry, was about thirty years of age, being the son (as was supposed) of Joseph, the son of Heli,</v>
<v n="24">the son of Matthat, the son of Levi, the son of Melchi, the son of Jannai, the son of Joseph,</v>
<v n="25">the son of Mattathias, the son of Amos, the son of Nahum, the son of Esli, the son of Naggai,</v>
<v n="26">the son of Maath, the son of Mattathias, the son of Semein, the son of Josech, the son of Joda,</v>
<v n="27">the son of Joanan, the son of Rhesa, the son of Zerubbabel, the son of Shealtiel, the son of Neri,</v>
<v n="28">the son of Melchi, the son of Addi, the son of Cosam, the son of Elmadam, the son of Er,</v>
<v n="29">the son of Joshua, the son of Eliezer, the son of Jorim, the son of Matthat, the son of Levi,</v>
<v n="30">the son of Simeon, the son of Judah, the son of Joseph, the son of Jonam, the son of Eliakim,</v>
<v n="31">the son of Melea, the son of Menna, the son of Mattatha, the son of Nathan, the son of David,</v>
<v n="32">the son of Jesse, the son of Obed, the son of Boaz, the son of Sala, the son of Nahshon,</v>
<v n="33">the son of Amminadab, the son of Admin, the son of Arni, the son of Hezron, the son of Perez, the son of Judah,</v>
<v n="34">the son of Jacob, the son of Isaac, the son of Abraham, the son of Terah, the son of Nahor,</v>
<v n="35">the son of Serug, the son of Reu, the son of Peleg, the son of Eber, the son of Shelah,</v>
<v n="36">the son of Cainan, the son of Arphaxad, the son of Shem, the son of Noah, the son of Lamech,</v>
<v n="37">the son of Methuselah, the son of Enoch, the son of Jared, the son of Mahalaleel, the son of Cainan,</v>
<v n="38">the son of Enos, the son of Seth, the son of Adam, the son of God.</v>
</c>
<c n="4">
<v n="1">And Jesus, full of the Holy Spirit, returned from the Jordan and was led by the Spirit in the wilderness</v>
<v n="2">for forty days, being tempted by the devil. And he ate nothing during those days. And when they were ended, he was hungry.</v>
<v n="3">The devil said to him, "If you are the Son of God, command this stone to become bread."</v>
<v n="4">And Jesus answered him, "It is written, 'Man shall not live by bread alone.'"</v>
<v n="5">And the devil took him up and showed him all the kingdoms of the world in a moment of time,</v>
<v n="6">and said to him, "To you I will give all this authority and their glory, for it has been delivered to me, and I give it to whom I will.</v>
<v n="7">If you, then, will worship me, it will all be yours."</v>
<v n="8">And Jesus answered him, "It is written, "'You shall worship the Lord your God, and him only shall you serve.'"</v>
<v n="9">And he took him to Jerusalem and set him on the pinnacle of the temple and said to him, "If you are the Son of God, throw yourself down from here,</v>
<v n="10">for it is written, "'He will command his angels concerning you, to guard you,'</v>
<v n="11">and "'On their hands they will bear you up, lest you strike your foot against a stone.'"</v>
<v n="12">And Jesus answered him, "It is said, 'You shall not put the Lord your God to the test.'"</v>
<v n="13">And when the devil had ended every temptation, he departed from him until an opportune time.</v>
<v n="14">And Jesus returned in the power of the Spirit to Galilee, and a report about him went out through all the surrounding country.</v>
<v n="15">And he taught in their synagogues, being glorified by all.</v>
<v n="16">And he came to Nazareth, where he had been brought up. And as was his custom, he went to the synagogue on the Sabbath day, and he stood up to read.</v>
<v n="17">And the scroll of the prophet Isaiah was given to him. He unrolled the scroll and found the place where it was written,</v>
<v n="18">"The Spirit of the Lord is upon me, because he has anointed me to proclaim good news to the poor. He has sent me to proclaim liberty to the captives and recovering of sight to the blind, to set at liberty those who are oppressed,</v>
<v n="19">to proclaim the year of the Lord's favor."</v>
<v n="20">And he rolled up the scroll and gave it back to the attendant and sat down. And the eyes of all in the synagogue were fixed on him.</v>
<v n="21">And he began to say to them, "Today this Scripture has been fulfilled in your hearing."</v>
<v n="22">And all spoke well of him and marveled at the gracious words that were coming from his mouth. And they said, "Is not this Joseph's son?"</v>
<v n="23">And he said to them, "Doubtless you will quote to me this proverb, 'Physician, heal yourself.' What we have heard you did at Capernaum, do here in your hometown as well."</v>
<v n="24">And he said, "Truly, I say to you, no prophet is acceptable in his hometown.</v>
<v n="25">But in truth, I tell you, there were many widows in Israel in the days of Elijah, when the heavens were shut up three years and six months, and a great famine came over all the land,</v>
<v n="26">and Elijah was sent to none of them but only to Zarephath, in the land of Sidon, to a woman who was a widow.</v>
<v n="27">And there were many lepers in Israel in the time of the prophet Elisha, and none of them was cleansed, but only Naaman the Syrian."</v>
<v n="28">When they heard these things, all in the synagogue were filled with wrath.</v>
