<v n="14">I tell you, this man went down to his house justified, rather than the other. For everyone who exalts himself will be humbled, but the one who humbles himself will be exalted."</v>
<v n="15">Now they were bringing even infants to him that he might touch them. And when the disciples saw it, they rebuked them.</v>
<v n="16">But Jesus called them to him, saying, "Let the children come to me, and do not hinder them, for to such belongs the kingdom of God.</v>
<v n="17">Truly, I say to you, whoever does not receive the kingdom of God like a child shall not enter it."</v>
<v n="18">And a ruler asked him, "Good Teacher, what must I do to inherit eternal life?"</v>
<v n="19">And Jesus said to him, "Why do you call me good? No one is good except God alone.</v>
<v n="20">You know the commandments: 'Do not commit adultery, Do not murder, Do not steal, Do not bear false witness, Honor your father and mother.'"</v>
<v n="21">And he said, "All these I have kept from my youth."</v>
<v n="22">When Jesus heard this, he said to him, "One thing you still lack. Sell all that you have and distribute to the poor, and you will have treasure in heaven; and come, follow me."</v>
<v n="23">But when he heard these things, he became very sad, for he was extremely rich.</v>
<v n="24">Jesus, looking at him with sadness, said, "How difficult it is for those who have wealth to enter the kingdom of God!</v>
<v n="25">For it is easier for a camel to go through the eye of a needle than for a rich person to enter the kingdom of God."</v>
<v n="26">Those who heard it said, "Then who can be saved?"</v>
<v n="27">But he said, "What is impossible with men is possible with God."</v>
<v n="28">And Peter said, "See, we have left our homes and followed you."</v>
<v n="29">And he said to them, "Truly, I say to you, there is no one who has left house or wife or brothers or parents or children, for the sake of the kingdom of God,</v>
<v n="30">who will not receive many times more in this time, and in the age to come eternal life."</v>
<v n="31">And taking the twelve, he said to them, "See, we are going up to Jerusalem, and everything that is written about the Son of Man by the prophets will be accomplished.</v>
<v n="32">For he will be delivered over to the Gentiles and will be mocked and shamefully treated and spit upon.</v>
<v n="33">And after flogging him, they will kill him, and on the third day he will rise."</v>
<v n="34">But they understood none of these things. This saying was hidden from them, and they did not grasp what was said.</v>
<v n="35">As he drew near to Jericho, a blind man was sitting by the roadside begging.</v>
<v n="36">And hearing a crowd going by, he inquired what this meant.</v>
<v n="37">They told him, "Jesus of Nazareth is passing by."</v>
<v n="38">And he cried out, "Jesus, Son of David, have mercy on me!"</v>
<v n="39">And those who were in front rebuked him, telling him to be silent. But he cried out all the more, "Son of David, have mercy on me!"</v>
<v n="40">And Jesus stopped and commanded him to be brought to him. And when he came near, he asked him,</v>
<v n="41">"What do you want me to do for you?" He said, "Lord, let me recover my sight."</v>
<v n="42">And Jesus said to him, "Recover your sight; your faith has made you well."</v>
<v n="43">And immediately he recovered his sight and followed him, glorifying God. And all the people, when they saw it, gave praise to God.</v>
</c>
<c n="19">
<v n="1">He entered Jericho and was passing through.</v>
<v n="2">And there was a man named Zacchaeus. He was a chief tax collector and was rich.</v>
<v n="3">And he was seeking to see who Jesus was, but on account of the crowd he could not, because he was small of stature.</v>
<v n="4">So he ran on ahead and climbed up into a sycamore tree to see him, for he was about to pass that way.</v>
<v n="5">And when Jesus came to the place, he looked up and said to him, "Zacchaeus, hurry and come down, for I must stay at your house today."</v>
<v n="6">So he hurried and came down and received him joyfully.</v>
<v n="7">And when they saw it, they all grumbled, "He has gone in to be the guest of a man who is a sinner."</v>
<v n="8">And Zacchaeus stood and said to the Lord, "Behold, Lord, the half of my goods I give to the poor. And if I have defrauded anyone of anything, I restore it fourfold."</v>
<v n="9">And Jesus said to him, "Today salvation has come to this house, since he also is a son of Abraham.</v>
<v n="10">For the Son of Man came to seek and to save the lost."</v>
<v n="11">As they heard these things, he proceeded to tell a parable, because he was near to Jerusalem, and because they supposed that the kingdom of God was to appear immediately.</v>
<v n="12">He said therefore, "A nobleman went into a far country to receive for himself a kingdom and then return.</v>
<v n="13">Calling ten of his servants, he gave them ten minas, and said to them, 'Engage in business until I come.'</v>
<v n="14">But his citizens hated him and sent a delegation after him, saying, 'We do not want this man to reign over us.'</v>
<v n="15">When he returned, having received the kingdom, he ordered these servants to whom he had given the money to be called to him, that he might know what they had gained by doing business.</v>
<v n="16">The first came before him, saying, 'Lord, your mina has made ten minas more.'</v>
<v n="17">And he said to him, 'Well done, good servant! Because you have been faithful in a very little, you shall have authority over ten cities.'</v>
<v n="18">And the second came, saying, 'Lord, your mina has made five minas.'</v>
<v n="19">And he said to him, 'And you are to be over five cities.'</v>
<v n="20">Then another came, saying, 'Lord, here is your mina, which I kept laid away in a handkerchief;</v>
<v n="21">for I was afraid of you, because you are a severe man. You take what you did not deposit, and reap what you did not sow.'</v>
<v n="22">He said to him, 'I will condemn you with your own words, you wicked servant! You knew that I was a severe man, taking what I did not deposit and reaping what I did not sow?</v>
<v n="23">Why then did you not put my money in the bank, and at my coming I might have collected it with interest?'</v>
<v n="24">And he said to those who stood by, 'Take the mina from him, and give it to the one who has the ten minas.'</v>
<v n="25">And they said to him, 'Lord, he has ten minas!'</v>
<v n="26">'I tell you that to everyone who has, more will be given, but from the one who has not, even what he has will be taken away.</v>
<v n="27">But as for these enemies of mine, who did not want me to reign over them, bring them here and slaughter them before me.'"</v>
<v n="28">And when he had said these things, he went on ahead, going up to Jerusalem.</v>
<v n="29">When he drew near to Bethphage and Bethany, at the mount that is called Olivet, he sent two of the disciples,</v>
<v n="30">saying, "Go into the village in front of you, where on entering you will find a colt tied, on which no one has ever yet sat. Untie it and bring it here.</v>
<v n="31">If anyone asks you, 'Why are you untying it?' you shall say this: 'The Lord has need of it.'"</v>
<v n="32">So those who were sent went away and found it just as he had told them.</v>
<v n="33">And as they were untying the colt, its owners said to them, "Why are you untying the colt?"</v>
<v n="34">And they said, "The Lord has need of it."</v>
<v n="35">And they brought it to Jesus, and throwing their cloaks on the colt, they set Jesus on it.</v>
<v n="36">And as he rode along, they spread their cloaks on the road.</v>
<v n="37">As he was drawing near--already on the way down the Mount of Olives--the whole multitude of his disciples began to rejoice and praise God with a loud voice for all the mighty works that they had seen,</v>
<v n="38">saying, "Blessed is the King who comes in the name of the Lord! Peace in heaven and glory in the highest!"</v>
<v n="39">And some of the Pharisees in the crowd said to him, "Teacher, rebuke your disciples."</v>
<v n="40">He answered, "I tell you, if these were silent, the very stones would cry out."</v>
<v n="41">And when he drew near and saw the city, he wept over it,</v>
<v n="42">saying, "Would that you, even you, had known on this day the things that make for peace! But now they are hidden from your eyes.</v>
<v n="43">For the days will come upon you, when your enemies will set up a barricade around you and surround you and hem you in on every side</v>
<v n="44">and tear you down to the ground, you and your children within you. And they will not leave one stone upon another in you, because you did not know the time of your visitation."</v>
<v n="45">And he entered the temple and began to drive out those who sold,</v>
<v n="46">saying to them, "It is written, 'My house shall be a house of prayer,' but you have made it a den of robbers."</v>
<v n="47">And he was teaching daily in the temple. The chief priests and the scribes and the principal men of the people were seeking to destroy him,</v>
<v n="48">but they did not find anything they could do, for all the people were hanging on his words.</v>
</c>
<c n="20">
<v n="1">One day, as Jesus was teaching the people in the temple and preaching the gospel, the chief priests and the scribes with the elders came up</v>
<v n="2">and said to him, "Tell us by what authority you do these things, or who it is that gave you this authority."</v>
<v n="3">He answered them, "I also will ask you a question. Now tell me,</v>
<v n="4">Was the baptism of John from heaven or from man?"</v>
<v n="5">And they discussed it with one another, saying, "If we say, 'From heaven,' he will say, 'Why did you not believe him?'</v>
<v n="6">But if we say, 'From man,' all the people will stone us to death, for they are convinced that John was a prophet."</v>
<v n="7">So they answered that they did not know where it came from.</v>
<v n="8">And Jesus said to them, "Neither will I tell you by what authority I do these things."</v>
<v n="9">And he began to tell the people this parable: "A man planted a vineyard and let it out to tenants and went into another country for a long while.</v>
<v n="10">When the time came, he sent a servant to the tenants, so that they would give him some of the fruit of the vineyard. But the tenants beat him and sent him away empty-handed.</v>
<v n="11">And he sent another servant. But they also beat and treated him shamefully, and sent him away empty-handed.</v>
<v n="12">And he sent yet a third. This one also they wounded and cast out.</v>
<v n="13">Then the owner of the vineyard said, 'What shall I do? I will send my beloved son; perhaps they will respect him.'</v>
<v n="14">But when the tenants saw him, they said to themselves, 'This is the heir. Let us kill him, so that the inheritance may be ours.'</v>
<v n="15">And they threw him out of the vineyard and killed him. What then will the owner of the vineyard do to them?</v>
<v n="16">He will come and destroy those tenants and give the vineyard to others." When they heard this, they said, "Surely not!"</v>
<v n="17">But he looked directly at them and said, "What then is this that is written: "'The stone that the builders rejected has become the cornerstone'?</v>
<v n="18">Everyone who falls on that stone will be broken to pieces, and when it falls on anyone, it will crush him."</v>
<v n="19">The scribes and the chief priests sought to lay hands on him at that very hour, for they perceived that he had told this parable against them, but they feared the people.</v>
<v n="20">So they watched him and sent spies, who pretended to be sincere, that they might catch him in something he said, so as to deliver him up to the authority and jurisdiction of the governor.</v>
<v n="21">So they asked him, "Teacher, we know that you speak and teach rightly, and show no partiality, but truly teach the way of God.</v>
<v n="22">Is it lawful for us to give tribute to Caesar, or not?"</v>
<v n="23">But he perceived their craftiness, and said to them,</v>
<v n="24">"Show me a denarius. Whose likeness and inscription does it have?" They said, "Caesar's."</v>
<v n="25">He said to them, "Then render to Caesar the things that are Caesar's, and to God the things that are God's."</v>
<v n="26">And they were not able in the presence of the people to catch him in what he said, but marveling at his answer they became silent.</v>
<v n="27">There came to him some Sadducees, those who deny that there is a resurrection,</v>
<v n="28">and they asked him a question, saying, "Teacher, Moses wrote for us that if a man's brother dies, having a wife but no children, the man must take the widow and raise up offspring for his brother.</v>
<v n="29">Now there were seven brothers. The first took a wife, and died without children.</v>
<v n="30">And the second</v>
<v n="31">and the third took her, and likewise all seven left no children and died.</v>
<v n="32">Afterward the woman also died.</v>
<v n="33">In the resurrection, therefore, whose wife will the woman be? For the seven had her as wife."</v>
<v n="34">And Jesus said to them, "The sons of this age marry and are given in marriage,</v>
<v n="35">but those who are considered worthy to attain to that age and to the resurrection from the dead neither marry nor are given in marriage,</v>
<v n="36">for they cannot die anymore, because they are equal to angels and are sons of God, being sons of the resurrection.</v>
<v n="37">But that the dead are raised, even Moses showed, in the passage about the bush, where he calls the Lord the God of Abraham and the God of Isaac and the God of Jacob.</v>
<v n="38">Now he is not God of the dead, but of the living, for all live to him."</v>
<v n="39">Then some of the scribes answered, "Teacher, you have spoken well."</v>
<v n="40">For they no longer dared to ask him any question.</v>
<v n="41">But he said to them, "How can they say that the Christ is David's son?</v>
<v n="42">For David himself says in the Book of Psalms, "'The Lord said to my Lord, Sit at my right hand,</v>
<v n="43">until I make your enemies your footstool.'</v>
<v n="44">David thus calls him Lord, so how is he his son?"</v>
<v n="45">And in the hearing of all the people he said to his disciples,</v>
<v n="46">"Beware of the scribes, who like to walk around in long robes, and love greetings in the marketplaces and the best seats in the synagogues and the places of honor at feasts,</v>
<v n="47">who devour widows' houses and for a pretense make long prayers. They will receive the greater condemnation."</v>
</c>
<c n="21">
<v n="1">Jesus looked up and saw the rich putting their gifts into the offering box,</v>
<v n="2">and he saw a poor widow put in two small copper coins.</v>
<v n="3">And he said, "Truly, I tell you, this poor widow has put in more than all of them.</v>
<v n="4">For they all contributed out of their abundance, but she out of her poverty put in all she had to live on."</v>
<v n="5">And while some were speaking of the temple, how it was adorned with noble stones and offerings, he said,</v>
<v n="6">"As for these things that you see, the days will come when there will not be left here one stone upon another that will not be thrown down."</v>
<v n="7">And they asked him, "Teacher, when will these things be, and what will be the sign when these things are about to take place?"</v>
<v n="8">And he said, "See that you are not led astray. For many will come in my name, saying, 'I am he!' and, 'The time is at hand!' Do not go after them.</v>
<v n="9">And when you hear of wars and tumults, do not be terrified, for these things must first take place, but the end will not be at once."</v>
<v n="10">Then he said to them, "Nation will rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom.</v>
<v n="11">There will be great earthquakes, and in various places famines and pestilences. And there will be terrors and great signs from heaven.</v>
<v n="12">But before all this they will lay their hands on you and persecute you, delivering you up to the synagogues and prisons, and you will be brought before kings and governors for my name's sake.</v>
<v n="13">This will be your opportunity to bear witness.</v>
<v n="14">Settle it therefore in your minds not to meditate beforehand how to answer,</v>
<v n="15">for I will give you a mouth and wisdom, which none of your adversaries will be able to withstand or contradict.</v>
<v n="16">You will be delivered up even by parents and brothers and relatives and friends, and some of you they will put to death.</v>
<v n="17">You will be hated by all for my name's sake.</v>
<v n="18">But not a hair of your head will perish.</v>
<v n="19">By your endurance you will gain your lives.</v>
<v n="20">"But when you see Jerusalem surrounded by armies, then know that its desolation has come near.</v>
<v n="21">Then let those who are in Judea flee to the mountains, and let those who are inside the city depart, and let not those who are out in the country enter it,</v>
<v n="22">for these are days of vengeance, to fulfill all that is written.</v>
<v n="23">Alas for women who are pregnant and for those who are nursing infants in those days! For there will be great distress upon the earth and wrath against this people.</v>
<v n="24">They will fall by the edge of the sword and be led captive among all nations, and Jerusalem will be trampled underfoot by the Gentiles, until the times of the Gentiles are fulfilled.</v>
<v n="25">"And there will be signs in sun and moon and stars, and on the earth distress of nations in perplexity because of the roaring of the sea and the waves,</v>
<v n="26">people fainting with fear and with foreboding of what is coming on the world. For the powers of the heavens will be shaken.</v>
<v n="27">And then they will see the Son of Man coming in a cloud with power and great glory.</v>
<v n="28">Now when these things begin to take place, straighten up and raise your heads, because your redemption is drawing near."</v>
<v n="29">And he told them a parable: "Look at the fig tree, and all the trees.</v>
<v n="30">As soon as they come out in leaf, you see for yourselves and know that the summer is already near.</v>
<v n="31">So also, when you see these things taking place, you know that the kingdom of God is near.</v>
<v n="32">Truly, I say to you, this generation will not pass away until all has taken place.</v>
<v n="33">Heaven and earth will pass away, but my words will not pass away.</v>
<v n="34">"But watch yourselves lest your hearts be weighed down with dissipation and drunkenness and cares of this life, and that day come upon you suddenly like a trap.</v>
<v n="35">For it will come upon all who dwell on the face of the whole earth.</v>
<v n="36">But stay awake at all times, praying that you may have strength to escape all these things that are going to take place, and to stand before the Son of Man."</v>
<v n="37">And every day he was teaching in the temple, but at night he went out and lodged on the mount called Olivet.</v>
<v n="38">And early in the morning all the people came to him in the temple to hear him.</v>
</c>
<c n="22">
<v n="1">Now the Feast of Unleavened Bread drew near, which is called the Passover.</v>
<v n="2">And the chief priests and the scribes were seeking how to put him to death, for they feared the people.</v>
<v n="3">Then Satan entered into Judas called Iscariot, who was of the number of the twelve.</v>
<v n="4">He went away and conferred with the chief priests and officers how he might betray him to them.</v>
<v n="5">And they were glad, and agreed to give him money.</v>
<v n="6">So he consented and sought an opportunity to betray him to them in the absence of a crowd.</v>
<v n="7">Then came the day of Unleavened Bread, on which the Passover lamb had to be sacrificed.</v>
<v n="8">So Jesus sent Peter and John, saying, "Go and prepare the Passover for us, that we may eat it."</v>
<v n="9">They said to him, "Where will you have us prepare it?"</v>
<v n="10">He said to them, "Behold, when you have entered the city, a man carrying a jar of water will meet you. Follow him into the house that he enters</v>
<v n="11">and tell the master of the house, 'The Teacher says to you, Where is the guest room, where I may eat the Passover with my disciples?'</v>
<v n="12">And he will show you a large upper room furnished; prepare it there."</v>
<v n="13">And they went and found it just as he had told them, and they prepared the Passover.</v>
<v n="14">And when the hour came, he reclined at table, and the apostles with him.</v>
<v n="15">And he said to them, "I have earnestly desired to eat this Passover with you before I suffer.</v>
<v n="16">For I tell you I will not eat it until it is fulfilled in the kingdom of God."</v>
<v n="17">And he took a cup, and when he had given thanks he said, "Take this, and divide it among yourselves.</v>
<v n="18">For I tell you that from now on I will not drink of the fruit of the vine until the kingdom of God comes."</v>
<v n="19">And he took bread, and when he had given thanks, he broke it and gave it to them, saying, "This is my body, which is given for you. Do this in remembrance of me."</v>
<v n="20">And likewise the cup after they had eaten, saying, "This cup that is poured out for you is the new covenant in my blood.</v>
<v n="21">But behold, the hand of him who betrays me is with me on the table.</v>
<v n="22">For the Son of Man goes as it has been determined, but woe to that man by whom he is betrayed!"</v>
<v n="23">And they began to question one another, which of them it could be who was going to do this.</v>
<v n="24">A dispute also arose among them, as to which of them was to be regarded as the greatest.</v>
<v n="25">And he said to them, "The kings of the Gentiles exercise lordship over them, and those in authority over them are called benefactors.</v>
<v n="26">But not so with you. Rather, let the greatest among you become as the youngest, and the leader as one who serves.</v>
<v n="27">For who is the greater, one who reclines at table or one who serves? Is it not the one who reclines at table? But I am among you as the one who serves.</v>
<v n="28">"You are those who have stayed with me in my trials,</v>
<v n="29">and I assign to you, as my Father assigned to me, a kingdom,</v>
<v n="30">that you may eat and drink at my table in my kingdom and sit on thrones judging the twelve tribes of Israel.</v>
<v n="31">"Simon, Simon, behold, Satan demanded to have you, that he might sift you like wheat,</v>
<v n="32">but I have prayed for you that your faith may not fail. And when you have turned again, strengthen your brothers."</v>
<v n="33">Peter said to him, "Lord, I am ready to go with you both to prison and to death."</v>
<v n="34">Jesus said, "I tell you, Peter, the rooster will not crow this day, until you deny three times that you know me."</v>
<v n="35">And he said to them, "When I sent you out with no moneybag or knapsack or sandals, did you lack anything?" They said, "Nothing."</v>
<v n="36">He said to them, "But now let the one who has a moneybag take it, and likewise a knapsack. And let the one who has no sword sell his cloak and buy one.</v>
<v n="37">For I tell you that this Scripture must be fulfilled in me: 'And he was numbered with the transgressors.' For what is written about me has its fulfillment."</v>
<v n="38">And they said, "Look, Lord, here are two swords." And he said to them, "It is enough."</v>
<v n="39">And he came out and went, as was his custom, to the Mount of Olives, and the disciples followed him.</v>
<v n="40">And when he came to the place, he said to them, "Pray that you may not enter into temptation."</v>
<v n="41">And he withdrew from them about a stone's throw, and knelt down and prayed,</v>
<v n="42">saying, "Father, if you are willing, remove this cup from me. Nevertheless, not my will, but yours, be done."</v>
<v n="43">And there appeared to him an angel from heaven, strengthening him.</v>
<v n="44">And being in an agony he prayed more earnestly; and his sweat became like great drops of blood falling down to the ground.</v>
<v n="45">And when he rose from prayer, he came to the disciples and found them sleeping for sorrow,</v>
<v n="46">and he said to them, "Why are you sleeping? Rise and pray that you may not enter into temptation."</v>
<v n="47">While he was still speaking, there came a crowd, and the man called Judas, one of the twelve, was leading them. He drew near to Jesus to kiss him,</v>
<v n="48">but Jesus said to him, "Judas, would you betray the Son of Man with a kiss?"</v>
<v n="49">And when those who were around him saw what would follow, they said, "Lord, shall we strike with the sword?"</v>
<v n="50">And one of them struck the servant of the high priest and cut off his right ear.</v>
<v n="51">But Jesus said, "No more of this!" And he touched his ear and healed him.</v>
<v n="52">Then Jesus said to the chief priests and officers of the temple and elders, who had come out against him, "Have you come out as against a robber, with swords and clubs?</v>
<v n="53">When I was with you day after day in the temple, you did not lay hands on me. But this is your hour, and the power of darkness."</v>
<v n="54">Then they seized him and led him away, bringing him into the high priest's house, and Peter was following at a distance.</v>
<v n="55">And when they had kindled a fire in the middle of the courtyard and sat down together, Peter sat down among them.</v>
<v n="56">Then a servant girl, seeing him as he sat in the light and looking closely at him, said, "This man also was with him."</v>
<v n="57">But he denied it, saying, "Woman, I do not know him."</v>
<v n="58">And a little later someone else saw him and said, "You also are one of them." But Peter said, "Man, I am not."</v>
<v n="59">And after an interval of about an hour still another insisted, saying, "Certainly this man also was with him, for he too is a Galilean."</v>
<v n="60">But Peter said, "Man, I do not know what you are talking about." And immediately, while he was still speaking, the rooster crowed.</v>
<v n="61">And the Lord turned and looked at Peter. And Peter remembered the saying of the Lord, how he had said to him, "Before the rooster crows today, you will deny me three times."</v>
<v n="62">And he went out and wept bitterly.</v>
<v n="63">Now the men who were holding Jesus in custody were mocking him as they beat him.</v>
<v n="64">They also blindfolded him and kept asking him, "Prophesy! Who is it that struck you?"</v>
<v n="65">And they said many other things against him, blaspheming him.</v>
<v n="66">When day came, the assembly of the elders of the people gathered together, both chief priests and scribes. And they led him away to their council, and they said,</v>
<v n="67">"If you are the Christ, tell us." But he said to them, "If I tell you, you will not believe,</v>
<v n="68">and if I ask you, you will not answer.</v>
<v n="69">But from now on the Son of Man shall be seated at the right hand of the power of God."</v>
<v n="70">So they all said, "Are you the Son of God, then?" And he said to them, "You say that I am."</v>
<v n="71">Then they said, "What further testimony do we need? We have heard it ourselves from his own lips."</v>
</c>
<c n="23">
<v n="1">Then the whole company of them arose and brought him before Pilate.</v>
<v n="2">And they began to accuse him, saying, "We found this man misleading our nation and forbidding us to give tribute to Caesar, and saying that he himself is Christ, a king."</v>
<v n="3">And Pilate asked him, "Are you the King of the Jews?" And he answered him, "You have said so."</v>
<v n="4">Then Pilate said to the chief priests and the crowds, "I find no guilt in this man."</v>
<v n="5">But they were urgent, saying, "He stirs up the people, teaching throughout all Judea, from Galilee even to this place."</v>
<v n="6">When Pilate heard this, he asked whether the man was a Galilean.</v>
<v n="7">And when he learned that he belonged to Herod's jurisdiction, he sent him over to Herod, who was himself in Jerusalem at that time.</v>
<v n="8">When Herod saw Jesus, he was very glad, for he had long desired to see him, because he had heard about him, and he was hoping to see some sign done by him.</v>
<v n="9">So he questioned him at some length, but he made no answer.</v>
<v n="10">The chief priests and the scribes stood by, vehemently accusing him.</v>
<v n="11">And Herod with his soldiers treated him with contempt and mocked him. Then, arraying him in splendid clothing, he sent him back to Pilate.</v>
<v n="12">And Herod and Pilate became friends with each other that very day, for before this they had been at enmity with each other.</v>
<v n="13">Pilate then called together the chief priests and the rulers and the people,</v>
<v n="14">and said to them, "You brought me this man as one who was misleading the people. And after examining him before you, behold, I did not find this man guilty of any of your charges against him.</v>
<v n="15">Neither did Herod, for he sent him back to us. Look, nothing deserving death has been done by him.</v>
<v n="16">I will therefore punish and release him."</v>
<v n="17">See Footnote</v>
<v n="18">But they all cried out together, "Away with this man, and release to us Barabbas"--</v>
<v n="19">a man who had been thrown into prison for an insurrection started in the city and for murder.</v>
<v n="20">Pilate addressed them once more, desiring to release Jesus,</v>
<v n="21">but they kept shouting, "Crucify, crucify him!"</v>
<v n="22">A third time he said to them, "Why, what evil has he done? I have found in him no guilt deserving death. I will therefore punish and release him."</v>
<v n="23">But they were urgent, demanding with loud cries that he should be crucified. And their voices prevailed.</v>
<v n="24">So Pilate decided that their demand should be granted.</v>
<v n="25">He released the man who had been thrown into prison for insurrection and murder, for whom they asked, but he delivered Jesus over to their will.</v>
<v n="26">And as they led him away, they seized one Simon of Cyrene, who was coming in from the country, and laid on him the cross, to carry it behind Jesus.</v>
<v n="27">And there followed him a great multitude of the people and of women who were mourning and lamenting for him.</v>
<v n="28">But turning to them Jesus said, "Daughters of Jerusalem, do not weep for me, but weep for yourselves and for your children.</v>
<v n="29">For behold, the days are coming when they will say, 'Blessed are the barren and the wombs that never bore and the breasts that never nursed!'</v>
<v n="30">Then they will begin to say to the mountains, 'Fall on us,' and to the hills, 'Cover us.'</v>
<v n="31">For if they do these things when the wood is green, what will happen when it is dry?"</v>
<v n="32">Two others, who were criminals, were led away to be put to death with him.</v>
<v n="33">And when they came to the place that is called The Skull, there they crucified him, and the criminals, one on his right and one on his left.</v>
<v n="34">And Jesus said, "Father, forgive them, for they know not what they do." And they cast lots to divide his garments.</v>
<v n="35">And the people stood by, watching, but the rulers scoffed at him, saying, "He saved others; let him save himself, if he is the Christ of God, his Chosen One!"</v>
<v n="36">The soldiers also mocked him, coming up and offering him sour wine</v>
<v n="37">and saying, "If you are the King of the Jews, save yourself!"</v>
<v n="38">There was also an inscription over him, "This is the King of the Jews."</v>
<v n="39">One of the criminals who were hanged railed at him, saying, "Are you not the Christ? Save yourself and us!"</v>
<v n="40">But the other rebuked him, saying, "Do you not fear God, since you are under the same sentence of condemnation?</v>
<v n="41">And we indeed justly, for we are receiving the due reward of our deeds; but this man has done nothing wrong."</v>
<v n="42">And he said, "Jesus, remember me when you come into your kingdom."</v>
<v n="43">And he said to him, "Truly, I say to you, today you will be with me in Paradise."</v>
<v n="44">It was now about the sixth hour, and there was darkness over the whole land until the ninth hour,</v>
<v n="45">while the sun's light failed. And the curtain of the temple was torn in two.</v>
<v n="46">Then Jesus, calling out with a loud voice, said, "Father, into your hands I commit my spirit!" And having said this he breathed his last.</v>
<v n="47">Now when the centurion saw what had taken place, he praised God, saying, "Certainly this man was innocent!"</v>
<v n="48">And all the crowds that had assembled for this spectacle, when they saw what had taken place, returned home beating their breasts.</v>
<v n="49">And all his acquaintances and the women who had followed him from Galilee stood at a distance watching these things.</v>
<v n="50">Now there was a man named Joseph, from the Jewish town of Arimathea. He was a member of the council, a good and righteous man,</v>
<v n="51">who had not consented to their decision and action; and he was looking for the kingdom of God.</v>
<v n="52">This man went to Pilate and asked for the body of Jesus.</v>
<v n="53">Then he took it down and wrapped it in a linen shroud and laid him in a tomb cut in stone, where no one had ever yet been laid.</v>
<v n="54">It was the day of Preparation, and the Sabbath was beginning.</v>
<v n="55">The women who had come with him from Galilee followed and saw the tomb and how his body was laid.</v>
<v n="56">Then they returned and prepared spices and ointments.On the Sabbath they rested according to the commandment.</v>
</c>
<c n="24">
<v n="1">But on the first day of the week, at early dawn, they went to the tomb, taking the spices they had prepared.</v>
<v n="2">And they found the stone rolled away from the tomb,</v>
<v n="3">but when they went in they did not find the body of the Lord Jesus.</v>
<v n="4">While they were perplexed about this, behold, two men stood by them in dazzling apparel.</v>
<v n="5">And as they were frightened and bowed their faces to the ground, the men said to them, "Why do you seek the living among the dead?</v>
<v n="6">He is not here, but has risen. Remember how he told you, while he was still in Galilee,</v>
<v n="7">that the Son of Man must be delivered into the hands of sinful men and be crucified and on the third day rise."</v>
<v n="8">And they remembered his words,</v>
<v n="9">and returning from the tomb they told all these things to the eleven and to all the rest.</v>
<v n="10">Now it was Mary Magdalene and Joanna and Mary the mother of James and the other women with them who told these things to the apostles,</v>
<v n="11">but these words seemed to them an idle tale, and they did not believe them.</v>
<v n="12">But Peter rose and ran to the tomb; stooping and looking in, he saw the linen cloths by themselves; and he went home marveling at what had happened.</v>
<v n="13">That very day two of them were going to a village named Emmaus, about seven miles from Jerusalem,</v>
<v n="14">and they were talking with each other about all these things that had happened.</v>
<v n="15">While they were talking and discussing together, Jesus himself drew near and went with them.</v>
<v n="16">But their eyes were kept from recognizing him.</v>
<v n="17">And he said to them, "What is this conversation that you are holding with each other as you walk?" And they stood still, looking sad.</v>
<v n="18">Then one of them, named Cleopas, answered him, "Are you the only visitor to Jerusalem who does not know the things that have happened there in these days?"</v>
<v n="19">And he said to them, "What things?" And they said to him, "Concerning Jesus of Nazareth, a man who was a prophet mighty in deed and word before God and all the people,</v>
<v n="20">and how our chief priests and rulers delivered him up to be condemned to death, and crucified him.</v>
<v n="21">But we had hoped that he was the one to redeem Israel. Yes, and besides all this, it is now the third day since these things happened.</v>
<v n="22">Moreover, some women of our company amazed us. They were at the tomb early in the morning,</v>
<v n="23">and when they did not find his body, they came back saying that they had even seen a vision of angels, who said that he was alive.</v>
<v n="24">Some of those who were with us went to the tomb and found it just as the women had said, but him they did not see."</v>
<v n="25">And he said to them, "O foolish ones, and slow of heart to believe all that the prophets have spoken!</v>
<v n="26">Was it not necessary that the Christ should suffer these things and enter into his glory?"</v>
<v n="27">And beginning with Moses and all the Prophets, he interpreted to them in all the Scriptures the things concerning himself.</v>
<v n="28">So they drew near to the village to which they were going. He acted as if he were going farther,</v>
<v n="29">but they urged him strongly, saying, "Stay with us, for it is toward evening and the day is now far spent." So he went in to stay with them.</v>
<v n="30">When he was at table with them, he took the bread and blessed and broke it and gave it to them.</v>
<v n="31">And their eyes were opened, and they recognized him. And he vanished from their sight.</v>
<v n="32">They said to each other, "Did not our hearts burn within us while he talked to us on the road, while he opened to us the Scriptures?"</v>
<v n="33">And they rose that same hour and returned to Jerusalem. And they found the eleven and those who were with them gathered together,</v>
<v n="34">saying, "The Lord has risen indeed, and has appeared to Simon!"</v>
<v n="35">Then they told what had happened on the road, and how he was known to them in the breaking of the bread.</v>
<v n="36">As they were talking about these things, Jesus himself stood among them, and said to them, "Peace to you!"</v>
<v n="37">But they were startled and frightened and thought they saw a spirit.</v>
<v n="38">And he said to them, "Why are you troubled, and why do doubts arise in your hearts?</v>
<v n="39">See my hands and my feet, that it is I myself. Touch me, and see. For a spirit does not have flesh and bones as you see that I have."</v>
<v n="40">And when he had said this, he showed them his hands and his feet.</v>
<v n="41">And while they still disbelieved for joy and were marveling, he said to them, "Have you anything here to eat?"</v>
<v n="42">They gave him a piece of broiled fish,</v>
<v n="43">and he took it and ate before them.</v>
<v n="44">Then he said to them, "These are my words that I spoke to you while I was still with you, that everything written about me in the Law of Moses and the Prophets and the Psalms must be fulfilled."</v>
<v n="45">Then he opened their minds to understand the Scriptures,</v>
<v n="46">and said to them, "Thus it is written, that the Christ should suffer and on the third day rise from the dead,</v>
<v n="47">and that repentance and forgiveness of sins should be proclaimed in his name to all nations, beginning from Jerusalem.</v>
<v n="48">You are witnesses of these things.</v>
<v n="49">And behold, I am sending the promise of my Father upon you. But stay in the city until you are clothed with power from on high."</v>
<v n="50">Then he led them out as far as Bethany, and lifting up his hands he blessed them.</v>
<v n="51">While he blessed them, he parted from them and was carried up into heaven.</v>
<v n="52">And they worshiped him and returned to Jerusalem with great joy,</v>
<v n="53">and were continually in the temple blessing God.</v>
</c>
</b>
<b n="John">
<c n="1">
<v n="1">In the beginning was the Word, and the Word was with God, and the Word was God.</v>
<v n="2">He was in the beginning with God.</v>
<v n="3">All things were made through him, and without him was not any thing made that was made.</v>
<v n="4">In him was life, and the life was the light of men.</v>
<v n="5">The light shines in the darkness, and the darkness has not overcome it.</v>
<v n="6">There was a man sent from God, whose name was John.</v>
<v n="7">He came as a witness, to bear witness about the light, that all might believe through him.</v>
<v n="8">He was not the light, but came to bear witness about the light.</v>
<v n="9">The true light, which enlightens everyone, was coming into the world.</v>
<v n="10">He was in the world, and the world was made through him, yet the world did not know him.</v>
<v n="11">He came to his own, and his own people did not receive him.</v>
<v n="12">But to all who did receive him, who believed in his name, he gave the right to become children of God,</v>
<v n="13">who were born, not of blood nor of the will of the flesh nor of the will of man, but of God.</v>
<v n="14">And the Word became flesh and dwelt among us, and we have seen his glory, glory as of the only Son from the Father, full of grace and truth.</v>
<v n="15">(John bore witness about him, and cried out, "This was he of whom I said, 'He who comes after me ranks before me, because he was before me.'")</v>
<v n="16">And from his fullness we have all received, grace upon grace.</v>
<v n="17">For the law was given through Moses; grace and truth came through Jesus Christ.</v>
<v n="18">No one has ever seen God; the only God, who is at the Father's side, he has made him known.</v>
<v n="19">And this is the testimony of John, when the Jews sent priests and Levites from Jerusalem to ask him, "Who are you?"</v>
<v n="20">He confessed, and did not deny, but confessed, "I am not the Christ."</v>
<v n="21">And they asked him, "What then? Are you Elijah?" He said, "I am not.Are you the Prophet?" And he answered, "No."</v>
<v n="22">So they said to him, "Who are you? We need to give an answer to those who sent us. What do you say about yourself?"</v>
<v n="23">He said, "I am the voice of one crying out in the wilderness, 'Make straight the way of the Lord,' as the prophet Isaiah said."</v>
<v n="24">(Now they had been sent from the Pharisees.)</v>
<v n="25">They asked him, "Then why are you baptizing, if you are neither the Christ, nor Elijah, nor the Prophet?"</v>
<v n="26">John answered them, "I baptize with water, but among you stands one you do not know,</v>
<v n="27">even he who comes after me, the strap of whose sandal I am not worthy to untie."</v>
<v n="28">These things took place in Bethany across the Jordan, where John was baptizing.</v>
<v n="29">The next day he saw Jesus coming toward him, and said, "Behold, the Lamb of God, who takes away the sin of the world!</v>
<v n="30">This is he of whom I said, 'After me comes a man who ranks before me, because he was before me.'</v>
<v n="31">I myself did not know him, but for this purpose I came baptizing with water, that he might be revealed to Israel."</v>
<v n="32">And John bore witness: "I saw the Spirit descend from heaven like a dove, and it remained on him.</v>
<v n="33">I myself did not know him, but he who sent me to baptize with water said to me, 'He on whom you see the Spirit descend and remain, this is he who baptizes with the Holy Spirit.'</v>
<v n="34">And I have seen and have borne witness that this is the Son of God."</v>
<v n="35">The next day again John was standing with two of his disciples,</v>
<v n="36">and he looked at Jesus as he walked by and said, "Behold, the Lamb of God!"</v>
<v n="37">The two disciples heard him say this, and they followed Jesus.</v>
<v n="38">Jesus turned and saw them following and said to them, "What are you seeking?" And they said to him, "Rabbi" (which means Teacher), "where are you staying?"</v>
<v n="39">He said to them, "Come and you will see." So they came and saw where he was staying, and they stayed with him that day, for it was about the tenth hour.</v>
<v n="40">One of the two who heard John speak and followed Jesus was Andrew, Simon Peter's brother.</v>
<v n="41">He first found his own brother Simon and said to him, "We have found the Messiah" (which means Christ).</v>
<v n="42">He brought him to Jesus. Jesus looked at him and said, "So you are Simon the son of John? You shall be called Cephas" (which means Peter ).</v>
<v n="43">The next day Jesus decided to go to Galilee. He found Philip and said to him, "Follow me."</v>
<v n="44">Now Philip was from Bethsaida, the city of Andrew and Peter.</v>
<v n="45">Philip found Nathanael and said to him, "We have found him of whom Moses in the Law and also the prophets wrote, Jesus of Nazareth, the son of Joseph."</v>
<v n="46">Nathanael said to him, "Can anything good come out of Nazareth?" Philip said to him, "Come and see."</v>
<v n="47">Jesus saw Nathanael coming toward him and said of him, "Behold, an Israelite indeed, in whom there is no deceit!"</v>
<v n="48">Nathanael said to him, "How do you know me?" Jesus answered him, "Before Philip called you, when you were under the fig tree, I saw you."</v>
<v n="49">Nathanael answered him, "Rabbi, you are the Son of God! You are the King of Israel!"</v>
<v n="50">Jesus answered him, "Because I said to you, 'I saw you under the fig tree,' do you believe? You will see greater things than these."</v>
<v n="51">And he said to him, "Truly, truly, I say to you, you will see heaven opened, and the angels of God ascending and descending on the Son of Man."</v>
</c>
<c n="2">
<v n="1">On the third day there was a wedding at Cana in Galilee, and the mother of Jesus was there.</v>
<v n="2">Jesus also was invited to the wedding with his disciples.</v>
<v n="3">When the wine ran out, the mother of Jesus said to him, "They have no wine."</v>
<v n="4">And Jesus said to her, "Woman, what does this have to do with me? My hour has not yet come."</v>
<v n="5">His mother said to the servants, "Do whatever he tells you."</v>
<v n="6">Now there were six stone water jars there for the Jewish rites of purification, each holding twenty or thirty gallons.</v>
<v n="7">Jesus said to the servants, "Fill the jars with water." And they filled them up to the brim.</v>
<v n="8">And he said to them, "Now draw some out and take it to the master of the feast." So they took it.</v>
<v n="9">When the master of the feast tasted the water now become wine, and did not know where it came from (though the servants who had drawn the water knew), the master of the feast called the bridegroom</v>
<v n="10">and said to him, "Everyone serves the good wine first, and when people have drunk freely, then the poor wine. But you have kept the good wine until now."</v>
<v n="11">This, the first of his signs, Jesus did at Cana in Galilee, and manifested his glory. And his disciples believed in him.</v>
<v n="12">After this he went down to Capernaum, with his mother and his brothers and his disciples, and they stayed there for a few days.</v>
<v n="13">The Passover of the Jews was at hand, and Jesus went up to Jerusalem.</v>
<v n="14">In the temple he found those who were selling oxen and sheep and pigeons, and the money-changers sitting there.</v>
<v n="15">And making a whip of cords, he drove them all out of the temple, with the sheep and oxen. And he poured out the coins of the money-changers and overturned their tables.</v>
<v n="16">And he told those who sold the pigeons, "Take these things away; do not make my Father's house a house of trade."</v>
<v n="17">His disciples remembered that it was written, "Zeal for your house will consume me."</v>
<v n="18">So the Jews said to him, "What sign do you show us for doing these things?"</v>
<v n="19">Jesus answered them, "Destroy this temple, and in three days I will raise it up."</v>
<v n="20">The Jews then said, "It has taken forty-six years to build this temple, and will you raise it up in three days?"</v>
<v n="21">But he was speaking about the temple of his body.</v>
<v n="22">When therefore he was raised from the dead, his disciples remembered that he had said this, and they believed the Scripture and the word that Jesus had spoken.</v>
<v n="23">Now when he was in Jerusalem at the Passover Feast, many believed in his name when they saw the signs that he was doing.</v>
<v n="24">But Jesus on his part did not entrust himself to them, because he knew all people</v>
<v n="25">and needed no one to bear witness about man, for he himself knew what was in man.</v>
</c>
<c n="3">
<v n="1">Now there was a man of the Pharisees named Nicodemus, a ruler of the Jews.</v>
<v n="2">This man came to Jesus by night and said to him, "Rabbi, we know that you are a teacher come from God, for no one can do these signs that you do unless God is with him."</v>
<v n="3">Jesus answered him, "Truly, truly, I say to you, unless one is born again he cannot see the kingdom of God."</v>
<v n="4">Nicodemus said to him, "How can a man be born when he is old? Can he enter a second time into his mother's womb and be born?"</v>
<v n="5">Jesus answered, "Truly, truly, I say to you, unless one is born of water and the Spirit, he cannot enter the kingdom of God.</v>
<v n="6">That which is born of the flesh is flesh, and that which is born of the Spirit is spirit.</v>
<v n="7">Do not marvel that I said to you, 'You must be born again.'</v>
<v n="8">The wind blows where it wishes, and you hear its sound, but you do not know where it comes from or where it goes. So it is with everyone who is born of the Spirit."</v>
<v n="9">Nicodemus said to him, "How can these things be?"</v>
<v n="10">Jesus answered him, "Are you the teacher of Israel and yet you do not understand these things?</v>
<v n="11">Truly, truly, I say to you, we speak of what we know, and bear witness to what we have seen, but you do not receive our testimony.</v>
<v n="12">If I have told you earthly things and you do not believe, how can you believe if I tell you heavenly things?</v>
<v n="13">No one has ascended into heaven except he who descended from heaven, the Son of Man.</v>
<v n="14">And as Moses lifted up the serpent in the wilderness, so must the Son of Man be lifted up,</v>
<v n="15">that whoever believes in him may have eternal life.</v>
<v n="16">"For God so loved the world, that he gave his only Son, that whoever believes in him should not perish but have eternal life.</v>
<v n="17">For God did not send his Son into the world to condemn the world, but in order that the world might be saved through him.</v>
<v n="18">Whoever believes in him is not condemned, but whoever does not believe is condemned already, because he has not believed in the name of the only Son of God.</v>
<v n="19">And this is the judgment: the light has come into the world, and people loved the darkness rather than the light because their deeds were evil.</v>
<v n="20">For everyone who does wicked things hates the light and does not come to the light, lest his deeds should be exposed.</v>
<v n="21">But whoever does what is true comes to the light, so that it may be clearly seen that his deeds have been carried out in God."</v>
<v n="22">After this Jesus and his disciples went into the Judean countryside, and he remained there with them and was baptizing.</v>
<v n="23">John also was baptizing at Aenon near Salim, because water was plentiful there, and people were coming and being baptized</v>
<v n="24">(for John had not yet been put in prison).</v>
<v n="25">Now a discussion arose between some of John's disciples and a Jew over purification.</v>
<v n="26">And they came to John and said to him, "Rabbi, he who was with you across the Jordan, to whom you bore witness--look, he is baptizing, and all are going to him."</v>
<v n="27">John answered, "A person cannot receive even one thing unless it is given him from heaven.</v>
<v n="28">You yourselves bear me witness, that I said, 'I am not the Christ, but I have been sent before him.'</v>
<v n="29">The one who has the bride is the bridegroom. The friend of the bridegroom, who stands and hears him, rejoices greatly at the bridegroom's voice. Therefore this joy of mine is now complete.</v>
<v n="30">He must increase, but I must decrease."</v>
<v n="31">He who comes from above is above all. He who is of the earth belongs to the earth and speaks in an earthly way. He who comes from heaven is above all.</v>
<v n="32">He bears witness to what he has seen and heard, yet no one receives his testimony.</v>
<v n="33">Whoever receives his testimony sets his seal to this, that God is true.</v>
<v n="34">For he whom God has sent utters the words of God, for he gives the Spirit without measure.</v>
<v n="35">The Father loves the Son and has given all things into his hand.</v>
<v n="36">Whoever believes in the Son has eternal life; whoever does not obey the Son shall not see life, but the wrath of God remains on him.</v>
</c>
<c n="4">
<v n="1">Now when Jesus learned that the Pharisees had heard that Jesus was making and baptizing more disciples than John</v>
<v n="2">(although Jesus himself did not baptize, but only his disciples),</v>
<v n="3">he left Judea and departed again for Galilee.</v>
<v n="4">And he had to pass through Samaria.</v>
<v n="5">So he came to a town of Samaria called Sychar, near the field that Jacob had given to his son Joseph.</v>
<v n="6">Jacob's well was there; so Jesus, wearied as he was from his journey, was sitting beside the well. It was about the sixth hour.</v>
<v n="7">There came a woman of Samaria to draw water. Jesus said to her, "Give me a drink."</v>
<v n="8">(For his disciples had gone away into the city to buy food.)</v>
<v n="9">The Samaritan woman said to him, "How is it that you, a Jew, ask for a drink from me, a woman of Samaria?" (For Jews have no dealings with Samaritans.)</v>
<v n="10">Jesus answered her, "If you knew the gift of God, and who it is that is saying to you, 'Give me a drink,' you would have asked him, and he would have given you living water."</v>
<v n="11">The woman said to him, "Sir, you have nothing to draw water with, and the well is deep. Where do you get that living water?</v>
<v n="12">Are you greater than our father Jacob? He gave us the well and drank from it himself, as did his sons and his livestock."</v>
<v n="13">Jesus said to her, "Everyone who drinks of this water will be thirsty again,</v>
<v n="14">but whoever drinks of the water that I will give him will never be thirsty forever. The water that I will give him will become in him a spring of water welling up to eternal life."</v>
<v n="15">The woman said to him, "Sir, give me this water, so that I will not be thirsty or have to come here to draw water."</v>
<v n="16">Jesus said to her, "Go, call your husband, and come here."</v>
<v n="17">The woman answered him, "I have no husband." Jesus said to her, "You are right in saying, 'I have no husband';</v>
<v n="18">for you have had five husbands, and the one you now have is not your husband. What you have said is true."</v>
<v n="19">The woman said to him, "Sir, I perceive that you are a prophet.</v>
<v n="20">Our fathers worshiped on this mountain, but you say that in Jerusalem is the place where people ought to worship."</v>
<v n="21">Jesus said to her, "Woman, believe me, the hour is coming when neither on this mountain nor in Jerusalem will you worship the Father.</v>
<v n="22">You worship what you do not know; we worship what we know, for salvation is from the Jews.</v>
<v n="23">But the hour is coming, and is now here, when the true worshipers will worship the Father in spirit and truth, for the Father is seeking such people to worship him.</v>
<v n="24">God is spirit, and those who worship him must worship in spirit and truth."</v>
<v n="25">The woman said to him, "I know that Messiah is coming (he who is called Christ). When he comes, he will tell us all things."</v>
<v n="26">Jesus said to her, "I who speak to you am he."</v>
<v n="27">Just then his disciples came back. They marveled that he was talking with a woman, but no one said, "What do you seek?" or, "Why are you talking with her?"</v>
<v n="28">So the woman left her water jar and went away into town and said to the people,</v>
<v n="29">"Come, see a man who told me all that I ever did. Can this be the Christ?"</v>
<v n="30">They went out of the town and were coming to him.</v>
<v n="31">Meanwhile the disciples were urging him, saying, "Rabbi, eat."</v>
<v n="32">But he said to them, "I have food to eat that you do not know about."</v>
<v n="33">So the disciples said to one another, "Has anyone brought him something to eat?"</v>
<v n="34">Jesus said to them, "My food is to do the will of him who sent me and to accomplish his work.</v>
<v n="35">Do you not say, 'There are yet four months, then comes the harvest'? Look, I tell you, lift up your eyes, and see that the fields are white for harvest.</v>
<v n="36">Already the one who reaps is receiving wages and gathering fruit for eternal life, so that sower and reaper may rejoice together.</v>
<v n="37">For here the saying holds true, 'One sows and another reaps.'</v>
<v n="38">I sent you to reap that for which you did not labor. Others have labored, and you have entered into their labor."</v>
<v n="39">Many Samaritans from that town believed in him because of the woman's testimony, "He told me all that I ever did."</v>
<v n="40">So when the Samaritans came to him, they asked him to stay with them, and he stayed there two days.</v>
<v n="41">And many more believed because of his word.</v>
<v n="42">They said to the woman, "It is no longer because of what you said that we believe, for we have heard for ourselves, and we know that this is indeed the Savior of the world."</v>
<v n="43">After the two days he departed for Galilee.</v>
<v n="44">(For Jesus himself had testified that a prophet has no honor in his own hometown.)</v>
<v n="45">So when he came to Galilee, the Galileans welcomed him, having seen all that he had done in Jerusalem at the feast. For they too had gone to the feast.</v>
<v n="46">So he came again to Cana in Galilee, where he had made the water wine. And at Capernaum there was an official whose son was ill.</v>
<v n="47">When this man heard that Jesus had come from Judea to Galilee, he went to him and asked him to come down and heal his son, for he was at the point of death.</v>
<v n="48">So Jesus said to him, "Unless you see signs and wonders you will not believe."</v>
<v n="49">The official said to him, "Sir, come down before my child dies."</v>
<v n="50">Jesus said to him, "Go; your son will live." The man believed the word that Jesus spoke to him and went on his way.</v>
<v n="51">As he was going down, his servants met him and told him that his son was recovering.</v>
<v n="52">So he asked them the hour when he began to get better, and they said to him, "Yesterday at the seventh hour the fever left him."</v>
<v n="53">The father knew that was the hour when Jesus had said to him, "Your son will live." And he himself believed, and all his household.</v>
<v n="54">This was now the second sign that Jesus did when he had come from Judea to Galilee.</v>
</c>
<c n="5">
<v n="1">After this there was a feast of the Jews, and Jesus went up to Jerusalem.</v>
<v n="2">Now there is in Jerusalem by the Sheep Gate a pool, in Aramaic called Bethesda, which has five roofed colonnades.</v>
<v n="3">In these lay a multitude of invalids--blind, lame, and paralyzed.</v>
<v n="4">See Footnote</v>
<v n="5">One man was there who had been an invalid for thirty-eight years.</v>
<v n="6">When Jesus saw him lying there and knew that he had already been there a long time, he said to him, "Do you want to be healed?"</v>
<v n="7">The sick man answered him, "Sir, I have no one to put me into the pool when the water is stirred up, and while I am going another steps down before me."</v>
<v n="8">Jesus said to him, "Get up, take up your bed, and walk."</v>
<v n="9">And at once the man was healed, and he took up his bed and walked.Now that day was the Sabbath.</v>
<v n="10">So the Jews said to the man who had been healed, "It is the Sabbath, and it is not lawful for you to take up your bed."</v>
<v n="11">But he answered them, "The man who healed me, that man said to me, 'Take up your bed, and walk.'"</v>
<v n="12">They asked him, "Who is the man who said to you, 'Take up your bed and walk'?"</v>
<v n="13">Now the man who had been healed did not know who it was, for Jesus had withdrawn, as there was a crowd in the place.</v>
<v n="14">Afterward Jesus found him in the temple and said to him, "See, you are well! Sin no more, that nothing worse may happen to you."</v>
<v n="15">The man went away and told the Jews that it was Jesus who had healed him.</v>
<v n="16">And this was why the Jews were persecuting Jesus, because he was doing these things on the Sabbath.</v>
<v n="17">But Jesus answered them, "My Father is working until now, and I am working."</v>
<v n="18">This was why the Jews were seeking all the more to kill him, because not only was he breaking the Sabbath, but he was even calling God his own Father, making himself equal with God.</v>
<v n="19">So Jesus said to them, "Truly, truly, I say to you, the Son can do nothing of his own accord, but only what he sees the Father doing. For whatever the Father does, that the Son does likewise.</v>
<v n="20">For the Father loves the Son and shows him all that he himself is doing. And greater works than these will he show him, so that you may marvel.</v>
<v n="21">For as the Father raises the dead and gives them life, so also the Son gives life to whom he will.</v>
<v n="22">The Father judges no one, but has given all judgment to the Son,</v>
<v n="23">that all may honor the Son, just as they honor the Father. Whoever does not honor the Son does not honor the Father who sent him.</v>
<v n="24">Truly, truly, I say to you, whoever hears my word and believes him who sent me has eternal life. He does not come into judgment, but has passed from death to life.</v>
<v n="25">"Truly, truly, I say to you, an hour is coming, and is now here, when the dead will hear the voice of the Son of God, and those who hear will live.</v>
<v n="26">For as the Father has life in himself, so he has granted the Son also to have life in himself.</v>
<v n="27">And he has given him authority to execute judgment, because he is the Son of Man.</v>
<v n="28">Do not marvel at this, for an hour is coming when all who are in the tombs will hear his voice</v>
<v n="29">and come out, those who have done good to the resurrection of life, and those who have done evil to the resurrection of judgment.</v>
<v n="30">"I can do nothing on my own. As I hear, I judge, and my judgment is just, because I seek not my own will but the will of him who sent me.</v>
<v n="31">If I alone bear witness about myself, my testimony is not deemed true.</v>
<v n="32">There is another who bears witness about me, and I know that the testimony that he bears about me is true.</v>
<v n="33">You sent to John, and he has borne witness to the truth.</v>
<v n="34">Not that the testimony that I receive is from man, but I say these things so that you may be saved.</v>
<v n="35">He was a burning and shining lamp, and you were willing to rejoice for a while in his light.</v>
<v n="36">But the testimony that I have is greater than that of John. For the works that the Father has given me to accomplish, the very works that I am doing, bear witness about me that the Father has sent me.</v>
<v n="37">And the Father who sent me has himself borne witness about me. His voice you have never heard, his form you have never seen,</v>
<v n="38">and you do not have his word abiding in you, for you do not believe the one whom he has sent.</v>
<v n="39">You search the Scriptures because you think that in them you have eternal life; and it is they that bear witness about me,</v>
<v n="40">yet you refuse to come to me that you may have life.</v>
<v n="41">I do not receive glory from people.</v>
<v n="42">But I know that you do not have the love of God within you.</v>
<v n="43">I have come in my Father's name, and you do not receive me. If another comes in his own name, you will receive him.</v>
<v n="44">How can you believe, when you receive glory from one another and do not seek the glory that comes from the only God?</v>
<v n="45">Do not think that I will accuse you to the Father. There is one who accuses you: Moses, on whom you have set your hope.</v>
<v n="46">If you believed Moses, you would believe me; for he wrote of me.</v>
<v n="47">But if you do not believe his writings, how will you believe my words?"</v>
</c>
<c n="6">
<v n="1">After this Jesus went away to the other side of the Sea of Galilee, which is the Sea of Tiberias.</v>
<v n="2">And a large crowd was following him, because they saw the signs that he was doing on the sick.</v>
<v n="3">Jesus went up on the mountain, and there he sat down with his disciples.</v>
<v n="4">Now the Passover, the feast of the Jews, was at hand.</v>
<v n="5">Lifting up his eyes, then, and seeing that a large crowd was coming toward him, Jesus said to Philip, "Where are we to buy bread, so that these people may eat?"</v>
<v n="6">He said this to test him, for he himself knew what he would do.</v>
<v n="7">Philip answered him, "Two hundred denarii would not buy enough bread for each of them to get a little."</v>
<v n="8">One of his disciples, Andrew, Simon Peter's brother, said to him,</v>
<v n="9">"There is a boy here who has five barley loaves and two fish, but what are they for so many?"</v>
<v n="10">Jesus said, "Have the people sit down." Now there was much grass in the place. So the men sat down, about five thousand in number.</v>
<v n="11">Jesus then took the loaves, and when he had given thanks, he distributed them to those who were seated. So also the fish, as much as they wanted.</v>
<v n="12">And when they had eaten their fill, he told his disciples, "Gather up the leftover fragments, that nothing may be lost."</v>
<v n="13">So they gathered them up and filled twelve baskets with fragments from the five barley loaves, left by those who had eaten.</v>
<v n="14">When the people saw the sign that he had done, they said, "This is indeed the Prophet who is to come into the world!"</v>
<v n="15">Perceiving then that they were about to come and take him by force to make him king, Jesus withdrew again to the mountain by himself.</v>
<v n="16">When evening came, his disciples went down to the sea,</v>
<v n="17">got into a boat, and started across the sea to Capernaum. It was now dark, and Jesus had not yet come to them.</v>
<v n="18">The sea became rough because a strong wind was blowing.</v>
<v n="19">When they had rowed about three or four miles, they saw Jesus walking on the sea and coming near the boat, and they were frightened.</v>
<v n="20">But he said to them, "It is I; do not be afraid."</v>
<v n="21">Then they were glad to take him into the boat, and immediately the boat was at the land to which they were going.</v>
<v n="22">On the next day the crowd that remained on the other side of the sea saw that there had been only one boat there, and that Jesus had not entered the boat with his disciples, but that his disciples had gone away alone.</v>
<v n="23">Other boats from Tiberias came near the place where they had eaten the bread after the Lord had given thanks.</v>
<v n="24">So when the crowd saw that Jesus was not there, nor his disciples, they themselves got into the boats and went to Capernaum, seeking Jesus.</v>
<v n="25">When they found him on the other side of the sea, they said to him, "Rabbi, when did you come here?"</v>
<v n="26">Jesus answered them, "Truly, truly, I say to you, you are seeking me, not because you saw signs, but because you ate your fill of the loaves.</v>
<v n="27">Do not labor for the food that perishes, but for the food that endures to eternal life, which the Son of Man will give to you. For on him God the Father has set his seal."</v>
<v n="28">Then they said to him, "What must we do, to be doing the works of God?"</v>
<v n="29">Jesus answered them, "This is the work of God, that you believe in him whom he has sent."</v>
<v n="30">So they said to him, "Then what sign do you do, that we may see and believe you? What work do you perform?</v>
<v n="31">Our fathers ate the manna in the wilderness; as it is written, 'He gave them bread from heaven to eat.'"</v>
<v n="32">Jesus then said to them, "Truly, truly, I say to you, it was not Moses who gave you the bread from heaven, but my Father gives you the true bread from heaven.</v>
<v n="33">For the bread of God is he who comes down from heaven and gives life to the world."</v>
<v n="34">They said to him, "Sir, give us this bread always."</v>
<v n="35">Jesus said to them, "I am the bread of life; whoever comes to me shall not hunger, and whoever believes in me shall never thirst.</v>
<v n="36">But I said to you that you have seen me and yet do not believe.</v>
<v n="37">All that the Father gives me will come to me, and whoever comes to me I will never cast out.</v>
<v n="38">For I have come down from heaven, not to do my own will but the will of him who sent me.</v>
<v n="39">And this is the will of him who sent me, that I should lose nothing of all that he has given me, but raise it up on the last day.</v>
<v n="40">For this is the will of my Father, that everyone who looks on the Son and believes in him should have eternal life, and I will raise him up on the last day."</v>
<v n="41">So the Jews grumbled about him, because he said, "I am the bread that came down from heaven."</v>
<v n="42">They said, "Is not this Jesus, the son of Joseph, whose father and mother we know? How does he now say, 'I have come down from heaven'?"</v>
<v n="43">Jesus answered them, "Do not grumble among yourselves.</v>
<v n="44">No one can come to me unless the Father who sent me draws him. And I will raise him up on the last day.</v>
<v n="45">It is written in the Prophets, 'And they will all be taught by God.' Everyone who has heard and learned from the Father comes to me--</v>
<v n="46">not that anyone has seen the Father except he who is from God; he has seen the Father.</v>
<v n="47">Truly, truly, I say to you, whoever believes has eternal life.</v>
<v n="48">I am the bread of life.</v>
<v n="49">Your fathers ate the manna in the wilderness, and they died.</v>
<v n="50">This is the bread that comes down from heaven, so that one may eat of it and not die.</v>
<v n="51">I am the living bread that came down from heaven. If anyone eats of this bread, he will live forever. And the bread that I will give for the life of the world is my flesh."</v>
<v n="52">The Jews then disputed among themselves, saying, "How can this man give us his flesh to eat?"</v>
<v n="53">So Jesus said to them, "Truly, truly, I say to you, unless you eat the flesh of the Son of Man and drink his blood, you have no life in you.</v>
<v n="54">Whoever feeds on my flesh and drinks my blood has eternal life, and I will raise him up on the last day.</v>
<v n="55">For my flesh is true food, and my blood is true drink.</v>
<v n="56">Whoever feeds on my flesh and drinks my blood abides in me, and I in him.</v>
<v n="57">As the living Father sent me, and I live because of the Father, so whoever feeds on me, he also will live because of me.</v>
<v n="58">This is the bread that came down from heaven, not as the fathers ate and died. Whoever feeds on this bread will live forever."</v>
<v n="59">Jesus said these things in the synagogue, as he taught at Capernaum.</v>
<v n="60">When many of his disciples heard it, they said, "This is a hard saying; who can listen to it?"</v>
<v n="61">But Jesus, knowing in himself that his disciples were grumbling about this, said to them, "Do you take offense at this?</v>
<v n="62">Then what if you were to see the Son of Man ascending to where he was before?</v>
<v n="63">It is the Spirit who gives life; the flesh is of no avail. The words that I have spoken to you are spirit and life.</v>
<v n="64">But there are some of you who do not believe." (For Jesus knew from the beginning who those were who did not believe, and who it was who would betray him.)</v>
<v n="65">And he said, "This is why I told you that no one can come to me unless it is granted him by the Father."</v>
<v n="66">After this many of his disciples turned back and no longer walked with him.</v>
<v n="67">So Jesus said to the Twelve, "Do you want to go away as well?"</v>
<v n="68">Simon Peter answered him, "Lord, to whom shall we go? You have the words of eternal life,</v>
<v n="69">and we have believed, and have come to know, that you are the Holy One of God."</v>
<v n="70">Jesus answered them, "Did I not choose you, the Twelve? And yet one of you is a devil."</v>
<v n="71">He spoke of Judas the son of Simon Iscariot, for he, one of the Twelve, was going to betray him.</v>
</c>
<c n="7">
<v n="1">After this Jesus went about in Galilee. He would not go about in Judea, because the Jews were seeking to kill him.</v>
<v n="2">Now the Jews' Feast of Booths was at hand.</v>
<v n="3">So his brothers said to him, "Leave here and go to Judea, that your disciples also may see the works you are doing.</v>
<v n="4">For no one works in secret if he seeks to be known openly. If you do these things, show yourself to the world."</v>
<v n="5">For not even his brothers believed in him.</v>
<v n="6">Jesus said to them, "My time has not yet come, but your time is always here.</v>
<v n="7">The world cannot hate you, but it hates me because I testify about it that its works are evil.</v>
<v n="8">You go up to the feast. I am not going up to this feast, for my time has not yet fully come."</v>
<v n="9">After saying this, he remained in Galilee.</v>
<v n="10">But after his brothers had gone up to the feast, then he also went up, not publicly but in private.</v>
<v n="11">The Jews were looking for him at the feast, and saying, "Where is he?"</v>
<v n="12">And there was much muttering about him among the people. While some said, "He is a good man," others said, "No, he is leading the people astray."</v>
<v n="13">Yet for fear of the Jews no one spoke openly of him.</v>
<v n="14">About the middle of the feast Jesus went up into the temple and began teaching.</v>
<v n="15">The Jews therefore marveled, saying, "How is it that this man has learning, when he has never studied?"</v>
<v n="16">So Jesus answered them, "My teaching is not mine, but his who sent me.</v>
<v n="17">If anyone's will is to do God's will, he will know whether the teaching is from God or whether I am speaking on my own authority.</v>
<v n="18">The one who speaks on his own authority seeks his own glory, but the one who seeks the glory of him who sent him is true, and in him there is no falsehood.</v>
<v n="19">Has not Moses given you the law? Yet none of you keeps the law. Why do you seek to kill me?"</v>
<v n="20">The crowd answered, "You have a demon! Who is seeking to kill you?"</v>
<v n="21">Jesus answered them, "I did one deed, and you all marvel at it.</v>
<v n="22">Moses gave you circumcision (not that it is from Moses, but from the fathers), and you circumcise a man on the Sabbath.</v>
<v n="23">If on the Sabbath a man receives circumcision, so that the law of Moses may not be broken, are you angry with me because on the Sabbath I made a man's whole body well?</v>
<v n="24">Do not judge by appearances, but judge with right judgment."</v>
<v n="25">Some of the people of Jerusalem therefore said, "Is not this the man whom they seek to kill?</v>
<v n="26">And here he is, speaking openly, and they say nothing to him! Can it be that the authorities really know that this is the Christ?</v>
<v n="27">But we know where this man comes from, and when the Christ appears, no one will know where he comes from."</v>
<v n="28">So Jesus proclaimed, as he taught in the temple, "You know me, and you know where I come from? But I have not come of my own accord. He who sent me is true, and him you do not know.</v>
<v n="29">I know him, for I come from him, and he sent me."</v>
<v n="30">So they were seeking to arrest him, but no one laid a hand on him, because his hour had not yet come.</v>
<v n="31">Yet many of the people believed in him. They said, "When the Christ appears, will he do more signs than this man has done?"</v>
<v n="32">The Pharisees heard the crowd muttering these things about him, and the chief priests and Pharisees sent officers to arrest him.</v>
<v n="33">Jesus then said, "I will be with you a little longer, and then I am going to him who sent me.</v>
<v n="34">You will seek me and you will not find me. Where I am you cannot come."</v>
<v n="35">The Jews said to one another, "Where does this man intend to go that we will not find him? Does he intend to go to the Dispersion among the Greeks and teach the Greeks?</v>
<v n="36">What does he mean by saying, 'You will seek me and you will not find me,' and, 'Where I am you cannot come'?"</v>
<v n="37">On the last day of the feast, the great day, Jesus stood up and cried out, "If anyone thirsts, let him come to me and drink.</v>
<v n="38">Whoever believes in me, as the Scripture has said, 'Out of his heart will flow rivers of living water.'"</v>
<v n="39">Now this he said about the Spirit, whom those who believed in him were to receive, for as yet the Spirit had not been given, because Jesus was not yet glorified.</v>
<v n="40">When they heard these words, some of the people said, "This really is the Prophet."</v>
<v n="41">Others said, "This is the Christ." But some said, "Is the Christ to come from Galilee?</v>
<v n="42">Has not the Scripture said that the Christ comes from the offspring of David, and comes from Bethlehem, the village where David was?"</v>
<v n="43">So there was a division among the people over him.</v>
<v n="44">Some of them wanted to arrest him, but no one laid hands on him.</v>
<v n="45">The officers then came to the chief priests and Pharisees, who said to them, "Why did you not bring him?"</v>
<v n="46">The officers answered, "No one ever spoke like this man!"</v>
<v n="47">The Pharisees answered them, "Have you also been deceived?</v>
<v n="48">Have any of the authorities or the Pharisees believed in him?</v>
<v n="49">But this crowd that does not know the law is accursed."</v>
<v n="50">Nicodemus, who had gone to him before, and who was one of them, said to them,</v>
<v n="51">"Does our law judge a man without first giving him a hearing and learning what he does?"</v>
<v n="52">They replied, "Are you from Galilee too? Search and see that no prophet arises from Galilee." [The earliest manuscripts do not include John 7:53-8:11]</v>
<v n="53">[[They went each to his own house,</v>
</c>
<c n="8">
<v n="1">but Jesus went to the Mount of Olives.</v>
<v n="2">Early in the morning he came again to the temple. All the people came to him, and he sat down and taught them.</v>
<v n="3">The scribes and the Pharisees brought a woman who had been caught in adultery, and placing her in the midst</v>
<v n="4">they said to him, "Teacher, this woman has been caught in the act of adultery.</v>
<v n="5">Now in the Law Moses commanded us to stone such women. So what do you say?"</v>
<v n="6">This they said to test him, that they might have some charge to bring against him. Jesus bent down and wrote with his finger on the ground.</v>
<v n="7">And as they continued to ask him, he stood up and said to them, "Let him who is without sin among you be the first to throw a stone at her."</v>
<v n="8">And once more he bent down and wrote on the ground.</v>
<v n="9">But when they heard it, they went away one by one, beginning with the older ones, and Jesus was left alone with the woman standing before him.</v>
<v n="10">Jesus stood up and said to her, "Woman, where are they? Has no one condemned you?"</v>
<v n="11">She said, "No one, Lord." And Jesus said, "Neither do I condemn you; go, and from now on sin no more."]]</v>
<v n="12">Again Jesus spoke to them, saying, "I am the light of the world. Whoever follows me will not walk in darkness, but will have the light of life."</v>
